# Zentinel — Deep Adversarial Review

_Generated by a phased multi-agent review (ground-truth via zigars MCP → 13-dimension loop-until-dry discovery → dedup → adversarial verification → completeness critic → synthesis). A finding is CONFIRMED only when ≥2 of 3 skeptic lenses (correctness, Zig-semantics/safety, reproduction) upheld it against the real code and zigars tool output; Critical/High/Medium used three independent skeptic agents, Low a single consolidated 3-lens skeptic. Toolchain: Zig 0.16.0 / ZLS 0.16.0._

**Build compiles:** true  |  **Confirmed:** 67  |  **Suspected:** 17  |  **Refuted & dropped:** 9

## Executive Overview

Zentinel compiles cleanly and is heavily governed, but the audit surfaces a tier of behavioral defects that strike the product's three core jobs — mutation generation, apply/revert, and kill-detection — not just polish. The single most serious risk is kill-count integrity: the compile-vs-test-failure discriminator in runner.zig (the literal "passed;" marker at line 109 plus isCompileFailure at 124/161) is unreliable under the standard `zig build test` command, so genuinely killed mutants can be silently rebucketed as compile_error and vice-versa, corrupting the headline "{killed}/{survived}" score (H4). Two unrecoverable panics deny or abort the tool on perfectly legal input: integer_literal_boundary/loop_boundary compute `value +/- 1` in i128 with no bounds check (integer_boundary.zig:83-84), so a max-value decimal comparison operand crashes the whole scan (H1), and doctest `--case` line refs overflow an unchecked u32 accumulator into a SIGABRT instead of a clean not-found (M4). The advertised safety-mode matrix is inert: safety_modes.buildFlag (the `-O<mode>` flag) has no production caller — confirmed only self- and test-referenced — so every mode runs Debug and `--mode ReleaseFast` results are silently wrong (H5). Under the supported `--jobs > 1` path, setupWorkspace walks the live project root (cli.zig:249-256) while sibling workers create/delete workspaces inside that same tree, nondeterministically misclassifying mutants as `invalid` (H3). Mutation generation also emits guaranteed-dead mutants: errdefer_remove orphans the statement's terminating `;` (error_path.zig:94-100), making the common single-expression errdefer idiom always a compile_error and thus never killable (H2), while error_catch_unreachable strands `|err|` captures (M1) and boolean_literal mutates `true`/`false` enum field names (L23). Several documented privacy/determinism guarantees are only partially met — id/operator/selection_reason AI-context fields and file:// URIs bypass redactField (M9, M8, L29), and `//`-comment and post-`:`/`=`/`>` path over/under-matching corrupts excerpts and leaks absolute paths into committed reports (M3, L28). A recurring smell compounds the risk: config and API surface that is parsed and validated but never consumed (cache.enabled/directory, report.formats, ai.source_context_lines, zig.modes=[]) and dead public exports (writeJson, cacheDirIn/outDirIn, diagnosticsToJson, the whole src/property subsystem), which makes the system look more wired than it is. Test coverage is broad but under-pins the parts that matter most — report.summarize arithmetic is unpinned against a score-inflating regression (M10), the dangling-original integration guard is inert under an arena allocator (L2), and the sole e2e kill/survive test binds only fungible aggregate counts so an add↔mul classification swap passes CI (S7).

## Confirmed Findings (detail)

### [H1] integer_literal_boundary / loop_boundary crash the whole process via i128 overflow panic on a max-value decimal literal

- **Severity:** High  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 3/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D1-mutators
- **Location(s):** `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/mutators/integer_boundary.zig`, `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/mutators/loop_boundary.zig`, `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/run_command.zig`, `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/list_mutants_command.zig`

**Evidence:**
```zig
integer_boundary.zig parses any plain-decimal literal operand of a comparison into i128 and then emits value+1 / value-1 with NO overflow guard:
  line 70-71: `if (!isPlainDecimal(text)) return; const value = std.fmt.parseInt(i128, text, 10) catch return;`
  line 83:    `try emit(... "{d}", .{value + 1});`
  line 84:    `try emit(... "{d}", .{value - 1});`
isPlainDecimal (line 32-36) accepts ANY all-ASCII-digit string, so the literal `170141183460469231731687303715884105727` (i128 max = 2^127-1) passes the gate, parses successfully into i128, and then `value + 1` overflows i128. In Zig's default Debug/ReleaseSafe this is a checked illegal behavior -> `panic: integer overflow`, which a `catch` cannot intercept. loop_boundary.zig has the identical pattern at lines 115/120/121 for a `for (a..b)` range end literal. Both collect() functions run IN-PROCESS during candidate generation: run_command.zig:595-596 and list_mutants_command.zig:92-93 call `integer_boundary.collect` / `loop_boundary.collect` directly inside the candidate loop (run_command.zig:581-597), not in a sandboxed subprocess, so the panic aborts the entire `zentinel run` / `zentinel list-mutants` invocation before any mutant is applied or reported. The `-1` path is safe (isPlainDecimal forbids the leading '-', so the smallest reachable value is 0 and 0-1=-1 fits i128); only the `value + 1` site overflows, and only at exactly i128 max.
```

**Tool confirmation:** Reproduced the exact code path with the real Zig 0.16.0 toolchain in /tmp/zentinel_mut_test/repro_full.zig, which copies isPlainDecimal verbatim and runs parseInt(i128)+`value + 1`: `zig test` output -> `thread panic: integer overflow` at `const s = try std.fmt.bufPrint(&buf, "{d}", .{value + 1});` with signal ABRT (exit non-zero). A second standalone repro (check_overflow.zig) confirmed parseInt succeeds on the i128-max string (`parsed value ok = 170141183460469231731687303715884105727`) and that `value + 1` then panics. AST dump (check_nodedata.zig) confirmed `x == 0` yields a `.number_literal` operand node reached by emitForOperand, and `for (0..10)` yields a `.for_range` whose end is a `.number_literal`, so both collect paths genuinely reach this arithmetic. grep confirmed the four arithmetic sites (integer_boundary.zig:83-84, loop_boundary.zig:120-121) and that no surrounding guard exists. grep of test/mutators/{integer_boundary,loop_boundary}_test.zig found no test exercising a literal anywhere near i128 max (largest is unrelated), so the case is uncovered.

**Why it is wrong:** Mutation candidate generation must be total over any parseable input file: the mutator's OWN computation (value+/-1 in i128) overflows on a legal Zig source literal. There is no bounds check before the addition and the panic is unrecoverable, so a single such literal in any scanned production file (e.g. a hash seed, bitmask, or i128 boundary constant written in decimal) takes down the run.

**Impact & repro:** Denial of the whole tool: any project whose source contains a plain-decimal integer literal equal to 170141183460469231731687303715884105727 used as a direct comparison operand (==,!=,<,<=,>,>=) or as a `for (a..b)` range end will make `zentinel run` and `zentinel list-mutants` abort with `panic: integer overflow` during candidate generation. No mutants are produced, no report is written, and the failure is a hard process abort rather than a graceful diagnostic. This contradicts the deterministic_core contract that mutators emit candidates (or skip) but never crash.  
_Repro:_ 1) Create a file f.zig with: `fn f(x: i128) bool { return x == 170141183460469231731687303715884105727; }` 2) Run `zentinel run` (or `zentinel list-mutants`) over it (integer_literal_boundary operator is stable/enabled, config.zig). 3) During generateCandidates, integer_boundary.emitForOperand parses the literal to i128 max and evaluates `value + 1` -> process aborts with `thread panic: integer overflow`. Equivalent for loop_boundary with `for (0..170141183460469231731687303715884105727) |i| {}`. Verified mechanically in /tmp/zentinel_mut_test/repro_full.zig and check_overflow.zig against zig 0.16.0.

**Suggested fix:** Guard the arithmetic against i128 overflow before formatting. Use `std.math.add(i128, value, 1)` / `std.math.sub(i128, value, 1)` and `catch return` (skip the boundary that would overflow), or parse into i129 / use `@addWithOverflow` and drop the overflowing candidate. Same fix at integer_boundary.zig:83-84 and loop_boundary.zig:120-121. A boundary mutant at the literal's own representational max is not meaningful anyway, so skipping it is correct behavior. Add a regression test with the i128-max literal as a comparison operand and as a for-range end.

**Lens verdicts:** CORRECTNESS: UPHELD, Zig-semantics/safety: integer overflow UB, comptime-vs-runtime arithmetic, error-union vs illegal-behavior, Debug-vs-ReleaseFast runtime-safety, in-process panic propagation.: UPHELD, REPRODUCTION: UPHELD

---
### [H2] errdefer_remove emits a dangling-semicolon (syntactically invalid) mutant -> guaranteed compile_error

- **Severity:** High  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 3/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D1-mutators
- **Location(s):** `src/mutators/error_path.zig:86-118`, `test/fixtures/mutators/errdefer/ops.zig:5`, `test/fixtures/mutators/errdefer/survivor.zig:8`, `test/mutators/errdefer_test.zig:35`

**Evidence:**
```zig
`collectErrdefer` (src/mutators/error_path.zig:94-100) computes the candidate span from the `errdefer` keyword (`kw = tree.nodeMainToken(node)`) through the *body expression's* last token (`last = tree.lastToken(node)`; `end = tokenStart(last) + len(tokenSlice(last))`) and replaces that span with the literal `"errdefer {}"`. For an errdefer whose body is an expression or assignment (the dominant idiom, e.g. `errdefer alloc.destroy(p);`), `lastToken` of the `.@"errdefer"` node resolves through `opt_token_and_node[1]` to the body and stops at the body's final token (`)` or the RHS) — it does NOT include the statement-terminating `;`. The span is therefore `errdefer alloc.destroy(p)` (no semicolon), confirmed verbatim by the project's own test at test/mutators/errdefer_test.zig:35 which asserts `c[0].original == "errdefer alloc.destroy(p)"`. Applying the replacement leaves the orphaned `;`, producing `errdefer {};`. Block-bodied errdefers (`errdefer { ... }`) are the only safe case because `}` ends the statement with no trailing `;`.
```

**Tool confirmation:** (1) Zig 0.16.0 AST layout confirmed against the real std source `/Users/.../0.16.0/lib/std/zig/Ast.zig`: `.@"errdefer"` uses `opt_token_and_node` and `lastToken` follows `opt_token_and_node[1]` (line 957), i.e. the body — never the trailing `;`. (2) A standalone program replicating the exact span math (`zig run`) printed `original errdefer span = <<errdefer alloc.destroy(p)>>` and mutated source containing `errdefer {};` for both expr-body and assign-body cases. (3) `zig ast-check` on the mutated outputs (expr body /tmp/m1.zig, assign body /tmp/m2.zig, and the survivor-fixture form /tmp/survivor_mut.zig) ALL produced `error: expected statement, found ';'` at the `errdefer {};` line. (4) Control `errdefer {}` with no trailing `;` (block-body result, /tmp/m3.zig) ast-check passed (exit clean, no error). (5) Proposed-fix probe (extend span by one token when `tokens[last+1] == .semicolon`) produced `errdefer {}` and ast-check passed.

**Why it is wrong:** Off-by-one in the span end: the errdefer mutator targets a whole *statement* but spans only its *body expression*, orphaning the `;` that terminates the statement. `error_catch_unreachable` and `optional_orelse_unreachable` are unaffected because they target sub-expressions whose surrounding `;` belongs to an enclosing statement, not to the spanned node.

**Impact & repro:** For the common errdefer idiom (single-expression / assignment cleanup such as `errdefer allocator.free(buf);`, `errdefer self.deinit();`, `errdefer alloc.destroy(p);`), every `errdefer_remove` mutant is syntactically invalid by construction and the `zig build`/`zig test` command fails to compile. mutant_runner.terminalStatus (src/mutant_runner.zig:46-52) maps a compile failure to status `.compile_error` (operator declares `expected_compile = .may_fail`, so it is not treated as a crash/abort). Net effect: these mutants can NEVER be killed-or-survived and contribute ZERO test-adequacy signal — the operator is silently a no-op for its most important targets. The project's own survivor fixture (test/fixtures/mutators/errdefer/survivor.zig) documents this exact mutant as an intended SURVIVOR demonstrating a weak test suite, but it actually yields a compile_error, so the documented survivor scenario is unreachable. Only block-bodied errdefers produce valid mutants. The entire test suite pass …[clipped]  
_Repro:_ 1) Take any function with an expression-bodied errdefer, e.g. `errdefer alloc.destroy(p);` (see test/fixtures/mutators/errdefer/ops.zig:5 or survivor.zig:8). 2) Run the errdefer_remove operator (run_command.zig:594 wires error_path.collect into the live pipeline). 3) Apply the single emitted candidate (replace span `errdefer alloc.destroy(p)` with `errdefer {}`). 4) Result is `errdefer {};`. 5) `zig ast-check` on the mutated file → `error: expected statement, found ';'`. Verified directly: /tmp/m1.zig, /tmp/m2.zig, /tmp/survivor_mut.zig all fail ast-check; the same source with `errdefer {}` (no `;`) passes.

**Suggested fix:** In collectErrdefer (src/mutators/error_path.zig), extend the span to swallow the statement terminator before computing `end`: after `const last = tree.lastToken(node);`, if the following token is a semicolon, advance one token, e.g. `var last = tree.lastToken(node); const ttags = tree.tokens.items(.tag); if (last + 1 < ttags.len and ttags[last + 1] == .semicolon) last += 1;` then compute `end` from that `last`. The replacement `errdefer {}` is itself a complete statement and needs no trailing `;`. (Verified: this produces `errdefer {}` which ast-check accepts.) Also update the test expectation at test/mutators/errdefer_test.zig:35 (which currently bakes in the buggy span by expecting `original == "errdefer alloc.destroy(p)"` without the `;`) and add a regression test that compiles/ast-checks the *applied* mutation rather than only inspecting candidate metadata.

**Lens verdicts:** CORRECTNESS: UPHELD, Zig-semantics/safety: parser/AST token-span semantics for the `.@"errdefer"` node and the real-compiler validity of the resulting `errdefer {};` source.: UPHELD, REPRODUCTION: UPHELD

---
### [H3] Parallel setupWorkspace full-tree walk races sibling workers' create/delete under the shared project root -> spurious 'invalid' mutants

- **Severity:** High  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 3/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D2-applyrevert, D5-concurrency
- **Location(s):** `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/cli.zig:240-260`, `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/cli.zig:281-308`, `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/worker_pool.zig:54-89`, `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/mutant_runner.zig:159-166`, `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/cli.zig`, `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/run_command.zig`, `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/worker_pool.zig`, `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/mutant_runner.zig`

**Evidence:**
```zig
setupWorkspace (src/cli.zig:240) builds each per-mutant workspace by walking the ENTIRE shared project dir: `var walker = try rt.root_dir.walk(rt.gpa); while (try walker.next(rt.io)) |entry| { if (entry.kind != .file) continue; if (copyExcluded(entry.path)) continue; ... rt.root_dir.copyFile(entry.path, dir, entry.path, ...) }` and afterward `dir.writeFile(... m.file ...)`. The mutant runner adapter mutantRunSpecsFn (src/cli.zig:296-304) runs this per worker and tears the workspace down in a `defer`: `ws.dir.close(rt.io); rt.root_dir.deleteTree(rt.io, ws.rel) catch { _ = rt.cleanup_failures.fetchAdd(1, .monotonic); }`. The workspace root is `.zig-cache/zentinel/workspaces/<run_id>/<mutant_id>` (src/worker_pool.zig:88-90). worker_pool.run (src/worker_pool.zig:54-83) spawns real std.Threads for jobs>1, each calling runOneMutant -> mutant_executor.runSpecs -> mutantRunSpecsFn with the SHARED RunCtx (rt.root_dir, rt.gpa). copyExcluded (src/cli.zig:228-232) only filters which yielded files are copied; it does NOT prune walker descent. Zig 0.16.0 std.Io.Dir.Walker.next (/opt/homebrew/Cellar/zig/0.16.0_1/lib/zig/std/Io/Dir.zig:365-372) unconditionally calls `self.inner.enter(io, entry.?)` for every directory entry, and enter (Dir.zig:277-296) does `entry.dir.openDir(io, entry.basename, .{.iterate=true})` propagating any error except NameTooLong; SelectiveWalker.next (Dir.zig:237-258) returns that error to the caller. deleteTree's own doc (Dir.zig:1401) states 'This operation is not atomic on most file systems.' So while worker A's walker descends into `.zig-cache/zentinel/workspaces/<run_id>/<mutantB>` (it is NOT skipped from descent), worker B's defer can deleteTree that exact subtree, making A's enter()->openDir fail with FileNotFound/NotDir. `try walker.next` then propagates the error out of setupWorkspace; mutantRunSpecsFn's `setupWorkspace(...) catch { return ...runSpecs(... .create_failed ...) }` converts it to WorkspaceOutcome.create_failed, and mutant_runner.runSpe …[clipped]
```

**Tool confirmation:** zig_std_signature Dir.walk => snippet 'Recursively iterates over a directory ... See also: walkSelectively' (source /opt/homebrew/Cellar/zig/0.16.0_1/lib/zig/std/Io/Dir.zig:397). zig_std_signature Dir.deleteTree => doc 'This operation is not atomic on most file systems.' (Dir.zig:1401). Direct read of Dir.zig:237-296,365-372 confirms Walker.next ALWAYS enter()s directories and enter()'s openDir return-propagates errors (only NameTooLong is unreachable), and SelectiveWalker.next returns iterator errors to the caller. Bash grep confirmed run.jobs is parsed (src/config.zig:380) and --jobs maps to a worker count (src/run_command.zig:192-197, runOneMutant at src/run_command.zig:118-123). Bash grep of test/ shows the parallel test in test/run_command_test.zig injects a MOCK MutantRunner; the only real-disk integration test (test/integration_run_test.zig) runs the fixture test/fixtures/integration/sample/zentinel.toml which sets NO jobs (defaults to 1), so the real concurrent setupWorkspace path is never exercised. || zig_references (loaded via ToolSearch) on src/cli.zig line 239 char 3 returned exactly two locations: the def {line 239} and ONE caller {line 295,char15} = mutantRunSpecsFn  …[clipped]

**Why it is wrong:** The walk is rooted at rt.root_dir (the live project root that physically contains `.zig-cache/zentinel/workspaces/...`), not a pristine snapshot. Because workspaces are created and torn down inside the very tree every other worker is simultaneously traversing, the recursive openDir/copyFile syscalls observe a directory subtree mutating underneath them. There is no mutex, no per-worker root snapshot, and no per-entry error tolerance (every walker.next/copyFile is a hard `try`), so any transient FileNotFound/NotDir from the race is converted into a terminal create_failed for that mutant.

**Impact & repro:** Under the supported `--jobs > 1` / `run.jobs > 1` parallel mode, mutants are nondeterministically misclassified as `invalid` instead of their true `killed`/`survived` verdict. This (a) directly violates the framework's core invariant that worker count changes only concurrency and never a mutant's result (worker_pool.zig:5-8, run_command.zig:107/117/277-281); (b) corrupts the mutation score: an `invalid` mutant is excluded from kill/survive accounting (report.summarize), so survivors can be silently dropped from the denominator, inflating or destabilizing the score run-to-run; (c) makes parallel runs non-reproducible, defeating the determinism guarantee the report format is built on. Also a latent O(N^2) traversal blowup: each of N workers re-walks (and openDir-descends into) every other worker's copied tree under `.zig-cache/zentinel/workspaces/`, since those dirs are excluded from copy but not from traversal.  
_Repro:_ 1) Create a project with several mutable .zig files producing many candidates so workers overlap in time. 2) Set run.jobs = 8 (or pass `--jobs 8`) and run `zentinel run --report json`. 3) Run repeatedly; observe that the set of mutants with status `invalid` (failure_summary 'sandbox: mutation workspace could not be created') varies between runs and shrinks/disappears at `--jobs 1`. The variance is the race: workers' tree walks transiently fail to openDir a sibling workspace being deleteTree'd. A deterministic stress harness can force it by making teardown of early-finishing mutants overlap the walk of later ones (e.g. uneven per-mutant test durations). No equivalent automated coverage exists today (integration test uses jobs=1; parallel unit test uses a mock runner).

**Suggested fix:** Do not walk the live shared project tree from each worker during the parallel phase. Options: (a) snapshot/copy the project tree ONCE (excluding .git/.zig-cache/zig-out) into an immutable per-run base before Phase B, then for each mutant hardlink/copy from that stable base instead of re-walking root_dir; (b) use std.Io.Dir.walkSelectively and refuse to `enter()` any directory whose path is copyExcluded (.zig-cache, zig-out, .git) so workers never descend into the actively-mutating cache tree -- this both removes the race source and the wasted I/O; (c) at minimum, build each workspace from the already-in-memory FileSource set (files.items are read into memory in runRun, src/cli.zig:481-493) plus the unchanged auxiliary files, rather than re-reading the filesystem under concurrent mutation. Whichever path is chosen, a workspace-creation failure that is actually a transient FS race must not be collapsed into mutant status `.invalid` without retry, since that hides survivors.

**Lens verdicts:** CORRECTNESS: UPHELD, Zig-semantics/safety: verified Walker descent/error-propagation semantics against the real std source, the allocator ownership/thread-safety of the shared RunCtx.gpa, defer-teardown ordering, and Debug-vs-ReleaseFast runtime behavior.: UPHELD, REPRODUCTION: UPHELD

### [H4] isCompileFailure marker heuristic is unreliable under `zig build test` -> compile/test-failure misclassification (both kill inflation and deflation)

- **Severity:** High  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 3/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D3-killdetect
- **Location(s):** `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/runner.zig`, `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/mutant_runner.zig`, `src/runner.zig:108-127,156-161`, `src/config.zig:362`, `test/runner_baseline_test.zig:176-223`

**Evidence:**
```zig
src/runner.zig:108-127 defines the only compile-error vs test-failure signal:
  const compile_diagnostic_marker = ": error: ";
  const test_runner_summary_marker = "passed;";
  fn isCompileFailure(stdout, stderr) bool {
      if (outputContains(stdout, stderr, test_runner_summary_marker)) return false;
      return outputContains(stdout, stderr, compile_diagnostic_marker);
  }
runner.zig:161 is its sole consumer: `failure_kind = if (isCompileFailure(raw.stdout, raw.stderr)) .compile_error else .test_failure;`. mutant_runner.zig:49 then maps `.failed` with `failure_kind == .compile_error` to ResultStatus `.compile_error`, and everything else to `.killed`. So the killed/compile_error split rests entirely on these two string markers, with NO use of the actual term/exit_code to disambiguate.

The classifier assumes (per docs/REPORT_FORMAT.md:232) that a post-compile assertion failure ALWAYS prints the `N passed; M skipped; K failed.` summary (carrying "passed;") and that ": error: " only appears for compile diagnostics. Both assumptions are false in common configurations. || isCompileFailure (runner.zig:124-126) returns true only if output lacks `test_runner_summary_marker` ("passed;", :109) AND contains `compile_diagnostic_marker` (": error: ", :108). For a non-zero exit, classifyCommand sets failure_kind = compile_error iff isCompileFailure else test_failure (runner.zig:161); terminalStatus maps .failed+.test_failure -> .killed (mutant_runner.zig:49). The default test.commands is ["zig build test"] (config.zig:362). Under `zig build test` (which uses the `--listen=-` build protocol), a compile/link failure does NOT emit a `<path>:<line>:<col>: error:` token and does NOT print `N passed;`, so isCompileFailure returns FALSE and the build failure is bucketed as test_failure -> killed.
```

**Tool confirmation:** Ground-truth experiments on the pinned Zig 0.16.0 (confirmed `zig version` = 0.16.0):
(1) Direct `zig test` all-pass prints `All 1 tests passed.` -> contains "passed." NOT "passed;". Only failure/skip prints the semicolon form `N passed; M skipped; K failed.`.
(2) Under `zig build test`, the `--listen=-` aggregator NEVER forwards the per-binary `N passed;` summary. A RUNTIME test failure (exit 1, not a compile error) emits `error: 'mod.test.x' failed:` plus `Build Summary: 3/5 steps succeeded (1 failed); 1/2 tests passed (1 failed)`; grep over the captured stdout+stderr: `passed;` count = 0, `: error: ` count = 0 (the `error:` lines are line-start, no leading `: `). A PANIC failure under `zig build test` likewise shows `passed;`=0.
(3) Decisive repro: a `zig build test` runtime failure where the failing test legitimately emits a `path:line:col: error: msg` diagnostic line (captured stderr included `src/foo.zig:3:5: error: expected type 'u8'`). grep on the real captured output: `passed;` = 0, `: error: ` = 1. Feeding that exact output through the isCompileFailure logic: outputContains("passed;")=False, outputContains(": error: ")=True => isCompileFailure=True => failure_kind=.compil …[clipped]

**Why it is wrong:** The two markers are not reliable discriminators. (a) The `passed;` guard depends on the per-binary test-runner summary line, which `zig build test` (the standard configured command for real Zig projects) does not forward -- it shows `; X/Y tests passed (Z failed)` instead, which has no `passed;` substring; a panicking test under direct `zig test` also never prints the summary because it aborts mid-run. (b) The `: error: ` marker matches ANY captured line of the form `<token>: error: <text>`, which is exactly what compiler/parser/linter test suites assert on or print -- including Zentinel's own AST/config diagnostic paths. So a genuine post-compile assertion failure (a real KILL) that emits a diagnostic-shaped line, with no `passed;` summary, is classified `.compile_error` instead of `.killed`.

**Impact & repro:** Kill-detection soundness failure: genuinely killed mutants are silently moved into the compile_error bucket. report_text.zig:49 headlines `{killed} killed, {survived} survived`; report.summarize (report.zig:223-235) counts compile_error separately from killed. A misclassified kill is dropped from `summary.killed` and never appears as survived either -- it is hidden in a bucket the user reads as a non-viable mutation. This deflates the reported mutation/kill score and corrupts the core promise of the tool. It is one-directional but systematic: it triggers for the most common build command (`zig build test`) whenever a failing test's output contains a `path:line:col: error:` diagnostic, and for any panic-induced kill whose panic message/trace contains `: error: `. (The inverse -- compile_error -> killed false kill -- was checked and is NOT generally reachable because compile errors never produce `passed;`; the failure mode here is kill -> compile_error.)  
_Repro:_ 1) Project configured with `commands = ["zig build test"]` (the default for real Zig projects). 2) A test exercises a component that prints/returns a Zig-compiler-style diagnostic `path:line:col: error: msg` (e.g. any AST/parse/lint/config-diagnostic test -- Zentinel itself has these). 3) A mutant makes that test FAIL at runtime (compiles fine, assertion fails). 4) Captured stdout+stderr then contains `: error: ` (from the diagnostic) but NOT `passed;` (zig build aggregates the summary). 5) isCompileFailure returns true -> result status `.compile_error`. EXPECTED `.killed`. Confirmed end-to-end with a real `zig build test` run (driver WIFEXITED 1) whose captured stderr produced `passed;`=0, `: error: `=1, and via feeding that exact captured output through the classifier logic.

**Suggested fix:** Do not rely on fragile output substrings alone to separate compile_error from test_failure. Prefer positive evidence that compilation succeeded and the test binary ran. Options, best first: (a) For generated/known `zig test <file>` and `zig build test` commands, detect a compile failure by the ABSENCE of any per-test progress/result line (e.g. `N/M ...OK|FAIL|SKIP`, the build `run test ... pass/fail/crash` line, or the `Build Summary:` token) rather than by presence of `: error: `; if the test binary demonstrably ran (any test-result line or a Build Summary present) then a non-zero exit is a test_failure/kill even if `: error: ` appears in asserted output. (b) Anchor compile_diagnostic_marker to a line START (`^<path>:<line>:<col>: error:`) and require it to NOT be inside the indented test-output block that `zig build` prefixes with whitespace, so diagnostics emitted BY a running test do not count. (c) Broaden test_runner_summary detection to also recognize the `zig build` aggregated f …[clipped]

**Lens verdicts:** CORRECTNESS: UPHELD, Zig-semantics/safety: UPHELD, REPRODUCTION: UPHELD

### [H5] Safety/optimization mode is never applied to the spawned command: buildFlag is dead code, every mode runs identical Debug

- **Severity:** High  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 2/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D2-applyrevert
- **Location(s):** `src/run_command.zig`, `src/safety_modes.zig`, `src/mutant_runner.zig`, `src/cli.zig`

**Evidence:**
```zig
The mode flows as a pure LABEL and never alters the executed argv. In run_command.zig the matrix is built by re-running mutants per mode WITHOUT any optimize flag: line 317 `col[ji] = mutant_executor.runSpecs(job.candidate, job.source, job.command_specs, job.commands, m).status;` passes the same `job.command_specs` (the narrowed `zig test <file>` / configured argv) for every mode `m`. That reaches cli.zig `mutantRunSpecsFn` (line 281), which receives `mode` (line 286) but only forwards it to `mutant_runner.runSpecs(..., mode)` (line 307); the actual spawn `executor.run(spec.argv)` (mutant_runner.zig:175) runs the argv unchanged. mutant_runner.zig uses `mode` only to populate the result label (`.mode = mode` at lines 68/80; classifyFromCommands line 57). The ONLY function that produces the `-O<mode>` flag, `safety_modes.buildFlag` (src/safety_modes.zig:27-34, `.ReleaseFast => "-OReleaseFast"`), has ZERO production callers. The docs state the intended behavior: docs/ZIG_SEMANTICS.md:82 "Zig safety and optimization modes affect behavior" and :96 "Killed in Debug, survived in ReleaseFast."
```

**Tool confirmation:** zig_references on src/safety_modes.zig:27 (`buildFlag`) returned ok:true, result:null (no callers). Repo-wide grep `grep -rn buildFlag src test build.zig`: only the definition (src/safety_modes.zig:27) and 4 lines of one isolated unit test (test/safety_mode_matrix_test.zig:31-35 `expectEqualStrings("-OReleaseFast", safety_modes.buildFlag(.ReleaseFast))`). grep for `-O`/`ODebug`/`ORelease`/`optimize` across all of src/ matched ONLY safety_modes.zig:27-34 (the dead function) — no injection site exists. `zig build` / `zig build test` both pass (ground truth), so this compiles and the suite is green despite the dead path.

**Why it is wrong:** Mutation-testing correctness under safety modes is a documented headline feature (task 058, docs/ZIG_SEMANTICS.md Safety Modes). Because the optimize flag is never passed, `zig test <file>` always builds in the default (Debug) optimization, so: (1) `zentinel run --mode ReleaseFast` records `result.mode = ReleaseFast` (run_command.zig:233, buildEntry mode label) for a mutant that was actually evaluated in Debug — an untruthful report field that also poisons the result-cache key (cache.zig computeKey includes `.mode = @tagName(mode)`, run_command.zig:354, so a Debug result is cached under a ReleaseFast key); (2) a multi-mode `zig.modes = ["Debug","ReleaseFast"]` matrix re-runs byte-identical commands for each column, so the mode-dependent kill the feature exists to surface (a Debug overflow/bounds safety check that is elided in ReleaseFast → killed in Debug, survives in ReleaseFast) can NEVER be observed in a real run; `safety_modes.isModeDependent` (safety_modes.zig:96) is effectively always false. This is a kill-detection/classification correctness failure squarely in this dimension's scope.

**Impact & repro:** Any user relying on Zig safety modes gets silently wrong mutation results. `--mode ReleaseFast`/`--mode ReleaseSmall` are inert (they only relabel a Debug run). The mode matrix reports uniform statuses regardless of true mode-dependence, hiding exactly the overflow/bounds/unreachable survivors that only appear when Debug safety checks are elided in Release builds. The report asserts a build mode the compiler never used, violating report truthfulness (docs/REPORT_FORMAT.md:83 lists `safety mode` as a determinism input).  
_Repro:_ Set `zig.modes = ["Debug", "ReleaseFast"]` (or run `zentinel run --mode ReleaseFast`) on a project with an integer-overflow mutant whose Debug safety check kills it. Observe in the JSON report that every `mode_matrix[*].status` is identical (and equals the Debug result), and `result.mode` claims ReleaseFast while the spawned command was plain `zig test <file>` with no `-OReleaseFast`. Code-path confirmation: trace `mode` from run_command.zig:233/317 → cli.zig:286/307 → mutant_runner.zig:175 (`executor.run(spec.argv)`, argv never amended) and note `buildFlag` is never called (zig_references null).

**Suggested fix:** Inject `safety_modes.buildFlag(mode)` into the build/test argv when the command is a Zig build/test invocation (e.g. append `-O<mode>` to `zig test <file>` / `zig build test` argv in commandSpecsForSelection/commandSpecsForConfigured, or have the production executor in cli.zig add it per-mode). The mode must reach `executor.run` as an actual argv element, not just the result label. Then add an integration test whose mock/real executor classifies based on the PRESENCE of the `-O<mode>` token in argv (the current modeCmd mock at test/run_command_test.zig:139-152 ignores argv and branches on the `mode` parameter, which is why the gap is invisible to tests). Until wired, `--mode`/multi-mode should be documented as non-functional or rejected rather than silently mislabeling.

**Lens verdicts:** CORRECTNESS: REFUTED, ZIG-SEMANTICS/SAFETY: UPHELD, REPRODUCTION: UPHELD

### [M1] error_catch_unreachable emits guaranteed compile_error at every catch-with-capture site (unused capture)

- **Severity:** Medium  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 3/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D1-mutators
- **Location(s):** `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/mutators/error_path.zig`, `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/test/mutators/error_path_test.zig`, `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/sandbox.zig`

**Evidence:**
```zig
error_path.zig:48-80 collectCatch sets the candidate span to the handler expression ONLY (firstToken..lastToken of nodeData(node).node_and_node[1]) and replacement = "unreachable". The `|err|` capture is OUTSIDE that span, so applying the candidate to `x catch |err| handle(err)` yields `x catch |err| unreachable`. The only guard is `if (std.mem.eql(u8, original, "unreachable")) return;` (line 63) -- there is NO capture detection. test/mutators/error_path_test.zig:65-85 EXPLICITLY asserts this for `e catch |err| handle(err)`: c[0].original == "handle(err)", c[0].replacement == "unreachable" (comment line 82: 'The span is the handler expression only, not the |err| capture.'), but the test never compiles the produced mutant. sandbox.zig:38-40 replaces exactly source[byte_start..byte_end] (the handler text) with the replacement, leaving the capture in place. Because a Zig capture's scope is only the handler, every COMPILING `catch |e| handler` uses `e` in the handler; replacing the handler with `unreachable` always orphans the capture.
```

**Tool confirmation:** Real zig 0.16.0 build-obj of the exact mutant text (cwd /tmp, zig 0.16.0 at /opt/homebrew/bin/zig): `pub fn f(x: anyerror!i32) i32 { const v = x catch |e| unreachable; return v; }` -> `c1.zig:2:24: error: unused capture` (also reproduced for the block-handler form, same error). CONTROL: `x catch unreachable` (no capture) compiled with NO error. std.zig.Ast dump confirmed the catch handler span excludes the capture (handler span printed as 'handle(e)' for `x catch |e| handle(e)`) and that a capture is detectable as token_tags[catch_main_token + 1] == .pipe (printed: "next tok tag=pipe '|'" for the capture form vs "number_literal '0'" for the no-capture form). mutant_runner.zig:46-53 terminalStatus maps any failed+compile_error command to status .compile_error and does NOT consult expected_compile; report.zig:228 buckets it into summary.compile_error. grep confirmed expected_compile is metadata only on the main run path (run_command.zig:665, report.zig:193), never used in classification.

**Why it is wrong:** The handler is the sole user of the capture variable; substituting `unreachable` for the handler leaves `|err|` unused, which Zig rejects with `error: unused capture`. Because expected_compile is not consulted by the classifier (mutant_runner.zig terminalStatus), the result is deterministically classified as `compile_error`, not `survived` and not `killed`.

**Impact & repro:** On any codebase that uses the idiomatic `something() catch |e| <handler>` form, error_catch_unreachable wastes a full apply+compile+classify cycle per site and can NEVER produce a kill there -- so it never actually tests whether the error branch is covered (the operator's entire purpose). Each such site adds noise to summary.compile_error. This is an operator-effectiveness/semantic-validity defect, not a hidden survivor: the main engine does not misclassify it as survived (so mutation score is not silently inflated), but the catch-with-capture handler -- arguably the highest-value error-path target -- is systematically un-testable by this operator. The doctest mutation path is unaffected because it only wires Phase 1 operators (arithmetic/comparison/logical/boolean), not error_path.  
_Repro:_ 1) Create a file with `pub fn f(x: anyerror!i32) i32 { const v = x catch |e| return; _ = v; return 0; }` style code, or simply `const v = x catch |e| handle(e);`. 2) Run the error_path collector (or `zentinel run` with error_catch_unreachable enabled). The emitted candidate has original = the handler text and replacement = "unreachable". 3) Apply it (sandbox.apply) -> `x catch |e| unreachable`. 4) `zig build-obj` the result -> `error: unused capture`. Minimal proof already run: /tmp/c1.zig and /tmp/c2.zig both produce `error: unused capture`; /tmp/c3.zig (no capture) compiles clean. Existing test test/mutators/error_path_test.zig:65 emits exactly this candidate.

**Suggested fix:** In collectCatch (error_path.zig), detect a capture before emitting: if `parsed.tree.tokens.items(.tag)[catch_main_token + 1] == .pipe`, then EITHER (a) skip the site (documented boundary, like the existing `orelse unreachable` skip), OR (b) extend the replacement span to begin right after the `catch` keyword (covering `|err| handler`) and replace the whole thing with `unreachable`, producing `x catch unreachable` -- which compiles (the control case proved this). Option (b) preserves the operator's intent for capture sites. Either way, add a test that COMPILES the produced mutant (e.g. via the integration/sandbox path) so an always-compile-error candidate cannot pass CI again; the current test only asserts the candidate fields, never that the mutant compiles.

**Lens verdicts:** CORRECTNESS: UPHELD, Zig-semantics/safety: error-union handling, capture-variable scope, comptime-vs-runtime rejection, and whether the Zig 0.16.0 compiler actually rejects the produced mutant as claimed.: UPHELD, REPRODUCTION: UPHELD

### [M2] copyExcluded path-prefix over-match drops discovered sibling-dir source files -> writeFile fails, mutant misclassified .invalid

- **Severity:** Medium  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 3/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D2-applyrevert
- **Location(s):** `src/cli.zig:228`, `src/cli.zig:255`, `src/cli.zig:258`, `src/cli.zig:296`, `src/project_model.zig:73`, `src/config.zig:97`, `src/mutant_runner.zig:159`

**Evidence:**
```zig
src/cli.zig:228-232 `copyExcluded` excludes workspace-copy candidates by RAW BYTE PREFIX: `std.mem.startsWith(u8, path, ".zig-cache") or startsWith(path,"zig-out") or startsWith(path,".git")`. Discovery uses SEGMENT GLOBS: src/project_model.zig:73 `isEligible` -> `matchGlob` splits on '/' and matches whole segments; default excludes (src/config.zig:97) are `{".zig-cache/**","zig-out/**","test/**"}` (note: no `.git/**`). In setupWorkspace (src/cli.zig:249-256) the walker copies each non-excluded file with `copyFile(..., .{ .make_path = true })` — this is the ONLY place a subdir parent is created in the workspace. For an excluded file that copy is skipped (line 253 `if (copyExcluded(entry.path)) continue;`). Then line 258 `dir.writeFile(rt.io, .{ .sub_path = m.file, .data = patched })` writes the patched mutant file with NO make_path. Confirmed via stdlib source: WriteFileOptions = { sub_path, data, flags: CreateFileOptions } has no make_path field; writeFile -> createFile, and createFile does not create parent dirs (WriteFileError = File.Writer.Error || File.OpenError). So when m.file lives in a subdir whose top segment only PREFIX-matches an excluded token (e.g. `zig-outputs/foo.zig`, `.github/workflows/x.zig`, `.gitlab/ci/gen.zig`, `.zig-cache-helpers/h.zig`), the parent dir is never created, writeFile returns error.FileNotFound, setupWorkspace fails, and src/cli.zig:296-298 returns `mutant_runner.runSpecs(..., .create_failed, ...)`. src/mutant_runner.zig:159-161 then returns invalidResult -> status .invalid (src/mutant_runner.zig:76-86). The mutant's real killed/survived verdict is permanently replaced by .invalid on every run. Additionally the `defer { ... deleteTree(ws.rel) }` at src/cli.zig:299-304 is armed only AFTER setupWorkspace succeeds, so the partial workspace (created dir + all files copied before the failing write) is leaked under .zig-cache on every such mutant.
```

**Tool confirmation:** Reproduced the prefix over-match with a standalone Zig 0.16.0 program (zig run): copyExcluded("zig-outputs/foo.zig")=true, copyExcluded(".github/workflows/x.zig")=true, copyExcluded(".gitlab/ci/gen.zig")=true, copyExcluded(".zig-cache-helpers/h.zig")=true, copyExcluded("zig-out/foo.zig")=true, copyExcluded("src/zig-out-helper.zig")=false. Confirmed WriteFileOptions has no make_path via zig_std_signature(Io.Dir.writeFile) + reading /opt/homebrew/Cellar/zig/0.16.0_1/lib/zig/std/Io/Dir.zig:646-664 (WriteFileOptions { sub_path, data, flags }; writeFile calls dir.createFile(io, sub_path, flags)). `zig build` exits 0 (tree unchanged; read-only audit). grep over test/ shows zero coverage of copyExcluded / prefix-vs-glob; the only integration fixture is the flat test/fixtures/integration/sample/calc.zig with no excluded-prefix subdir, so integration_run_test.zig never exercises the divergence.

**Why it is wrong:** copyExcluded was written to skip cache/VCS noise but uses startsWith on the full relative path instead of path-segment matching, so it also matches unrelated sibling directories that merely share a textual prefix (zig-out vs zig-outputs, .git vs .github/.gitlab/.gitkeep, .zig-cache vs .zig-cache-helpers). Discovery, by contrast, uses correct segment globs, so the set of files discovery feeds as mutation candidates is NOT a subset of the set copyExcluded copies. The patched-file write then relies on the (skipped) original copy having created the parent directory.

**Impact & repro:** Behavioral correctness of kill-detection/classification: any mutant whose source file sits in a subdirectory whose leading path segment prefix-collides with `.zig-cache`/`zig-out`/`.git` (reachable with a non-default `project.include` such as `**/*.zig` or `.github/**/*.zig`, or a project that stores generated/CI Zig under such a dir) is silently reported `.invalid` on every run instead of killed/survived. A real surviving mutant is hidden behind `.invalid` — exactly the seed-lead failure class, but via a live root cause distinct from the (now-fixed) dangling-original. The mutation score is silently wrong (those mutants are excluded from killed/survived) with no error surfaced. Secondary: a full project tree-copy is leaked under .zig-cache for each affected mutant because the deleteTree defer never arms. Distinct from the two prior-pass findings (full-tree-walk racing sibling deleteTree; walker descending into excluded dirs): this is a prefix-vs-segment semantic mismatch that makes the …[clipped]  
_Repro:_ 1) In a project, add a source dir whose name prefix-collides with an excluded token but is a different segment, e.g. create `zig-outputs/foo.zig` (or `.github/gen.zig`) containing a mutatable expr like `a + b`. 2) Set zentinel.toml `[project] include = ["**/*.zig"]` (or `include = ["zig-outputs/**/*.zig"]`) so discovery yields the file (default exclude `zig-out/**` does NOT match `zig-outputs/...`). 3) `zentinel run`. 4) Observe: every mutant in that file is reported status `invalid` (failure_summary 'sandbox: mutation workspace could not be created'), never killed/survived, and a leftover `.zig-cache/zentinel/workspaces/<run_id>/<m_id>/` partial tree remains. Direct unit-level repro of the root predicate: copyExcluded("zig-outputs/foo.zig") returns true (shown above), so the file is skipp …[clipped]

**Suggested fix:** Match excluded paths by whole path SEGMENT, not raw byte prefix — mirror project_model's glob semantics. E.g. exclude only when the FIRST path segment equals one of {".zig-cache","zig-out",".git"} (split entry.path on '/', compare segment[0]), or reuse project_model.matchGlob against the same exclude globs discovery uses so the copied set is exactly the discovered set's superset. Independently, harden the patched write at src/cli.zig:258 to create the parent dir first (e.g. `if (std.fs.path.dirname(m.file)) |p| try dir.createDirPath(rt.io, p);` before writeFile) so a missing parent can never silently downgrade a real mutant to .invalid. Add a setupWorkspace errdefer that deleteTree(rel) on failure to stop leaking partial workspaces. Add a regression test with an excluded-prefix sibling dir (e.g. zig-outputs/) and assert the mutant is classified killed/survived, not invalid.

**Lens verdicts:** CORRECTNESS: UPHELD, Zig-semantics/safety: UPHELD, REPRODUCTION: UPHELD

### [M3] Path redaction over-matches Zig // and /// comment markers as <path>, corrupting AI context and report excerpts

- **Severity:** Medium  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 3/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D6-safety
- **Location(s):** `src/ai/redaction.zig:85`, `src/ai/redaction.zig:91`, `src/ai/redaction.zig:101`, `src/ai/redaction.zig:104`, `src/ai/context.zig:208`, `src/report.zig:475`, `src/report.zig:490`, `src/report.zig:500`, `src/report.zig:503`

**Evidence:**
```zig
Both absolute-path normalizers treat a `/`-led run at a token boundary as a path when it contains a SECOND `/` (`inner_slashes >= 1`). Two consecutive slashes (`//`, `///`) ALWAYS satisfy this, so any `//`-led token at a boundary is rewritten to `<path>`.

redaction.zig (AI context):
  L90 `const at_boundary = i == 0 or !isPathByte(text[i - 1]);`
  L91 `if (text[i] == '/' and at_boundary) {`
  L101 `if (text[end] == '/') inner_slashes += 1;`
  L104 `if (inner_slashes >= 1) { try out.appendSlice(arena, "<path>"); changed = true; i = end; continue; }`
The module docstring (L79-84) and test (test/ai_context_test.zig:411-412) promise relative paths and division are preserved "so the AI still sees the mutated code" — but `//` is not preserved.

context.zig:208-215 `redactField` then does `if (np.changed) try log.add(label_absolute_path);` — so hitting a `//` comment also injects the synthetic `absolute_path` label into `privacy.redactions_applied`, which the code comments (context.zig:178-179) and docs/AI_CONTEXT_SCHEMA.md require to be TRUTHFUL.

report.zig:475-528 `normalizeExcerpt` has the identical boundary+inner_slashes logic (L489-507) and is the only sanitizer applied to committed-report evidence (runner.zig:96 boundedExcerpt).
```

**Tool confirmation:** Ran exact line-for-line copies of both functions via `zig run` (Zig 0.16.0).
normalizeAbsolutePaths outputs:
  in=[// increment the counter]            -> out=[<path> increment the counter]            changed=true
  in=[/// Returns the sum of a and b.]      -> out=[<path> Returns the sum of a and b.]      changed=true
  in=[x // 2]                               -> out=[x <path> 2]                               changed=true
  in=[    return a + b; // hot path]         -> out=[    return a + b; <path> hot path]        changed=true
  in=[a //= b]                              -> out=[a <path> b]                               changed=true
  in=[src/calc.zig]                         -> out=[src/calc.zig] changed=false (control)
  in=[const q = a / b;]                     -> out=[const q = a / b;] changed=false (control)
  in=[const url = "https://...api/key";]   -> unchanged (separate under-redaction, not this finding)
normalizeExcerpt outputs:
  in=[thread 1 panic: // note: see docs]    -> out=[thread 1 panic: <path> note: see docs]
  in=[error: expected ';' // trailing comment] -> out=[error: expected ';' <path> trailing comment]
  in=[(// parenthesized comment)]           -> out=[(<pa …[clipped]

**Why it is wrong:** The matcher's only test of "is this a path?" for the leading-slash branch is "does the run contain >= 1 further slash". `//` and `///` are not paths; they are Zig comment/doc-comment markers and also appear as `//=`-adjacent text and inside echoed source. Because the boundary check (start-of-text or a non-path byte such as space, `;`, `(`) is satisfied for typical comment positions, the run is consumed up to the next non-path-continuing space and replaced wholesale. The control cases (`src/calc.zig` has no boundary slash; `a / b` has zero inner slashes) correctly pass, which is why the existing tests (test/ai_context_test.zig:397-437) never caught it — none feed a `//` token.

**Impact & repro:** Two concrete harms, both on confirmed live paths: (1) AI advisory fidelity + privacy-log truthfulness: every AI flow runs mutant.diff, mutant.original, mutant.replacement, doctest mutated_diff (doctest_command.zig:1104), and all evidence excerpts through redactField/redactAndCapLogged. Any comment line in a diff/snippet/diagnostic is silently turned into `<path>`, so the model reasons over corrupted source, and privacy.redactions_applied gains a bogus `absolute_path` entry — violating the documented requirement that the field is non-empty exactly when a real redaction occurred. (2) Committed-report evidence corruption: normalizeExcerpt is the sole sanitizer for stdout_excerpt/stderr_excerpt/failure_summary in report.json; a `//`-bearing compiler note (e.g. `error: expected ';' // ...`) is lossily rewritten to `<path>`, degrading the deterministic evidence a developer relies on to triage a kill/survive. It is not a secret leak (it over-redacts) and there is currently no network egress ( …[clipped]  
_Repro:_ 1) AI context: build a mutation report whose mutant.diff (or a doctest survivor's mutation.mutated_diff) contains a context line with a `//` comment, e.g. `+    return a + b; // hot path`. Run `zentinel explain <ref> --ai-provider stub --format json`. Observe the emitted context's mutant.diff line rewritten to `... <path> hot path` and privacy.redactions_applied containing `"absolute_path"` even though no absolute path was present.
2) Report: any mutant whose command stderr contains a `//`-led token (Zig diagnostics that quote source lines with comments) yields a report.json evidence excerpt with that token replaced by `<path>`.
3) Unit-level: feed `"// note"` to redaction.normalizeAbsolutePaths -> returns `{ .text = "<path> note", .changed = true }` (confirmed by executing the exact funct …[clipped]

**Suggested fix:** Require a genuine path shape before treating a leading-slash run as a path, instead of `inner_slashes >= 1` alone. Minimal options: (a) reject runs whose first post-`/` byte is itself `/` (i.e. skip `//`/`///` sequences) before counting; (b) require the run to match an actual path grammar (a non-empty path segment of [A-Za-z0-9._-] between the slashes); or (c) require at least one alphanumeric/`.` segment between two single slashes. Apply the identical fix to both src/ai/redaction.zig normalizeAbsolutePaths (L104 guard) and src/report.zig normalizeExcerpt (L503 guard) since they share the root cause. Add regression tests feeding `//`, `///`, `a //= b`, and a `//`-comment diff line to assert they are preserved and that changed=false / redactions_applied stays empty.

**Lens verdicts:** CORRECTNESS: UPHELD, Zig-semantics/safety: UPHELD, REPRODUCTION: UPHELD

### [M4] Doctest lineOfRef unchecked u32 accumulator panics (SIGABRT) on a malformed --case source ref instead of returning CaseNotFound

- **Severity:** Medium  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 3/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D7-errorsets
- **Location(s):** `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/doctest_command.zig`

**Evidence:**
```zig
src/doctest_command.zig:258-267 `lineOfRef` parses the numeric part of a `file:line[:label]` ref with a hand-rolled accumulator and NO overflow guard:
` ` `
fn lineOfRef(ref: []const u8) u32 {
    const first = std.mem.indexOfScalar(u8, ref, ':') orelse return 0;
    var i = first + 1;
    var n: u32 = 0;
    while (i < ref.len and ref[i] >= '0' and ref[i] <= '9') : (i += 1) {
        n = n * 10 + (ref[i] - '0');
    }
    return n;
}
` ` `
User-controlled reach: cli.zig:1028 sets `case_ref = positional` for `flow_is_case`; cli.zig:1267 calls `doctest_command.run`; run() (line 103-104) calls `selectByRef(...ref)`; selectByRef (line 279-286) takes the non-`dt_` branch and calls `lineOfRef(ref)` at line 282 with the raw user ref. There is no numeric-range validation anywhere on this path. The digit loop overflows `n` once the number exceeds maxInt(u32)=4294967295. The sibling AI doctest path was deliberately hardened against exactly this: src/ai/doctest_command.zig:185 uses `std.fmt.parseInt(i64, line_str, 10) catch return null`, and test/ai_command_test.zig:441-461 (`dt_overflow`, line_start 4294967297) asserts the AI path returns a clean error. The plain doctest path was not given the same treatment, and test/doctest_cli_command_test.zig:168-186 only exercises small in-range line numbers (no overflow case).
```

**Tool confirmation:** Compiled the EXACT `lineOfRef` body as a standalone `zig test -OReleaseSafe /tmp/of_test.zig` with input `"x:99999999999"` (99,999,999,999 > maxInt(u32)). Result: `thread ... panic: integer overflow` then `error: the following test command terminated with signal ABRT`. build.zig:5 uses `b.standardOptimizeOption(.{})`, whose default is Debug (runtime safety ON), so the shipped/default binary takes the panicking path; an explicit `-Doptimize=ReleaseSafe` install panics identically. grep confirmed selectByRef->lineOfRef reachability and absence of any parseInt/range guard on the plain path (grep over src/doctest_command.zig, src/cli.zig). Whole-workspace `zig build` + `zig build test` are green (per provided ground truth), so this is an untested input class, not a build break.

**Why it is wrong:** The `--case <ref>` argument is fully attacker/typo controllable from the CLI. A perfectly ordinary malformed source ref (a fat-fingered line number, a concatenated id, or a hostile arg) makes the deterministic-core doctest command abort the whole process via an integer-overflow panic. The documented and intended outcome for an unresolvable ref is `error.CaseNotFound` -> `ZNTL_DOCTEST_CASE_NOT_FOUND` exit 2 (cli.zig:1268-1271); instead the user gets a SIGABRT crash with a std-lib panic stack trace. It is also an inconsistency: the AI doctest path resolves the identical ref class safely (parseInt catch return null), so two code paths disagree on whether the same malformed input is a clean miss or a crash.

**Impact & repro:** Process abort (SIGABRT) on `zentinel doctest --case "<file>:<overflowing-number>"` in the default Debug build and in ReleaseSafe, instead of the intended clean ZNTL_DOCTEST_CASE_NOT_FOUND (exit 2). In ReleaseFast/ReleaseSmall the multiply/add silently wraps to a truncated value (4294967296+5 -> 5), so the ref can resolve to the WRONG case rather than missing, selecting and executing an unintended doctest. No memory unsafety, but a denial-of-input / wrong-selection correctness bug on a public CLI surface.  
_Repro:_ 1) `zig build` (default = Debug, safety on). 2) Run the built binary: `./zig-out/bin/zentinel doctest --file <some-doc.md> --case "<some-doc.md>:99999999999"`. Observed: `panic: integer overflow` + SIGABRT (process aborts). Expected: `error[ZNTL_DOCTEST_CASE_NOT_FOUND]: --case did not resolve to exactly one case` and exit code 2. Minimal proof of the overflow itself: compile the `lineOfRef` body standalone and call `lineOfRef("x:99999999999")` under `-OReleaseSafe` -> panic: integer overflow / signal ABRT (done in this audit).

**Suggested fix:** Parse the line digits with a checked routine instead of the manual `n = n * 10 + d` accumulator, mirroring the already-hardened src/ai/doctest_command.zig:185. e.g. extract the digit run after the first ':' and use `std.fmt.parseInt(u32, digits, 10) catch return 0;` (or a sentinel that cannot match a real anchor line) so an out-of-range or overlong numeric ref deterministically fails to resolve and yields error.CaseNotFound rather than panicking or wrapping. Apply the identical fix to the duplicate helper in src/doctest/cache.zig:95-101 (flagged separately). Add a regression test in test/doctest_cli_command_test.zig with `case_ref = "<file>:99999999999"` asserting error.CaseNotFound, paralleling the existing AI `dt_overflow` test.

**Lens verdicts:** CORRECTNESS: UPHELD, ZIG-SEMANTICS/SAFETY: UPHELD, REPRODUCTION: UPHELD

---
### [M5] cache.enabled / cache.directory / report.formats are parsed and validated but never consumed

- **Severity:** Medium  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 3/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D11-cli
- **Location(s):** `src/config.zig`, `src/cli.zig`, `src/run_command.zig`, `src/cache.zig`

**Evidence:**
```zig
src/config.zig lines 55-57 declare cache_enabled, cache_directory, and report_formats in Config. Lines 422-424 and 388 parse and store these fields. A grep of the entire src/ tree for .cache_enabled, .cache_directory, and .report_formats returns zero hits outside config.zig. cli.zig writes cache.json to cfg.report_output_dir (line 570), not to cfg.cache_directory. The --report CLI flag governs format; cfg.report_formats is never consulted. docs/CONFIG_SPEC.md explicitly documents cache.enabled as 'Enables deterministic cache', cache.directory as 'Cache storage path', and report.formats as 'Report formats to emit', all implying observable behavior that does not exist.
```

**Tool confirmation:** Bash grep across /Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/ for .cache_enabled, .cache_directory, .report_formats returned zero hits outside config.zig. Build succeeded (exit 0, 0 diagnostics).

**Why it is wrong:** A user who configures cache.enabled = false expects caching to be disabled; it is not. A user who sets cache.directory to a custom path expects cache artifacts there; they are written to report_output_dir. A user who sets report.formats = ["json"] expects JSON-only output; it has no effect. These are silent deceptions in the public config API. report_formats also accepts arbitrary string values without per-element validation.

**Impact & repro:** Configuration expectations are silently violated. Users debugging caching or output behavior cannot rely on these fields. report_formats additionally accepts values like 'invalid_format' without error from config.load() or zentinel check.  
_Repro:_ Set [cache] enabled = false in zentinel.toml, run zentinel run. Cache behavior does not change. Set report.formats = ["invalid_format"], run zentinel check. No error is reported.

**Suggested fix:** Wire the three fields into command logic, or reject them with a 'not yet implemented' error at config.load() time. Add per-element validation of report_formats against the known enum {text, json, jsonl, junit}.

**Lens verdicts:** CORRECTNESS: UPHELD, Zig-semantics/safety: UPHELD, REPRODUCTION: UPHELD

### [M6] matcher.Mode json_unordered / regex / diagnostic are unreachable from block parsing

- **Severity:** Medium  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 3/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D11-cli
- **Location(s):** `src/doctest/block.zig`, `src/doctest/matcher.zig`, `src/doctest_command.zig`

**Evidence:**
```zig
block.MatchMode (block.zig:15) is `enum { none, subset, contains, exact }` — no `unordered` variant exists. matchModeFromToken (block.zig:59-63) has no entry for the string `"unordered"`. matchModeFor in doctest_command.zig:238-249 maps block.MatchMode to matcher.Mode but the json branch only maps `.subset => .json_subset`, collapsing everything else to `.json`. matcher.Mode.json_unordered (matcher.zig:17) is referenced only within matcher.zig itself: declaration (line 17) and the switch dispatch (line 35-36). || block.MatchMode has no `regex` or `diagnostic` variant. `matchModeFromToken` has no entry for those strings. `matchModeFor` (doctest_command.zig:238-249) for non-JSON blocks returns only `.contains` or `.exact`. The `diagnostic` language token is not recognized by `block.languageFromToken` (block.zig:37-43: only zig/bash/json/text/toml/other), so a `diagnostic expected` block gets `language=.other` and `is_doctest=false`, meaning it never reaches matching at all. The `regex` MatchMode is not produced by any block tag — `matchModeFromToken` only handles `subset`, `contains`, and `exact`.
```

**Tool confirmation:** zig_references on matcher.Mode.json_unordered (matcher.zig line 17, char 4): result set is {matcher.zig:17, matcher.zig:35} — zero external references from any file that could produce this mode value. zig_references on matcher.Mode.regex (line 14) confirms only matcher.zig and doctest_command.zig:240 (the json_subset path only). CONFIRMED. || zig_references on matcher.Mode.regex (matcher.zig line 13, char 4): {matcher.zig:13, matcher.zig:31, snapshot.zig:52} — snapshot.zig:52 is only the if-guard `if (mode == .regex)`. No reference from a caller that could set mode to .regex from block data. zig_references on matcher.Mode.diagnostic (line 15): {matcher.zig:15, matcher.zig:34, doctest_command.zig:240} — doctest_command.zig:240 is inside matchModeFor's json branch that never returns .diagnostic. CONFIRMED.

**Why it is wrong:** The docs at docs/DOCTEST_BLOCK_FORMATS.md:174 say 'arrays remain order-sensitive unless tagged `unordered`' and docs/DOCTEST_ARCHITECTURE.md:252 lists `json_unordered` as a first-class match mode. The fully-implemented `arrayMatch(.unordered)` logic in matcher.zig:313-328 is dead code: no block tag can ever produce this mode. A doctest author who writes `json expected unordered` would have `matchModeFromToken` return null for 'unordered', the block is classified without that mode attribute, and `matchModeFor` returns `.json` (exact semantic match). The `json_unordered` mode is documented, implemented, and unreachable.

**Impact & repro:** Any doctest that intends order-insensitive JSON array matching silently gets exact-order matching instead. Flaky tests that rely on implementation-defined array ordering will give false failures that can never be fixed through the documented `unordered` tag. The feature is completely non-functional despite passing compilation.  
_Repro:_ Write a markdown doctest with ` ```json expected unordered ``` ` following a CLI case that returns a JSON array in non-deterministic order. Run `zentinel doctest`. The case will fail on every order variation because `matchModeFor` returns `.json` (exact order), ignoring the `unordered` tag.

**Suggested fix:** Add `unordered` to block.MatchMode in block.zig:15 (`enum { none, subset, contains, exact, unordered }`), add `matchModeFromToken` entry for `"unordered"` at block.zig:61 (`if (std.mem.eql(u8, tok, "unordered")) return .unordered;`), and add the mapping in matchModeFor at doctest_command.zig:241 for the json branch: `.subset => .json_subset, .unordered => .json_unordered, else => .json`.

**Lens verdicts:** CORRECTNESS: UPHELD, Zig-semantics/safety: UPHELD, REPRODUCTION: UPHELD

### [M7] doctest --mutate (LIVE) under-reports: mutation_experiment.candidatesOrParseError carries the identical 4-of-8 collector restriction, silently emitting zero mutants for Phase-2-only snippets

- **Severity:** Medium  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 3/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** critic
- **Location(s):** `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/doctest/mutation_experiment.zig`, `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/cli.zig`, `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/run_command.zig`

**Evidence:**
```zig
mutation_experiment.zig:435-446 candidatesOrParseError is byte-for-byte the same 4-collector restriction as mutator_doctest.zig:68-79 (arithmetic/comparison/logical/boolean only; optional/error_path/integer_boundary/loop_boundary omitted). It is consumed by stableMutationRun at line 488: `const cands = switch (try candidatesOrParseError(arena, snippet))`, then `for (cands) |m|` at line 505 runs the mutants. For a snippet containing only Phase-2-mutable constructs (e.g. an `orelse` fallback, a `catch` handler, an `errdefer`, a loop/integer boundary) and no Phase-1 operator, candidatesOrParseError returns `.ok = &.{}` (NOT parse_error, NOT invalid_candidate), so the for-loop iterates zero times and the case yields zero mutation entries. The real run pipeline (run_command.zig:586-596) wires all 8 collectors and its own comment at lines 590-592 explicitly documents this exact bug-class: 'Phase-2 stable collectors (task 109): without these the optional, error-path, integer-boundary, and loop-boundary operators load in config but never emit a mutant, silently under-reporting coverage.'
```

**Tool confirmation:** grep `*\.collect` across src/ shows run_command.zig:586-596 and list_mutants_command.zig:83-93 each invoke all 8 collectors (arithmetic, comparison, logical, boolean, optional, error_path, integer_boundary, loop_boundary), whereas mutation_experiment.zig:440-443 and mutator_doctest.zig:73-76 invoke only the first 4. Caller chain confirmed by grep `mutation_experiment\.` in src/: cli.zig:1415 `mutation_experiment.mutateReportJson(gpa, doc, source, sr)` (the persisted `doctest --mutate` producer), cli.zig:1411 builds the SnippetRunner, cli.zig:1304 the command callback -- a live CLI path, not test-only. Read of stableMutationRun (lines 452-522) confirms the empty-candidate -> zero-entry flow with no diagnostic. (Empty-candidate behavior of the identical 4-collector body was independently observed in the validatePair Phase-2 probe: candidate_count=0.)

**Why it is wrong:** DOCTEST_MUTATION_STRATEGY.md:11 states the feature's goal is to 'Detect weak documentation examples that compile and pass but fail to catch meaningful mutations.' If a doctest example's only meaningful mutations are Phase-2 operators, the experiment generates no candidates at all, so a genuinely weak example (one a Phase-2 survivor would expose) is reported as having no mutants rather than as a documentation survivor -- the precise failure the feature exists to prevent.

**Impact & repro:** Live correctness defect in the shipped `doctest --mutate` command. A user whose documentation `zig test` snippet exercises an orelse/catch/errdefer/loop/integer-boundary construct gets a clean 'no mutations' report (false confidence) instead of the survivor analysis the real mutation pipeline would produce on the same code. Because there is no diagnostic, the gap is silent. This is the same class of silent under-reporting that task 109 fixed for run/list-mutants but which was not propagated to the two doctest copies.  
_Repro:_ Drive `zentinel doctest --mutate` (or call zentinel.doctest.mutation_experiment.mutateReportJson / stableMutationRun directly) over a doc whose ```zig test block is a passing test of a function like `fn pick(x: ?u32) u32 { return x orelse 7; }` with an assertion that the fallback is observable. stableMutationRun reaches candidatesOrParseError, gets `.ok = &.{}`, and emits a case with zero mutation entries (mutation_summary unchanged by any mutant) -- whereas `zentinel run` over the same source emits an optional_orelse_unreachable mutant.

**Suggested fix:** Add the 4 Phase-2 stable collectors to mutation_experiment.zig candidatesOrParseError (lines 440-443) to match run_command.zig:586-596. Better: extract the 8-collector invocation into one shared helper used by run_command, list_mutants_command, mutation_experiment, and mutator_doctest so a newly stabilized operator is wired in exactly one place and the doctest paths cannot silently diverge from the pipeline (this is the third+fourth divergent copy of the registry).

**Lens verdicts:** CORRECTNESS: UPHELD, Zig-semantics/safety: verified the empty-collector control flow, empty-slice dupe semantics, and the live error-union/opt-in caller chain.: UPHELD, REPRODUCTION: UPHELD

### [M8] AI-context normalizeAbsolutePaths misses scheme/colon-prefixed paths (file:// URIs) -> developer path leaks to provider

- **Severity:** Medium  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 2/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D6-safety
- **Location(s):** `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/ai/redaction.zig`, `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/ai/context.zig`

**Evidence:**
```zig
redaction.zig:36-38 isPathByte() classifies ':' as a path byte. normalizeAbsolutePaths (line 90-91) only triggers when `text[i]=='/' and at_boundary`, where `at_boundary = i==0 or !isPathByte(text[i-1])` (line 90). When a '/'-rooted path is immediately preceded by ':' (or any path byte), at_boundary is FALSE, so the path is never normalized to <path>. The redact() secondary pass only scrubs gh/aws/anthropic/jwt/pem VALUE shapes (line 245-317); a plain absolute path with no credential-shaped token survives verbatim. redactField (context.zig:208-215) runs normalizeAbsolutePaths then redact, so it inherits the gap and reaches the serialized context via buildContext->toJson with no second path pass.
```

**Tool confirmation:** Compiled the real src/ai/redaction.zig standalone (zig 0.16.0, `zig run --dep redaction -Mredaction=.../src/ai/redaction.zig`). Observed: input `see file:///Users/dev/secret/leak.zig` -> normalizeAbsolutePaths out=`see file:///Users/dev/secret/leak.zig` changed=false (UNCHANGED); `note:/Users/dev/secret/leak.zig more` -> unchanged changed=false; `@import:/Users/dev/secret/leak.zig` -> unchanged. Contrast: `in /Users/a/x.zig from /Users/b/y.zig` -> `in <path> from <path>` changed=true (boundary paths work).

**Why it is wrong:** docs/AI_CONTEXT_SCHEMA.md line 311 states the guarantee: an absolute multi-segment path 'is replaced by the <path> placeholder, so an absolute developer path ... never reaches a provider or the rendered output.' The implementation's boundary rule (preceded-by-non-path-byte) treats ':' as a path byte, so any path that follows a ':' — most concretely a file:// URI, which Zig/LLVM and build tooling commonly emit in diagnostics — is left verbatim. The report-sourced stderr/stdout excerpts and command `original`/`argv`/`cwd` strings are exactly where such tokens appear, and they are precisely the fields fed to the (possibly remote) provider.

**Impact & repro:** An absolute developer/home path (revealing username, project layout, machine structure) can be transmitted to an AI provider in `remote` mode despite the documented 'never reaches a provider' guarantee, and is echoed into the rendered advisory output. privacy.redactions_applied will not record `absolute_path` for these (changed=false), so the leak is also silent in the audit trail.  
_Repro:_ Build redaction.zig standalone and call normalizeAbsolutePaths(arena, "see file:///Users/dev/secret/leak.zig"). Result text is byte-identical to input, changed=false. Then redact() on the same text returns it unchanged (no credential shape). End-to-end: a mutation report whose result.evidence.stderr_excerpt contains a file:// URI flows through ai/command.zig redactAndCapLogged -> redactField -> normalizeAbsolutePaths and the path survives into the prompt context JSON.

**Suggested fix:** Treat a scheme/colon prefix as a token boundary for the '/'-rooted branch: when scanning a '/' at index i, allow the boundary when text[i-1]==':' (or more generally exclude ':' from the set of bytes that suppress a boundary). Equivalently, detect and normalize `scheme://path` and `label:/abs/path` forms. Add adversarial unit tests for file://, label:/abs, and alpha-glued absolute paths asserting the result is <path> and redactions_applied includes absolute_path.

**Lens verdicts:** CORRECTNESS: REFUTED, Zig-semantics/safety: UPHELD, REPRODUCTION: UPHELD

---
### [M9] AI-context mutant.id and operator fields bypass redaction (command.zig) -> untrusted-report paths/secrets leak verbatim

- **Severity:** Medium  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 2/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D6-safety
- **Location(s):** `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/ai/command.zig`, `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/ai/context.zig`, `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/ai/doctest_command.zig`

**Evidence:**
```zig
buildContext() in src/ai/command.zig routes file/original/replacement/diff/cwd/argv/skip_reason/version fields through context.redactField (lines 426-430, 445-447, 485, plus 316/318 in commandResultFromReport), but takes the report-sourced mutant id and operator VERBATIM:
  line 466: .id = s(get(mutant, "id")),
  line 470: .operator = s(get(mutant, "operator")),
  line 503: .name = s(get(mutant, "operator")),
The deterministic stub then echoes the raw id and operator into rendered output:
  line 657-658: refs[0] = .{ .kind = "mutant_diff", .ref = operator };
  line 662: .summary = ..."Mutant {s} in {s} ({s}) ...", .{ s(get(mutant, "id")), file, operator, ... }
The context struct (including the unredacted id/operator) is serialized whole into the prompt envelope sent to the provider: buildPromptValue → std.json.Stringify.valueAlloc (command.zig:529). context.validate (src/ai/context.zig:359-364) only existence-checks id and accepts operator via requireAll; it never constrains their format or content, so a value such as id="/Users/victim/.ssh/id_rsa ..." or operator="AKIA...secret..." passes validation unredacted. The same class of gap exists in the doctest engine: metaFromCase (doctest_command.zig:411-422) sets id=optStr(get(case,"id")) and redactedMeta (line 348-353) redacts only file and source_ref, not id. The reports are explicitly treated as untrusted: see command.zig:200 ("The report is untrusted (`--input-report`)") and doctest_command.zig:134. cli.zig reads the report raw (readFileAlloc at cli.zig:884/1152) with ONLY path-containment (F-5) on which file is read — there is NO report-schema validation of contents before fields are extracted. Because id/operator never pass through redactField, RedactionLog never records them, so privacy.redactions_applied (context.zig:199-201, command.zig:455) is silently INCOMPLETE for these fields while still presented as the authoritative privacy record.
```

**Tool confirmation:** zig_references on context.redactField (src/ai/context.zig:207) returned every call site (35 results). In the mutation context builder buildContext (command.zig 408-509) the redactField references are at lines 426,427,428,430,445,446,485 only — there is NO reference at line 466 (id) or 470/503 (operator), proving those fields are emitted without redaction. Grep of test/ and src/ai for any test asserting id/operator redaction returned zero matches (no coverage). zig_build/zig build test were clean (GT: exit 0), so this is a logic/completeness gap, not a compile issue.

**Why it is wrong:** The audit-F-4 hardening (documented at context.zig:204-207: redactField is "Used for the file, source, diff, and path fields that previously passed through verbatim") was meant to close verbatim AI-context field leaks under the explicit assumption that --input-report is untrusted. The id and operator fields were overlooked. Both are free-form JSON strings under full attacker control via a crafted report, and both reach (a) the prompt context that a remote provider can receive and (b) the advisory text rendered to stdout.

**Impact & repro:** A poisoned or third-party-supplied mutation report (or doctest report) can smuggle an absolute developer path or a secret-shaped value through the id/operator fields straight to the configured AI provider (including remote, when remote_allowed) and into the tool's stdout, completely bypassing the path-normalization and secret-value scrubbing applied to every other field. privacy.redactions_applied will not list these leaks, so the context misrepresents itself as fully redacted — defeating the privacy contract that the redaction subsystem exists to uphold.  
_Repro:_ Construct a self-consistent report.json with one mutant: {"run":{...},"baseline":{...},"summary":{...},"mutants":[{"id":"/Users/victim/.aws/credentials AKIAIOSFODNN7EXAMPLE","display_id":1,"operator":"sk-ant-api03-LEAKED","file":"src/x.zig","span":{...},"original":"a","replacement":"b","diff":[],"expected_compile":"compiles","result":{"status":"survived","mode":"Debug","commands":[{"command":{"original":"zig build test","argv":["zig","build","test"],"cwd":".","environment_policy":"minimal","shell":false},"phase":"mutant","status":"failed","exit_code":1,"timed_out":false,"failure_kind":"test_failure","evidence":{...},"skip_reason":null}],"evidence":{...},"skip_reason":null},"test_selection":{...}}]}. Run `zentinel explain 1 --input-report report.json --ai-provider stub`. resolveMutant (comm …[clipped]

**Suggested fix:** Treat id-class report fields like every other untrusted field: either (a) run mutant id, operator, and doctest case id through context.redactField (path-normalize + secret-scrub + log), matching file/original/replacement; or (b) hard-gate their format in context.validate / doctest validateContext (e.g. require mutant id to match m_[0-9a-f]+, operator to be in the known-operator set) so non-conforming content is rejected as an invalid report. Option (b) is preferable for id because ids should be opaque tokens; option (a) is the minimal change consistent with the existing F-4 approach. Mirror the fix in doctest_command.zig redactedMeta/metaFromCase.

**Lens verdicts:** CORRECTNESS: UPHELD, Zig-semantics/safety: slice lifetime/ownership of borrowed JSON string slices, verbatim-vs-redacted data flow, and absence of any comptime/runtime guard.: UPHELD, REPRODUCTION: REFUTED
