### [M10] report.summarize per-status arithmetic (compile_error/compiler_crash/timeout/skipped/invalid) is unpinned; validate() is blind to a score-inflating regression

- **Severity:** Medium  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 2/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D8-tests
- **Location(s):** `src/report.zig:223-235`, `src/report.zig:316-320`, `test/report_schema_test.zig:203-225`, `test/report_renderers_test.zig:241-255`, `test/report_renderers_test.zig:165-191`

**Evidence:**
```zig
src/report.zig:223-235 `summarize` is the sole producer of per-status counts: `.killed => s.killed += 1, .survived => s.survived += 1, .compile_error => s.compile_error += 1, .compiler_crash => s.compiler_crash += 1, .timeout => s.timeout += 1, .skipped => s.skipped += 1, .invalid => s.invalid += 1`. The only tests that pin summarize output to LITERAL expected counts are report_schema_test.zig:203-208 (`one_mutant` = a single .survived mutant -> total 1, survived 1, killed 0) and report_renderers_test.zig:241-249 (a {.killed, .survived} pair -> total 2, killed 1, survived 1). Neither builds a mutant with status .compile_error/.compiler_crash/.timeout/.skipped/.invalid and asserts the resulting count. The JUnit status-mapping test (report_renderers_test.zig:165-191) DOES construct single-mutant reports of each of those statuses, but asserts ONLY the rendered XML string (e.g. `<error type="zentinel.compile_error"` / `value="compile_error"`); it never inspects the `Summary` struct. report.validate (src/report.zig:319-320) checks summary correctness via `const derived = summarize(report.mutants); if (!std.meta.eql(report.summary, derived)) return .summary_count_mismatch;` -- it recomputes the expected summary with the SAME summarize function that production used to build report.summary, so any bug inside summarize is present identically on both sides of the eql and cannot be detected.
```

**Tool confirmation:** mcp__zigars__zig_test_for_symbol symbol=summarize returned coverage_status "no_direct_matches", candidate_tests [] (no test names/declarations reference summarize). Grep across test/ for `summary.compile_error|summary.compiler_crash|summary.timeout|summary.invalid|summary.skipped|derived.compile_error|derived.invalid|derived.timeout|derived.skipped|derived.compiler_crash` returned ZERO matches against report.Summary; the only `.invalid` count assertion found was test/doctest_mutate_stabilization_test.zig:69 `r.summary.mutation.invalid` which is the doctest report's separate summary type, not report.Summary. `zig build test` is green (GT) so the suite as written passes.

**Why it is wrong:** Mutation-testing tools live or die by the integrity of the kill/survive tally. The five non-kill terminal statuses (compile_error, compiler_crash, timeout, skipped, invalid) are exactly the buckets that must be kept OUT of the headline kill count -- I-010/F-016 explicitly exist to stop compile-errors being 'credited to the tests as killed'. Yet the count derivation that implements that separation has no test that would notice if an arm were rewired. validate() gives a false sense of safety because it is self-referential (derived from the same function), so reviewers assuming 'the validator checks the summary' are mistaken for the per-status breakdown.

**Impact & repro:** A one-line regression such as `.compile_error => s.killed += 1` (or the same for .invalid/.timeout) silently inflates the reported kill count and mutation score: compile-broken or unrunnable mutants get counted as caught by the test suite. report.validate still returns .ok (both sides recompute equally), every existing test still passes, and the JSON/JUnit output (src/report.zig:657-666) emits the wrong headline numbers. This is the precise mis-classification the project's own invariants (I-010, F-016, F-032) were built to prevent, but the summary-count layer has no regression guard for it.  
_Repro:_ 1) Read src/report.zig:223-235 (summarize) and 316-320 (validate uses summarize on both sides). 2) Confirm no literal count assertion exists for the five statuses: `grep -rn "summary.compile_error\|summary.invalid\|summary.timeout\|summary.skipped\|summary.compiler_crash\|derived.invalid\|derived.compile_error" test/` -> empty. 3) Mentally apply the mutation `.compile_error => s.killed += 1`: report_schema_test.zig:203 uses a survived mutant (arm untouched) -> passes; report_renderers_test.zig:241 uses killed+survived (arm untouched) -> passes; report_renderers_test.zig:173 builds a compile_error mutant but asserts only the XML string -> passes; validate() recomputes derived with the mutated summarize so std.meta.eql still holds -> .ok. CI stays green while a compile_error is counted as a  …[clipped]

**Suggested fix:** Add a unit test that builds a Mutant array spanning ALL seven ResultStatus values (one each, or a representative mix) and asserts every field of report.summarize(...) against literal expected counts -- especially `expectEqual(@as(u64,0), s.killed)` together with `expectEqual(@as(u64,1), s.compile_error)` etc., so a non-kill arm cannot be rewired into killed/survived without failing. This is independent of validate() (which cannot catch summarize bugs by construction). Optionally also assert the emitted JSON summary block (src/report.zig:657-666) for one such fixture.

**Lens verdicts:** CORRECTNESS: UPHELD, Zig-semantics/safety: REFUTED, REPRODUCTION: UPHELD

### [M11] JUnit XML renderer emits XML-illegal control characters (e.g. ANSI ESC), producing invalid XML

- **Severity:** Medium  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 2/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D11-cli
- **Location(s):** `src/report_junit.zig`, `src/runner.zig`

**Evidence:**
```zig
report_junit.zig:131-141: the `escape()` function replaces only the five XML special characters (`&`, `<`, `>`, `"`, `'`) and passes every other byte through verbatim with `else => try buf.append(arena, c)`. XML 1.0 forbids code points \x00-\x08, \x0b, \x0c, \x0e-\x1f (e.g. BEL \x07, BS \x08, ESC \x1b). Zig compiler output routinely contains ANSI escape sequences (\x1b[...m). runner.zig:96-100: `boundedExcerpt` calls `report.normalizeExcerpt` which only replaces hex addresses and absolute paths and does NOT strip control chars or ANSI codes; the raw bytes including \x1b are stored in `evidence.stdout_excerpt` / `evidence.stderr_excerpt`. These reach the JUnit renderer via `emitEvidence` at report_junit.zig:98-104 where `escape()` is called but does not filter them. Same path applies to baseline evidence (line 107-115) and per-command properties via `prop()` (line 126-128).
```

**Tool confirmation:** Build compiles with zero diagnostics (zig_build + zig_test exit 0). Source code read directly confirms the escape() implementation at report_junit.zig:131-141 and boundedExcerpt at runner.zig:96-100.

**Why it is wrong:** When `zentinel run --report junit` is used in CI, the XML emitted for any mutant whose test run produced ANSI-colored compiler output will contain bare \x1b characters. These are forbidden by XML 1.0. A strict XML parser (Jenkins, GitLab, GitHub Actions JUnit parsers) will reject the entire testsuite element, making the JUnit report silently useless.

**Impact & repro:** CI integration via `--report junit` silently produces malformed XML whenever Zig compiler output contains ANSI escape codes or other XML-prohibited control characters. The entire testsuite element is rejected by strict XML parsers, so all mutation results disappear from CI dashboards. Since `zig build test` emits colored output by default in many environments, this is a common case.  
_Repro:_ 1. Configure a project that produces colored terminal output (or any Zig error with an ANSI code). 2. Run `zentinel run --report junit`. 3. Inspect the emitted XML: it will contain literal \x1b characters. 4. Feed the XML to xmllint: it fails with 'invalid character' error.

**Suggested fix:** Extend `escape()` in `report_junit.zig` to replace XML-illegal control characters (\x00-\x08, \x0b, \x0c, \x0e-\x1f, \x7f) with a safe placeholder such as `?` or an XML character reference. Additionally strip ANSI CSI sequences (\x1b[...m) from evidence excerpts before they reach the JUnit renderer. The normalizer already has a correct ANSI stripper at normalizer.zig:63-70 (`matchAnsi`); the same logic can be extracted and applied to report excerpts in boundedExcerpt.

**Lens verdicts:** CORRECTNESS: REFUTED, Zig-semantics/safety: UPHELD, REPRODUCTION: UPHELD

### [M12] validate_pipeline_artifact_tree silently skips all committed verification/report.json artifacts

- **Severity:** Medium  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 2/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D12-build
- **Location(s):** `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/scripts/validate_task_system.py`, `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/artifacts/pipeline/059/verification/report.json`

**Evidence:**
```zig
validate_pipeline_artifact_tree (lines 1522-1579) iterates each task directory and opens only three subdirectories: handoffs/ (line 1531), locks/ (line 1555), and context/ (line 1569). It never opens verification/, escalation/, or stale_context/ subdirectories. Yet PIPELINE_SCHEMA_BY_VERSION (lines 1435-1442) registers zentinel.pipeline.verification.v1, zentinel.pipeline.stale_context.v1, and zentinel.pipeline.escalation.v1 schemas. The schema cache and registration exist but are never applied by the artifact-tree validator. Searching for 'verification_dir', 'escalation_dir', '"verification"' in validate_pipeline_artifact_tree returns zero matches.
```

**Tool confirmation:** Bash: find /Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/artifacts/pipeline -name '*.json' -not -path '*/handoffs/*' -not -path '*/locks/*' -not -path '*/context/*' -not -path '*/dogfood/*' | count = 48 verification/report.json files plus others. head -3 artifacts/pipeline/059/verification/report.json confirms schema_version: zentinel.pipeline.verification.v1. Bash grep for 'verification_dir' in validate_task_system.py returns zero matches.

**Why it is wrong:** 48 committed verification/report.json files that use the zentinel.pipeline.verification.v1 schema are committed to the repo but are never schema-validated by scripts/check_pipeline_artifacts.py (which delegates to validate_pipeline_artifact_tree). A malformed or schema-violating verification artifact can be committed and will pass CI stage 5 undetected. The self-test fixtures (ci_artifacts/valid and ci_artifacts/invalid) also only cover handoffs/, locks/, and context/, so the gap is invisible to the self-test.

**Impact & repro:** Any verification/report.json file with schema violations, missing required fields, or cross-artifact task_id mismatches passes CI undetected. Since every completed task produces a verification artifact and there are 48 such files, this represents a large unvalidated surface area for the pipeline integrity gate.  
_Repro:_ 1. Add a malformed verification artifact: echo '{"schema_version":"zentinel.pipeline.verification.v1","BAD":1}' > artifacts/pipeline/059/verification/report.json. 2. Run python3 scripts/check_pipeline_artifacts.py. 3. Observe: exit 0, no violation reported despite the required fields being absent.

**Suggested fix:** In validate_pipeline_artifact_tree, after the context_dir block (around line 1578), add a block that scans task_dir/verification/*.json files, loads each with _load_json_or_none, and applies subset_validate(data, _load_pipeline_schema('zentinel.pipeline.verification.v1'), ...). Also add a task_id cross-check (data.get('task_id') != task_id). Extend the ci_artifacts/invalid test fixtures with a verification-schema violation case so the self-test covers this path.

**Lens verdicts:** CORRECTNESS: UPHELD, ZIG-SEMANTICS/SAFETY: REFUTED, REPRODUCTION: UPHELD

### [L1] AI explain/suggest returns wrong error code (ZNTL_AI_REPORT_NOT_FOUND) for an existing report with an invalid empty-commands mutant

- **Severity:** Low  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 3/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D7-errorsets
- **Location(s):** `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/ai/command.zig`

**Evidence:**
```zig
resolveMutant (src/ai/command.zig:232-241) applies NO status filter, so an `invalid` mutant resolves like any other. run() (937-985) has no commands-presence guard between resolveMutant (948) and buildPromptValue (965). buildPromptValue -> buildContext (522, 415) -> commandsFromResult(arena, result, ...) at line 442. commandsFromResult (346-365): `if (arrOf(get(result,"commands"))) |items| { if (items.len > 0) {...} } return error.AiReportNotFound;`. For an invalid mutant the report serializes `"commands": []` (report.zig:124-162 always writes the slice; arrOf at src/ai/command.zig:218-224 returns a non-null empty slice), so items.len==0 falls through to line 364 `return error.AiReportNotFound`. run() maps that at 965-969 (`error.AiReportNotFound => return error.AiReportNotFound`). Invalid mutants with empty commands are emitted into real zentinel reports: mutant_runner.invalidResult sets `.commands = &.{}` (src/mutant_runner.zig:76-86); run_command builds an entry for every result unfiltered, incl. .invalid (src/run_command.zig:330-337, buildEntry copies result.commands at 670), and report.summarize counts .invalid (src/report.zig:223-235).
```

**Tool confirmation:** mcp__zigars__zig_error_sets on src/ai/command.zig enumerated the Failure-returning helpers and confirmed commandsFromResult (line 364) and requiredString/requiredBool/reportU32 all return error.AiReportNotFound. Bash grep of test/ai_commands_test.zig: the only AiReportNotFound tests are line 81-92 ("a missing report") and line 70 (token mapping); zero tests exercise explain/suggest on an invalid or empty-commands mutant (26 tests total). docs/ERROR_CODES.md:60 defines ZNTL_AI_REPORT_NOT_FOUND strictly as "AI command requires a deterministic report path that does not exist." docs/ERROR_CODES.md:61 shows the correct code for a non-resolving target is ZNTL_AI_TARGET_NOT_FOUND. Bash confirmed run_command.zig has no filter dropping .invalid results before report assembly (sed 296-303 shows only survivor reverification; the build loop at 330 is unfiltered).

**Why it is wrong:** commandsFromResult and commandResultFromReport conflate two distinct failure classes: "the report file/path does not exist" (the documented meaning of AiReportNotFound) and "the report exists, parses, and the target mutant resolves, but its result.commands array is empty/edge-shaped". An empty commands array is a LEGITIMATE, documented report state (every `invalid` mutant has one), not a missing report. The report is also explicitly untrusted (--input-report; the module's own comment at line 200-205 calls the report untrusted), so any parseable report with `"commands": []` on a resolved mutant hits the same path.

**Impact & repro:** `zentinel explain <ref>` / `zentinel suggest <ref>` targeting an invalid mutant (or any mutant with empty commands, including in an untrusted --input-report) reports `ZNTL_AI_REPORT_NOT_FOUND` ("report path does not exist") even though the report was read successfully and the mutant ref resolved. The operator is told the report is missing when it is present and the target was found, sending debugging in the wrong direction. AI is advisory-only and exit code is 2 either way, so there is no wrong mutant verdict or data corruption; the harm is a misleading diagnostic on a real, untested edge/malformed-input path.  
_Repro:_ 1. Produce or hand-write a zentinel.report.v1 JSON containing a mutant whose result.status is "invalid" and result.commands is [] (this is exactly what mutant_runner.invalidResult yields on a sandbox span/original failure, and what run_command writes into the report). 2. Run `zentinel explain <that-mutant-display-id-or-m_id> --input-report <report.json>`. 3. Observed: error[ZNTL_AI_REPORT_NOT_FOUND], exit 2. Expected: either a successful advisory explanation, or at minimum an accurate code (the report was found and the target resolved) — e.g. AiTargetNotFound/an invalid-report code, not "report not found". Trace: src/ai/command.zig:948 resolves -> 950 stub ok -> 965 buildPromptValue -> 442 commandsFromResult -> 364 returns AiReportNotFound -> 969 returns AiReportNotFound.

**Suggested fix:** Distinguish "report not found/unreadable" from "report content is malformed/edge-shaped". (a) Stop using error.AiReportNotFound for content-shape failures inside commandsFromResult / commandResultFromReport / requiredString / requiredBool / reportU32; route those to a distinct invalid-report failure (mapped to ZNTL_AI_RESPONSE_INVALID or a new ZNTL_AI_REPORT_INVALID code), reserving AiReportNotFound for the genuine missing/unparseable cases at lines 940-942. (b) Better for the advisory UX: allow an empty commands array for non-running statuses — when result.commands is empty (e.g. status invalid/skipped), build the context with `commands = &.{}` instead of failing, so explain/suggest can still describe why the mutant did not run. Add a test in test/ai_commands_test.zig covering explain/suggest on an invalid (empty-commands) mutant to lock the chosen behavior.

**Lens verdicts:** correctness: UPHELD, Zig-semantics/safety: error-union propagation, slice/JSON-array semantics, Debug-vs-ReleaseFast behavior, presence of guards.: UPHELD, REPRODUCTION: UPHELD

### [L2] Integration dangling-original regression guard is inert (ArenaAllocator never frees/poisons source, so the bug cannot manifest)

- **Severity:** Low  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 3/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D8-tests
- **Location(s):** `test/integration_run_test.zig:41-115`, `src/main.zig:7`, `src/cli.zig:515`, `src/run_command.zig:579-597`, `src/ast_backend.zig:123-143`

**Evidence:**
```zig
test/integration_run_test.zig:88-99 spawns the BUILT zentinel binary and asserts summary.invalid==0 (and lines 110-111 assert the error_catch_unreachable mutant is survived with original=="0"). The comment at lines 91-95 states this guards the dangling-original bug because 'on a Debug build the freed bytes poisoned to 0xAA'. But the real binary's allocator is an ArenaAllocator: src/main.zig:7 `const arena = init.arena.allocator();` (std.process.Init.arena is `*std.heap.ArenaAllocator`, confirmed process.zig:35), threaded via cli.run -> runRun -> src/cli.zig:515 `run_command.run(gpa, ...)` -> src/run_command.zig:582 `parse(arena, ...)` then :583 `defer parsed.deinit()`. generateCandidates allocates owned_source then makes many further arena allocations (testDeclRanges + 8 collect() calls) BEFORE deinit, so owned_source is never the most-recent allocation.
```

**Tool confirmation:** Read of std lib ArenaAllocator.free (/opt/homebrew/Cellar/zig/0.16.0_1/lib/zig/std/heap/ArenaAllocator.zig:608-636): if the freed slice is not the most-recent allocation it `return`s doing nothing (lines 620-623); even for the last allocation it only rewinds end_index via cmpxchg and NEVER writes 0xAA poison bytes. grep confirmed process.zig:35 `arena: *std.heap.ArenaAllocator`. grep confirmed src/cli.zig:515 passes `gpa` (which is main's arena) directly to run_command.run, not a fresh sub-arena. zig_test_for_symbol(classifyCommand) + Read confirm the compile/kill classification is independently and well covered, so this finding is about the dangling-original guard specifically.

**Why it is wrong:** The audit memo flags dangling-original as the critical Phase-2 defect, and integration_run_test.zig is presented (in its own comments) as the end-to-end regression guard. But the guard is inert: under an ArenaAllocator, `parsed.deinit()` frees nothing and poisons nothing, so Mutant.original keeps pointing at valid, unchanged bytes regardless of whether the src/ast_backend.zig:141 dup fix is present. The test would pass identically if the dup were reverted. The only test that actually creates the freeing/poisoning condition is sandbox_test.zig:136 (F-1), which deliberately uses std.testing.allocator (a GPA), a regime production does not use. So the headline end-to-end protection for the framework's most dangerous bug class is a false positive.

**Impact & repro:** A regression that reverts the Collector.add() dup (src/ast_backend.zig:141) would NOT be caught by the real-binary integration test. Detection relies entirely on the single sandbox_test.zig F-1 unit test, which (a) exercises only 3 of ~9 source-slice operators (error_catch_unreachable, boolean_literal, integer_literal_boundary) and (b) tests under a non-production allocator. Operators that borrow tree slices but are not in F-1 (arithmetic, comparison, logical, optional, loop_boundary, errdefer) have no teardown-survival guard at all. If the binary's allocator is ever changed from arena to a GPA/DebugAllocator, the dangling-original bug would silently reappear for those operators with zero failing test.  
_Repro:_ 1) Read src/main.zig:7 -> arena allocator. 2) Read /opt/homebrew/Cellar/zig/0.16.0_1/lib/zig/std/heap/ArenaAllocator.zig:608-636 -> free is a no-op rewind, no poisoning. 3) Conceptually revert src/ast_backend.zig:141 (drop `owned.original = try self.allocator.dupe(...)`, append `candidate` directly). 4) `zig build test` -> integration_run_test.zig 'invalid==0' still passes because the arena keeps owned_source valid; only sandbox_test.zig F-1 (GPA-backed) fails. This proves the integration assertion is not what catches the bug.

**Suggested fix:** Make the regression guard match production reality OR make production match the test. Either: (a) document that the dup is defense-in-depth and that production's arena already prevents the UAF (downgrading the integration comment's poisoning claim, which is factually wrong for an arena); or (b) add a unit/integration test that drives generateCandidates (or run_command.run) with a poisoning GeneralPurposeAllocator/DebugAllocator and asserts invalid==0 across ALL stable source-slice operators, so a revert of src/ast_backend.zig:141 fails. Option (b) is the real fix because it also future-proofs against an allocator change. At minimum, correct the misleading 'freed bytes poisoned to 0xAA' comment in test/integration_run_test.zig:94 since the spawned binary uses an arena.

**Lens verdicts:** CORRECTNESS: UPHELD, ZIG-SEMANTICS/SAFETY: verified ArenaAllocator free/poison behavior, allocator scope threading (arena vs GPA), slice/pointer lifetime of borrowed tree.source into owned_source across parsed.deinit, and the dup owner-conversion semantics.: UPHELD, REPRODUCTION: UPHELD

- **Severity:** Low  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 3/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D8-tests
- **Location(s):** `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/property/report.zig`, `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/test/property_generator_test.zig`, `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/test/fixtures/pipeline/property_tests/valid/not_property_required_skip.json`

**Evidence:**
```zig
All 8 invalid fixtures carry a VALID schema_version, scope (`property_required`), task_class, and status (confirmed by reading bad_invariant_category.json, missing_seed.json, status_mismatch.json, missing_shrinking_status.json — each has `"schema_version": "zentinel.pipeline.property_report.v1"`, valid scope/task_class/status). Therefore report.zig branches bad_schema_version (L83-84), bad_scope (L88-89), bad_task_class (L91-92), top-level missing_field for task_id/deterministic/properties (L86,94-98,104-108), bad_status (L100-102) and bad_result (L156-158) are reached by NO test. The `missing_skip_reason` branch (L113-114) requires scope=not_property_required WITH absent/empty skip_reason; the only fixture with that scope is the VALID not_property_required_skip.json (has a full skip_reason) — Bash loop over invalid/*.json found zero fixtures containing `not_property_required`, so both the null-reason and empty-reason sub-branches are unexercised.
```

**Tool confirmation:** Bash `grep -on 'return \.[a-z_]*;' src/property/report.zig` listed all returnable tags; cross-referenced against the `grep -rohn 'Violation\.[a-z_]*' test/` aggregate (only ok/failed_without_counterexample/status_mismatch/empty_property_required pinned for prep.Violation). This directly undermines 'distinguishes passing property evidence from missing or malformed evidence' (report.zig:6-7).  
_Repro:_ Inspect the 8 files in test/fixtures/pipeline/property_tests/invalid/ — every one has valid schema_version/scope/task_class/status, so none drives report.zig L83-102 or L156-158; not_property_required appears only in the valid fixture, so L113-114 is never the verdict.

**Lens verdicts:** CORRECTNESS: UPHELD, Zig-semantics/safety: UPHELD, REPRODUCTION: UPHELD

### [L4] commandSpecsForConfigured re-parses configured commands once per surviving mutant instead of once per run

- **Severity:** Low  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 3/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D10-perf
- **Location(s):** `src/run_command.zig`

**Evidence:**
```zig
Phase B.5 loop at lines 297–303: `commandSpecsForConfigured(arena, cfg.test_commands)` is called at line 300 inside `for (jobs, 0..) |job, ji| { if (results[ji].status != .survived) continue; if (!test_selection.needsConfiguredReverification(...)) continue; const reverify_specs = try commandSpecsForConfigured(arena, cfg.test_commands); ... }`. The function re-parses every configured command string via `command.parse` and allocates a new `[]command.Spec` slice on every iteration. Its only argument is `cfg.test_commands`, which is constant across the entire loop.
```

**Tool confirmation:** ZLS references confirm `commandSpecsForConfigured` (declared at run_command.zig:477, 0-based line 476) has exactly two reference locations: its declaration and the single call at run_command.zig:300 (0-based line 299). No other callers exist in the codebase. The function body (lines 477–490) parses each configured command via `command.parse` and heap-allocates a `Spec` per command on every call.

**Why it is wrong:** `cfg.test_commands` is a constant slice for the lifetime of the run function. Every surviving mutant that needs reverification causes a redundant full re-parse and re-allocation of the same configured-command argv structures. With S survivors the work is O(S * C) parses and allocations where C is the number of configured commands; with reverification in hand, S can be up to M mutants. The result is identical every iteration.

**Impact & repro:** CPU and allocator pressure proportional to the number of survivors that reach reverification. Each call allocates a new `[]command.Spec` slice plus per-command `[][]const u8` argv slices. In a project with many survivors (e.g. a weak test suite) and several configured test commands, this wasteful parsing occurs for every survivor.  
_Repro:_ Run `zentinel run` on any project with multiple configured commands and a high survivor count. Instrument `commandSpecsForConfigured` to count calls — it will be called once per surviving mutant that requires reverification, not once per run.

**Suggested fix:** Hoist the call before the Phase B.5 loop, computing `reverify_specs` once and reusing the slice for every surviving mutant: `const reverify_specs = try commandSpecsForConfigured(arena, cfg.test_commands);` at run_command.zig line ~297 before the `for` loop begins. The slice is read-only so sharing across iterations is safe.

**Lens verdicts:** CORRECTNESS: UPHELD, ZIG-SEMANTICS/SAFETY: UPHELD, REPRODUCTION: UPHELD

---
### [L5] commandSpecsForSelection called O(M) times per file instead of O(1)

- **Severity:** Low  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 3/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D10-perf
- **Location(s):** `src/run_command.zig`

**Evidence:**
```zig
Phase A loop (lines 267–273): for each `candidate` in `candidates`, line 271 calls `commandSpecsForSelection(arena, resolution.commands, candidate.file)`. The function signature (line 492) takes only `commands` and `file`. `resolution.commands` derives solely from per-file data (`fsel.same_file_tests`, `fsel.preflight`, `fsel.generated_in_baseline`, `cfg.test_commands`, `strategy`, `candidate.file`) — none of which vary across mutants from the same source file. `selectionForFile` has its own deduplication cache (`file_cache`, line 265, checked at line 526), but no equivalent cache exists for the `commandSpecsForSelection` result. For a file with K mutants, the function is called K times and produces an identical `[]command.Spec` on every call.
```

**Tool confirmation:** ZLS references for `commandSpecsForSelection` (declared at run_command.zig line 493, 0-based 492): declaration at 0-based line 491 and single call site at 0-based line 270 (source line 271) inside the per-mutant `for (candidates)` loop. `test_selection.resolve()` is also called at the same line 270 per mutant, producing `resolution.commands` that is purely per-file. `commandSpecsForSelection` body (lines 492–508) calls `test_selection.generatedCommand` and `test_selection.generatedCommandArgv` (both allocating) and `command.parse` per configured command — all of which are stable for a given file.

**Why it is wrong:** The cost of `commandSpecsForSelection` is O(C) allocations plus O(path) string formatting per call, where C is the number of configured test commands. For a typical project with many mutants per file (e.g. 10–100 arithmetic/comparison mutations in a single source file), this work is done K times for a K-mutant file when once would suffice. The result is structurally immutable (arena-owned slices of constant argv data).

**Impact & repro:** Wasted heap allocations and `command.parse` calls proportional to (mutants_per_file - 1) * configured_commands. For a heavily mutated file with 8 operators each producing 5+ mutants and 2 configured test commands, ~70+ redundant parse+alloc cycles occur during Phase A setup.  
_Repro:_ Instrument `commandSpecsForSelection` to count calls vs unique `file` arguments across a run on a project with multiple source files, each having multiple mutants. Call count will exceed unique-file count whenever any file has more than one mutant.

**Suggested fix:** Extend the existing `FileSelection` cache (or add a parallel `file_specs_cache`) to also memoize the `commandSpecsForSelection` result keyed by `candidate.file`. Since `resolution.commands` is already cached via `selectionForFile`, the spec can be computed once per unique file and reused for all mutants from that file: after retrieving `fsel` and computing `resolution`, check a `specs_cache` map keyed by `candidate.file` before calling `commandSpecsForSelection`.

**Lens verdicts:** CORRECTNESS: UPHELD, Zig-semantics/safety: UPHELD, REPRODUCTION: UPHELD

---
### [L6] error-path/optional skip-guards use exact byte-string equality, emitting no-op mutants on non-canonical formatting

- **Severity:** Low  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 3/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D1-mutators
- **Location(s):** `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/mutators/error_path.zig:99-101`, `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/mutators/error_path.zig:62-63`, `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/mutators/optional.zig:62-64`, `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/mutant.zig:100-107`

**Evidence:**
```zig
All three Phase-2 stable operators build `original = tree.source[start..end]` (verbatim source bytes spanning the handler/cleanup expression) and then guard against re-emitting an already-mutated form with an EXACT byte-string comparison:
- error_path.zig:100-101 `const replacement = "errdefer {}"; if (std.mem.eql(u8, original, replacement)) return;`
- error_path.zig:63 `if (std.mem.eql(u8, original, "unreachable")) return;`
- optional.zig:64 `if (std.mem.eql(u8, original, "unreachable")) return;`
Because the comparison is against ONE canonical spelling, a semantically-identical but differently-spaced source slips past the guard. Concrete case for errdefer_remove: source `errdefer  {}` (two spaces) yields `original = "errdefer  {}"` (12 bytes) and `replacement = "errdefer {}"` (11 bytes). They differ, so `mutant.zig:105` (`std.mem.eql(original, replacement)` -> false) and `hasValidEditShape` (mutant.zig:100-107) PASS and the candidate is emitted. Applying it (sandbox.zig:32-41) rewrites `errdefer  {}` -> `errdefer {}`: a pure-whitespace edit. Zig treats the two spellings as the identical program, so no test can ever distinguish them -> the mutant is a guaranteed SURVIVOR that represents no real test gap, inflating the surviving-mutant count and depressing the mutation score. The same class applies to a parenthesized handler: `x orelse (unreachable)` -> original `"(unreachable)"` != `"unreachable"`, so optional.zig emits `(unreachable)` -> `unreachable` (semantically identical), and `expr catch (unreachable)` likewise for error_path.zig.
```

**Tool confirmation:** mcp__zigars__zig_snippet_check on a 3-line fn containing both `errdefer {}` and `errdefer  {}` returned parse_status "ok", ok=true, parse_error_count=0 (evidence_basis: std.zig.Ast syntax parse) -- confirming both the canonical and the double-space spelling parse, so the double-space form reaches the .@"errdefer" node and the verbatim `tree.source[start..end]` reconstruction includes the extra space, defeating the exact-string guard. A separate snippet `errdefer{ acc = 1; }` also parsed ok=true, confirming the operator sees non-canonically-spaced errdefer bodies.

**Why it is wrong:** The skip-guards exist precisely to avoid emitting a no-op when the source already equals the post-mutation text, but they compare against a single hard-coded spelling instead of normalizing whitespace (or comparing the post-apply result to the source). Any source that is already semantically `errdefer {}` / `orelse unreachable` / `catch unreachable` but spelled with different interior whitespace or redundant parentheses bypasses the guard and produces an equivalent mutant. The dimension explicitly asks for operators that produce no-op mutants; this is one, confirmed by guard logic plus the parser.

**Impact & repro:** Guaranteed-equivalent mutants that always survive, polluting the surviving-mutant set and lowering the reported mutation score with a non-actionable survivor. No crash, no miscompile, no hidden real survivor. Only manifests on non-canonically-formatted source (zig fmt normalizes `errdefer  {}`->`errdefer {}` and strips the redundant parens), and only when the Phase-2 operators are enabled (default config is `phase1` only, per config.zig:358, so these operators are off by default). Hence Low.  
_Repro:_ 1) Create a .zig file with `fn f() void { errdefer  {} }` (two spaces after errdefer). 2) Run mutation with errdefer_remove enabled (config `[mutators] enabled = ["phase2"]` or `["all_stable"]`, or `--operator errdefer_remove`). 3) The candidate set includes an errdefer_remove mutant whose original is `errdefer  {}` and replacement `errdefer {}`; sandbox.apply succeeds and the mutant is reported as survived for every test suite. Equivalent recipe with `x orelse (unreachable)` for optional_orelse_unreachable and `expr catch (unreachable)` for error_catch_unreachable.

**Suggested fix:** Make the already-mutated guard whitespace/format-insensitive instead of exact-string: normalize the captured `original` (collapse runs of whitespace, strip redundant outer parens) before the `std.mem.eql` check, OR compute the post-apply text and skip when it equals the source slice modulo whitespace. Simplest robust option: after building `original`, strip surrounding parens and compare a whitespace-collapsed copy against the canonical `"unreachable"` / `"errdefer {}"` target. This is a guard-only change in error_path.zig (lines 63, 100-101) and optional.zig (line 64); no span/identity change.

**Lens verdicts:** correctness: UPHELD, zig-semantics-safety: UPHELD, reproduction: UPHELD

---
### [L7] Per-mutant workspace walker descends into excluded .git/.zig-cache/zig-out dirs (copyExcluded prunes files, not traversal)

- **Severity:** Low  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 3/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D2-applyrevert
- **Location(s):** `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/cli.zig:228-256`

**Evidence:**
```zig
copyExcluded (src/cli.zig:228) returns true for paths starting with '.zig-cache', 'zig-out', or '.git', and setupWorkspace (src/cli.zig:251-255) applies it as `if (copyExcluded(entry.path)) continue;` to skip COPYING those files. But the walker used (rt.root_dir.walk -> std.Io.Dir.Walker, Dir.zig:365-372) always descends into every subdirectory (it calls enter() for any directory entry before the caller ever inspects entry.path), so the entire .git, .zig-cache, and zig-out trees are still stat'd/iterated/openDir'd on EVERY mutant's setupWorkspace. There is no skip-subtree hook on Walker; only walkSelectively + caller-driven enter() can prune. The `.zig-cache/zentinel/workspaces/<run_id>/` tree grows with each concurrent mutant, so the descent cost grows during the run.
```

**Tool confirmation:** Read of /opt/homebrew/Cellar/zig/0.16.0_1/lib/zig/std/Io/Dir.zig:237-296,365-372 (via Bash sed) confirms Walker.next unconditionally enter()s directories and that walkSelectively is the only API exposing per-directory descent control. zig_std_signature Dir.walk doc-comment names walkSelectively as the selective alternative.

**Why it is wrong:** The comment and code intent is to exclude caches/VCS from the workspace, but excluding them from the file copy is not the same as excluding them from traversal. For a real repository, .git and .zig-cache are typically the largest subtrees, so each of N mutants pays a full recursive traversal of them. This is a clear inefficiency in the apply path and, more importantly, is the mechanism that makes finding #1 possible (descending into the actively-mutating .zig-cache/zentinel/workspaces tree).

**Impact & repro:** Wasted filesystem I/O on every per-mutant workspace creation, proportional to the size of .git/.zig-cache/zig-out (often dominant), multiplied by the mutant count. On its own this is a performance/robustness nit; combined with finding #1 it materially widens the race window. It does not by itself corrupt results in serial mode.  
_Repro:_ Run `zentinel run` on a project with a large .git or warm .zig-cache and observe (e.g. via fs tracing or wall-time scaling) that workspace setup time scales with cache/VCS size rather than only with the copied source set. Confirm by code inspection that copyExcluded gates copyFile but not walker descent.

**Suggested fix:** Switch setupWorkspace to std.Io.Dir.walkSelectively and skip `enter()` for any directory whose relative path matches copyExcluded (.zig-cache, zig-out, .git), pruning those subtrees from traversal entirely. This removes redundant I/O and eliminates descent into the run's own workspace cache (closing the race surface of finding #1).

**Lens verdicts:** correctness: UPHELD, zig-semantics-safety: UPHELD, reproduction: UPHELD

---
### [L8] Per-run workspace base directory ({run_id}/workspaces) is never deleted -> stale dir leaked every run

- **Severity:** Low  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 3/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D2-applyrevert
- **Location(s):** `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/cli.zig`, `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/worker_pool.zig`

**Evidence:**
```zig
setupWorkspace (src/cli.zig:243-245) computes rel = worker_pool.workspaceRoot(run_id, m.id) = ".zig-cache/zentinel/workspaces/{run_id}/{m.id}" (worker_pool.zig:88-90) and calls rt.root_dir.createDirPath(rt.io, rel) which (per std.Io.Dir.createDirPath docs: "Creates parent directories ... as necessary") creates ALL parents: .zig-cache/zentinel/workspaces/{run_id}/{m.id}. The only cleanup is the per-mutant leaf: mutantRunSpecsFn defer at src/cli.zig:299-304 does rt.root_dir.deleteTree(rt.io, ws.rel) for the {m.id} leaf only. A repo-wide grep for deleteTree/removeTree over the whole run path (cli.zig) shows exactly one deleteTree call (line 301, the per-mutant leaf); there is NO cleanup of the {run_id} parent or the workspaces/ base anywhere. So after a fully successful run the empty {run_id} directory and the workspaces/ tree persist, and accumulate one stale dir per run (run_id = "run_{x}" with x = wall-clock ms, cli.zig:313, so every invocation makes a new one).
```

**Tool confirmation:** zig_std_item createDirPath -> std/Io/Dir.zig:843 doc: "Creates parent directories with default permissions as necessary to ensure `sub_path` exists as a directory." confirming the {run_id} parent is materialized. grep over src/cli.zig: only deleteTree call is line 301 (ws.rel, the per-mutant leaf); run_id constructed at cli.zig:313. zig_references on RunCtx.cleanup_failures shows it is only touched at decl (163), the per-mutant deleteTree failure (302), init (510), and the warning emit (543) -- nothing deletes the base.

**Why it is wrong:** The cleanup design removes only the content-addressed per-mutant leaf workspace, not the per-run container it created via recursive createDirPath. No higher scope owns the {run_id}/workspaces lifetime.

**Impact & repro:** Unbounded accumulation of empty/stale directories under the project's .zig-cache/zentinel/workspaces/ across repeated runs. It is confined to the controlled Zig cache namespace (.zig-cache/zentinel/workspaces, cli.zig:338) and never touches the developer working tree, so I-007 is NOT violated and mutant classification is unaffected. Practical effect is disk/inode hygiene plus a slowly growing tree the per-mutant copy walker must still skip (copyExcluded prunes .zig-cache files but the walker still descends, compounding an already-reported descent cost).  
_Repro:_ Run `zentinel run` N times in a checkout, then inspect .zig-cache/zentinel/workspaces/ -- you will find N `run_<hex>` directories that were never removed (each empty on success, or containing orphaned per-mutant subtrees if any deleteTree failed). No `zentinel`-level command prunes them.

**Suggested fix:** After run_command.run returns (around cli.zig:541-543), best-effort delete the per-run base: rt.root_dir.deleteTree(rt.io, ".zig-cache/zentinel/workspaces/<run_id>") wrapped like the existing cleanup (increment cleanup_failures / warn on failure). Alternatively register the base-dir deleteTree with a defer in runRun right after the RunCtx/run_id is established so it is removed regardless of which branch returns.

**Lens verdicts:** correctness: UPHELD, zig-semantics-safety: UPHELD, reproduction: UPHELD

### [L9] Partial per-mutant workspace orphaned (and cleanup_failures undercounted) when setupWorkspace fails after createDirPath

- **Severity:** Low  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 3/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D2-applyrevert
- **Location(s):** `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/cli.zig`

**Evidence:**
```zig
In setupWorkspace (src/cli.zig:240-260): line 245 createDirPath(rel) materializes the {m.id} directory on disk; line 246 opens it with `errdefer dir.close(rt.io)` -- the errdefer ONLY closes the fd, it does not deleteTree(rel). If any subsequent step errors -- copyFile at line 255 (e.g. ENOSPC, EACCES, or a sibling worker's concurrent deleteTree under the shared rt.root_dir), pathEscapesRoot at 254/257 returning error.WorkspaceCreateFailed, or writeFile at 258 -- setupWorkspace returns an error with the on-disk {m.id} directory left partially populated. In the caller mutantRunSpecsFn (cli.zig:296-298) the failure is handled by `const ws = setupWorkspace(...) catch { return ...runSpecs(... .create_failed ...) }`, and the cleanup `defer { ws.dir.close; deleteTree(ws.rel); cleanup_failures.fetchAdd }` at lines 299-304 is registered ONLY AFTER setupWorkspace succeeds. On the failure path that defer is never registered, so the partial directory is never deleted and cleanup_failures is never incremented.
```

**Tool confirmation:** Read of src/cli.zig:240-308 (exact control flow): errdefer at line 247 is `dir.close(rt.io)` only; the deleteTree+cleanup_failures defer is at lines 299-304, lexically after the `setupWorkspace catch` at 296. grep confirms cleanup_failures.fetchAdd appears only at cli.zig:302 (the success-path deleteTree failure), so the setup-failure leak is invisible to emitCleanupWarningIfNeeded (cli.zig:543).

**Why it is wrong:** Cleanup ownership is split: setupWorkspace creates the directory but delegates its teardown to the caller's defer, which is only armed on success. The intermediate errdefer was written to release the fd, not to unwind the on-disk mkdir.

**Impact & repro:** Leftover partially-copied per-mutant workspace directories under .zig-cache/zentinel/workspaces/{run_id}/{m.id} after any setupWorkspace failure, and the user-facing cleanup warning (emitCleanupWarningIfNeeded, cli.zig:543) undercounts because cleanup_failures is not bumped on this path. Confined to the controlled cache (does not touch the dev tree; I-007 intact) and the affected mutant is still correctly classified .invalid via the .create_failed branch, so classification is sound. Overlaps in spirit with a prior pass finding about leaking a tree copy on a copyExcluded-driven writeFile failure; the distinct additions here are (a) the leak occurs for ANY setupWorkspace error, not just the copyExcluded mismatch, and (b) it bypasses the cleanup_failures counter so it is silent.  
_Repro:_ Force a copyFile/writeFile failure inside setupWorkspace (e.g. fill the device or make the workspace path read-only between createDirPath and copyFile) and run `zentinel run`; observe a residual .zig-cache/zentinel/workspaces/{run_id}/{m.id} directory and NO cleanup warning despite the orphan.

**Suggested fix:** In setupWorkspace, change the errdefer to also remove the created directory, e.g. `errdefer { dir.close(rt.io); rt.root_dir.deleteTree(rt.io, rel) catch {}; }` (or split into two errdefers ordered so the dir is closed then deleted). Optionally have that errdefer bump rt.cleanup_failures on deleteTree failure so the warning stays truthful.

**Lens verdicts:** correctness: UPHELD, zig-semantics-safety: UPHELD, reproduction: UPHELD

### [L10] Documented per-worker cache/output isolation unenforced: worker_pool.cacheDirIn/outDirIn are dead code

- **Severity:** Low  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 3/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D5-concurrency
- **Location(s):** `src/worker_pool.zig`, `src/cli.zig`, `src/runner.zig`

**Evidence:**
```zig
worker_pool.zig:9-12 and 92-102 document that per-unit workspace paths give each worker an isolated local `.zig-cache` and `zig-out` so 'concurrent workers never share a writable workspace, local .zig-cache, or zig-out directory', and provide pub fns `cacheDirIn` (line 94: returns `{root}/.zig-cache`) and `outDirIn` (line 100: returns `{root}/zig-out`) as the mechanism. But the production runner never uses them. setupWorkspace (cli.zig:240-260) only copies the project tree and overwrites the mutated file; execProcess (cli.zig:169-181) spawns the command with `cwd = ws.dir` and `environ_map = rt.env` and passes NO `--cache-dir`/`--prefix`. minimalEnviron (runner.zig:30-39) with env_allowlist (runner.zig:21) unconditionally forwards the host's `ZIG_LOCAL_CACHE_DIR` (and `ZIG_GLOBAL_CACHE_DIR`) into the minimal env of every spawned `zig build test` (default test command, config.zig:362). So actual isolation comes only from Zig's cwd-relative defaults; if the host has `ZIG_LOCAL_CACHE_DIR=<abs path>`, all parallel workers (worker_pool.run -> runOneMutant, run_command.zig:285/118-123) share that one local cache dir, contradicting docs/PERFORMANCE_STRATEGY.md:77 and docs/SANDBOX_SECURITY.md:80 ('No two workers may write the same local cache, output, or temporary build artifact path. This includes .zig-cache/, zig-out/').
```

**Tool confirmation:** mcp__zigars__zig_references on src/worker_pool.zig cacheDirIn (line 93, char 7) returned exactly ONE location -- the declaration itself (line 93:7-93:17), i.e. zero src/ call sites. Repo grep: `cacheDirIn`/`outDirIn` appear only in src/worker_pool.zig (decls) and test/worker_pool_test.zig + test/performance_benchmark_test.zig; grep for `cache-dir|--prefix|ZIG_LOCAL_CACHE_DIR|ZIG_GLOBAL_CACHE_DIR` in src/ returns ONLY runner.zig:21 (the passthrough allowlist) -- no override anywhere. Zig 0.16 source confirms the boundary: std/Build.zig:733 defaults the install prefix to build-root/zig-out (so zig-out stays cwd-isolated even with ZIG_LOCAL_CACHE_DIR set; only the local cache is redirected). mcp__zigars__zig_diagnostics on worker_pool.zig and run_command.zig: both null (clean). mcp__zigars__zig_unsafe_operations_audit on worker_pool.zig: only the documented *anyopaque Task-callback boundary (3 medium advisory sites), no real defect.

**Why it is wrong:** The module advertises a concrete isolation mechanism (content-addressed per-worker cache/out dirs via cacheDirIn/outDirIn) and a hard cross-worker no-shared-write contract, but the mechanism is never invoked. Isolation is incidental (Zig's cwd-relative `.zig-cache`/`zig-out`), and one inherited environment variable (ZIG_LOCAL_CACHE_DIR, itself explicitly allowlisted in SANDBOX_SECURITY.md:117) silently routes all parallel workers' local Zig caches to a single shared directory -- a direct internal conflict between two documented requirements that the code does not reconcile.

**Impact & repro:** Behavioral correctness impact is LOW and not substantiated: zig-out is cwd-isolated regardless (Build.zig:733), and Zig's local build cache is content-addressed and manifest-file-locked, which PERFORMANCE_STRATEGY.md:77 itself permits sharing for ('content-addressed compiler cache entries that cannot be corrupted by concurrent writes'). So no wrong-verdict (killed/survived/compile_error) could be demonstrated. The real defects are: (1) dead code -- the isolation helpers are maintained and unit-tested but never wired into the runner; (2) an unenforced documented isolation contract whose guarantee actually depends on the absence of a host env var that the runner is simultaneously mandated to forward.  
_Repro:_ Static: ZLS reference search on src/worker_pool.zig cacheDirIn returns only its declaration (no src/ callers); grep shows cli.zig passes no --cache-dir/--prefix and runner.zig forwards ZIG_LOCAL_CACHE_DIR via the allowlist. Dynamic (not run here -- no e2e parallel real-IO test exists per ground truth): set ZIG_LOCAL_CACHE_DIR=/tmp/shared-zig-cache, run `zentinel run --jobs 8` on a project whose default test command is `zig build test`; every worker's local cache resolves to /tmp/shared-zig-cache instead of its per-workspace .zig-cache, demonstrating the isolation helpers are not in effect.

**Suggested fix:** Either (a) wire the existing helpers into the spawn path so isolation is enforced independent of host env -- pass `--cache-dir <ws>/.zig-cache` and `--prefix <ws>/zig-out` (and/or set ZIG_LOCAL_CACHE_DIR=<ws>/.zig-cache in the per-command minimal env) when spawning each worker's command in execProcess/mutantRunSpecsFn; or (b) delete cacheDirIn/outDirIn and rewrite the worker_pool.zig:9-12/92-102 doc-comment and docs to state that per-worker isolation is provided by the per-mutant cwd, and explicitly document that a host-set ZIG_LOCAL_CACHE_DIR collapses local caches to a shared (content-addressed, lock-safe) directory. Option (a) is the stronger fix because it makes the documented contract true regardless of host environment.

**Lens verdicts:** correctness: UPHELD, zig-semantics-safety: UPHELD, reproduction: UPHELD

### [L11] matchGlob silently treats >64-segment paths as non-matching, dropping deeply nested source files from mutation with no diagnostic

- **Severity:** Low  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 3/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D7-errorsets
- **Location(s):** `src/project_model.zig`

**Evidence:**
```zig
`matchGlob` uses fixed 64-entry segment buffers and returns false if `splitSegments` overflows:

  src/project_model.zig:14  pub fn matchGlob(pattern: []const u8, path: []const u8) bool {
  src/project_model.zig:15      var pat_buf: [64][]const u8 = undefined;
  src/project_model.zig:16      var path_buf: [64][]const u8 = undefined;
  src/project_model.zig:17      const pat_segs = splitSegments(pattern, &pat_buf) orelse return false;
  src/project_model.zig:18      const path_segs = splitSegments(path, &path_buf) orelse return false;

  src/project_model.zig:21  fn splitSegments(s: []const u8, buf: *[64][]const u8) ?[][]const u8 {
  src/project_model.zig:24      while (it.next()) |seg| {
  src/project_model.zig:25          if (n >= buf.len) return null;   // overflow -> null -> matchGlob false

`isEligible` (line 73) returns false when no include matches, and `discover` (line 108) silently `continue`s on ineligible entries — so a `.zig` file nested deeper than 64 path segments is excluded from the mutation set with no diagnostic and no error.
```

**Tool confirmation:** Read of src/project_model.zig (full file) this session. The overflow branch returns null which `matchGlob` maps to false; `discover` (lines 104-110) drops non-eligible files silently. `zig build`/`zig build test` exit 0 (ground truth) — this is a silent eligibility drop, not a crash.

**Why it is wrong:** For a mutation-testing tool, silently NOT mutating an includable source file gives a false sense of coverage: the file contributes no candidates and never appears in the report, with nothing signaling it was skipped due to a structural limit rather than an exclude rule.

**Impact & repro:** A legitimately-included but very deeply nested file is silently omitted from mutation. Severity is Low because >64 path segments is pathological in practice, but the failure mode is silent under-coverage rather than a clear error, which is the worst-case behavior for a correctness tool.  
_Repro:_ Place a `.zig` file at a path with more than 64 `/`-separated segments under an included root (e.g. nested directories a/a/a/.../file.zig with >64 components). `matchGlob("src/**/*.zig", path)` returns false, `isEligible` returns false, and `discover` omits it with no diagnostic.

**Suggested fix:** Either grow/elide the segment cap with an allocator-backed split, or detect the overflow path and surface a diagnostic (e.g. a backend/config error) so an unmatched-due-to-depth file is reported rather than silently skipped. At minimum, document the 64-segment limit in docs/CONFIG_SPEC.md.

**Lens verdicts:** correctness: UPHELD, zig-semantics-safety: UPHELD, reproduction: UPHELD

### [L12] Doctest per-case workspace-creation failure aborts the whole run (exit 4) instead of isolating the case as invalid

- **Severity:** Low  |  **Confidence:** Medium  |  **Verification:** 3/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D7-errorsets
- **Location(s):** `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/doctest_command.zig`, `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/doctest/runner.zig`, `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/doctest/workspace.zig`, `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/mutant_runner.zig`, `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/cli.zig`

**Evidence:**
```zig
doctest_command.run loops over selected cases at src/doctest_command.zig:111-114 with `try cases.append(arena, try runCase(...))`. runCase -> runZig (src/doctest/runner.zig:144-146) does `try ctx.provider.materialize(plan)`, whose error set is workspace.MaterializeError = error{WorkspaceCreateFailed}||OutOfMemory (src/doctest/workspace.zig:100). doctest_command.run's RunError = error{CaseNotFound}||workspace.MaterializeError (src/doctest_command.zig:88), so a WorkspaceCreateFailed for ONE case propagates straight out, discarding every other case's result. The CLI adapter maps it to exit 4 with no report (src/cli.zig:1272-1275). The production materializer returns WorkspaceCreateFailed on any transient createDirPath/writeFile failure (src/cli.zig:791,795,797). By contrast the MUTATION path treats the identical condition as per-mutant isolation: mutant_runner.runSpecs converts WorkspaceOutcome.create_failed into an `invalid` MutationResult and continues the run (src/mutant_runner.zig:40, 159-161).
```

**Tool confirmation:** Grep over test/ (Bash) shows WorkspaceCreateFailed is asserted only in test/mutant_runner_test.zig (the mutation-isolation path); no doctest test exercises a per-case workspace-create failure. Grep of src/cli.zig confirms the only doctest handler for error.WorkspaceCreateFailed is at lines 1272-1275 returning 4. zig build + zig build test both pass (GT), so this is behavior, not a compile/type error. Read of src/doctest/runner.zig:144-146 and src/mutant_runner.zig:159-161 confirms the `try`-vs-`invalidResult` asymmetry.

**Why it is wrong:** runZig propagates the workspace error with `try` and the doctest command's error set re-exports MaterializeError, so the first failing case short-circuits the whole `for (selected)` loop. The mutation runner instead models workspace creation as a WorkspaceOutcome enum and folds a failure into a per-mutant `invalid` status, keeping the run going. The two subsystems made opposite choices for the same environmental failure.

**Impact & repro:** A transient or environmental filesystem failure (disk full, a pre-existing non-directory at the content-addressed workspace path, restrictive permissions) on a single Zig doctest case aborts the entire `zentinel doctest` run with internal-error exit 4 and emits no report, hiding the passing/failing verdicts of all other cases. The blast radius of one case's environment problem is the whole doctest report. Severity is Low because the trigger is environmental rather than content-controlled (the workspace path is a confined content hash, so isConfined/pathEscapesRoot do not fire on normal input) and exit-4 on an internal error is a defensible contract.  
_Repro:_ Run `zentinel doctest --file <doc-with-multiple-zig-cases>` where the doctest workspace root (.zig-cache/zentinel/doctest/<name>) cannot be created for exactly one case — e.g. pre-create a regular file at that case's planned workspace directory path so createDirPath fails (src/cli.zig:791), or run under a full/`chmod -w` .zig-cache. Result: doctest_command.run returns error.WorkspaceCreateFailed, CLI prints 'could not create doctest workspace' and exits 4 with no report. Equivalent failure in a `zentinel run` mutant yields an `invalid` mutant and a complete report instead.

**Suggested fix:** Make the doctest path symmetric with the mutation path: catch workspace.MaterializeError.WorkspaceCreateFailed inside runCase/runZig (or in the run loop) and emit a per-case CaseResult with status `.invalid` plus a ZNTL_DOCTEST_* workspace diagnostic, reserving exit 4 for genuinely run-wide internal errors (OutOfMemory). Alternatively, if aborting is intentional, document it in docs/DOCTEST_SPEC.md and add a test asserting the exit-4 abort so the contract is pinned. Either way, add explicit test coverage for the per-case workspace-failure path (currently none exists).

**Lens verdicts:** correctness: UPHELD, zig-semantics-safety: UPHELD, reproduction: UPHELD

---
### [L13] Entire src/property/ subsystem is production-unreferenced (exercised only by tests)

- **Severity:** Low  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 3/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D8-tests
- **Location(s):** `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/property/report.zig`, `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/property/generator.zig`, `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/root.zig`, `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/test/property_generator_test.zig`

**Evidence:**
```zig
src/property/report.zig exposes pub fn validate (line 80) for the zentinel.pipeline.property_report.v1 contract, and src/property/generator.zig exposes Generator (next/intRange/boolean/bytes). Both are re-exported from src/root.zig:39-42 as zentinel.property.{generator,report}. An exhaustive grep across src/ for property/report, property.report, property_report, and property.generator returns ONLY: the definitions themselves, the root.zig re-export, and a substring false-positive in src/report_junit.zig:127 (a JUnit <property> XML element, unrelated). No CLI verb references 'property' (grep of src/cli.zig: none). The only callers of prep.validate() are in test/property_generator_test.zig (lines 106,144,176,190,200,235,246,254). zig_test_for_symbol for 'validate' likewise returns only test files.
```

**Tool confirmation:** Bash grep: `grep -rn "property/report|property.report|pipeline.property_report|property_report" src/` -> only root.zig:36/41, report.zig:4/14/79 (self). `grep -rni property src/cli.zig` -> none. `grep -n property src/report_junit.zig` -> line 127 `<property name=...>` (XML, false positive). mcp__zigars__zig_test_for_symbol symbol=validate -> all candidate_tests are test/*.zig files. Build/test GT: `zig build test` exit 0 (the property tests pass) but exercise a module with zero product consumers.

**Why it is wrong:** This is the structural root of the cluster of property-report findings from earlier passes. The module's own docstring (report.zig:5-7) claims it is 'the executable check that distinguishes passing property evidence from missing or malformed evidence so pipeline verification can gate on it', but the shipped zentinel binary never calls it; enforcement of the property_report contract rests entirely on external tooling (scripts/validate_task_system.py / CI) and on property_generator_test.zig itself. Because validate() drives no product path, the test suite around it is the SOLE guard, and prior passes already showed that guard is tag-blind (the 8-fixture loop asserts only v != .ok) and skips the entire top-of-funnel. Net coverage-truth: a behavioral regression to validate() is invisible to every product code path and only weakly pinned by tests.

**Impact & repro:** A correctness regression in the property_report validator cannot be caught by any integration/product test (there is no product caller); it can only be caught by property_generator_test.zig, whose assertions (per earlier passes) do not pin violation tags or negative top-of-funnel branches. Coverage numbers / 'covered: true' registry rows for property evidence overstate real protection.  
_Repro:_ From repo root: `grep -rn "property\.report\|property/report" src/` shows no caller outside root.zig re-export and self; `grep -rni property src/cli.zig` shows no CLI verb; the only validate() call sites are in test/property_generator_test.zig.

**Suggested fix:** Either (a) wire the property_report validator into a real product path (e.g. a `zentinel verify` / pipeline gate subcommand in src/cli.zig that loads and validates artifacts/pipeline/<task>/property/report.json and exits non-zero on violation), or (b) explicitly document in the module and the coverage-gap README that src/property is a pipeline/test-only deterministic-core helper with no runtime consumer, and harden property_generator_test.zig to assert exact Violation tags (not just != .ok) and cover the untested rejection branches so the test guard is load-bearing.

**Lens verdicts:** correctness: UPHELD, zig-semantics-safety: UPHELD, reproduction: UPHELD

### [L14] Dead future_global_options array never read

- **Severity:** Low  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 3/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D9-arch
- **Location(s):** `src/root.zig`

**Evidence:**
```zig
src/root.zig:279 declares `const future_global_options = [_][]const u8{ "--config", "--root", "--verbose", "--quiet" };`. A workspace-wide grep for `future_global_options` returns exactly one hit — the declaration itself. The `dispatch()` function (same file, starting at line 296) does not iterate this array; it returns a generic `cli_invalid_option` error for any unknown option without consulting the array.
```

**Tool confirmation:** grep -rn 'future_global_options' /Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/ /Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/test/ returns exactly one result: src/root.zig:279 (the declaration). zig_dead_decl_candidates also flags it. Build succeeds with zero warnings (dead `const` at file scope is not a compile error in Zig).

**Why it is wrong:** The array documents anticipated future options but is never consumed by any code path. Its presence creates a false impression of correctness ("these options are handled somewhere") and it diverges silently from actual behaviour — `dispatch` already routes `--config` and `--root` via `route()` before the frozen dispatch is ever called, making this array doubly stale.

**Impact & repro:** Low. No runtime effect; the dead array occupies binary space and misleads reviewers about option handling.  
_Repro:_ Read src/root.zig:279-284 and src/root.zig:296-332 (`dispatch`); no code path reads the array.

**Suggested fix:** Delete lines 278-284 of src/root.zig (the array and its comment). The comment at line 329 already explains that `--config`/`--root` are owned by `route()`, making the declaration redundant.

**Lens verdicts:** correctness: UPHELD, zig-semantics-safety: UPHELD, reproduction: UPHELD

### [L16] Triplicated AI option-parsing loops across runAiCommand/runDoctestAi/runDoctestSurvivorAi

- **Severity:** Low  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 3/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D9-arch
- **Location(s):** `src/cli.zig`

**Evidence:**
```zig
src/cli.zig:838–865 (`runAiCommand`), src/cli.zig:989–1020 (`runDoctestAi`), and src/cli.zig:1109–1136 (`runDoctestSurvivorAi`) each contain structurally identical while-loops that hand-parse `--ai-provider`, `--input-report`, and `--format` options with identical error strings and logic. The only variation is the positional-arg variable name (`mutant_ref`, `positional`, `survivor_ref`) and the unknown-option error message text (`"unknown AI command option"` vs `"unknown doctest AI option"`). Grep confirms 6–7 `std.mem.eql`/`std.mem.startsWith` calls per loop with identical branch bodies.
```

**Tool confirmation:** `grep -n 'std.mem.eql\|std.mem.startsWith'` on each loop's line range returned 6, 7, and 6 matches respectively. Manual read of lines 838–865, 989–1020, and 1109–1136 confirms byte-for-byte identical handling of all three shared options.

**Why it is wrong:** Adding or modifying a shared AI option (e.g. `--format` gains a third value, or a new `--source-context-lines` option is introduced) requires three parallel changes with no mechanism enforcing consistency. Prior bugs in AI option handling (e.g. missing required-value checks) have been replicated into all three copies.

**Impact & repro:** Maintenance burden: each shared option change requires three edits. Risk of divergence is high — `runDoctestAi` already has a distinct `--file` branch and a different initial `i` value (`i = 1` vs `i = 0`), evidence that the copies have already started drifting. An inconsistency in option names or validation across the three functions is confusing to users.  
_Repro:_ Compare src/cli.zig lines 838–865, 989–1020, and 1109–1136 directly.

**Suggested fix:** Extract a shared `AiOptions` struct and a single `parseAiOptions(args, start_index, ...)` helper that returns the parsed fields. Each of the three functions calls the helper, then handles its own positional-argument logic. Alternatively, add the shared options to the existing `AiCliSettings`/`aiSettings` path so they are parsed in one place.

**Lens verdicts:** correctness: UPHELD, zig-semantics-safety: UPHELD, reproduction: UPHELD

### [L17] emitCleanupWarningIfNeeded silently ignores its arena allocator parameter

- **Severity:** Low  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 3/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D9-arch
- **Location(s):** `src/root.zig`

**Evidence:**
```zig
src/root.zig:396-400:
` ` `
pub fn emitCleanupWarningIfNeeded(arena: std.mem.Allocator, count: u32, stderr: *std.Io.Writer) !void {
    _ = arena;
    if (count == 0) return;
    try stderr.print("warning: failed to remove {d} mutation workspace(s)\n", .{count});
}
` ` `
Line 397 discards `arena` with `_ = arena`. The sister function `cleanupWarningText` at line 390 actually uses its `arena` parameter (it calls `std.fmt.allocPrint`). Callers: `src/cli.zig:543` passes `gpa`; `test/cli_test.zig:208-210` passes `std.testing.allocator`. Both allocators are silently dropped.
```

**Tool confirmation:** Direct code read of src/root.zig lines 396-400 confirmed `_ = arena;` at line 397. grep of all callers at src/cli.zig:543 and test/cli_test.zig:208,210 confirms the unused parameter is threaded through.

**Why it is wrong:** The function signature accepts an allocator but never allocates, using `stderr.print` directly instead of the allocating `cleanupWarningText`. The parameter was likely added for API symmetry with `cleanupWarningText` or in anticipation of future formatting complexity that never materialized. The two functions also independently format the same message string rather than sharing the format string through `cleanupWarningText`.

**Impact & repro:** No behavioral defect — the warning is emitted correctly. Architectural smell: a public API that accepts a resource and silently discards it misleads callers into thinking allocation is needed and creates a false dependency on an allocator at call sites. The duplicated format string across the two functions is a maintenance hazard.  
_Repro:_ Read src/root.zig:396-400. The `_ = arena;` suppression is explicit.

**Suggested fix:** Remove the `arena` parameter from `emitCleanupWarningIfNeeded` and update both call sites (`src/cli.zig:543`, `test/cli_test.zig:208,210`) accordingly. Optionally, implement it as a thin wrapper: `try stderr.writeAll(try cleanupWarningText(arena, count));` — but that reintroduces the allocator parameter with actual use.

**Lens verdicts:** correctness: UPHELD, zig-semantics-safety: UPHELD, reproduction: UPHELD

### [L18] sourceFor performs an O(M*F) linear scan, once per mutant candidate

- **Severity:** Low  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 3/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D10-perf
- **Location(s):** `src/run_command.zig`

**Evidence:**
```zig
src/run_command.zig:268: `const source = sourceFor(files, candidate.file) orelse return error.SourceFileMissing;` is called inside `for (candidates)` — once per mutant. `sourceFor` at lines 395–400 iterates `files` with a sequential `std.mem.eql` comparison per entry until a match is found.
```

**Tool confirmation:** Confirmed by reading src/run_command.zig lines 267–272 (the Phase A candidate loop) and lines 395–400 (the `sourceFor` implementation). No map or sorted lookup exists; it is a plain `for (files) |f|` linear scan.

**Why it is wrong:** When M mutants are generated across F source files, `sourceFor` performs M linear scans of the F-element files slice, giving O(M * F) string comparisons. Since candidates are sorted by file (via `mutant.sortAndDedupe`), consecutive mutants for the same file all re-scan the full slice until they hit the same entry.

**Impact & repro:** For a project with hundreds of mutants across dozens of files this is O(thousands) of path-string comparisons that are all redundant. The impact is small in absolute wall-clock terms compared with process spawning, but it grows with project size and is completely avoidable. The Phase A loop is serial and runs before any parallelism begins.  
_Repro:_ Run `zentinel run` on a project with many source files (20+) and many mutants per file (50+). Instrument `sourceFor` to count iterations; the total will approach M * F.

**Suggested fix:** Build a `std.StringHashMap([]const u8)` from `files` before the Phase A loop (path -> source bytes) and replace `sourceFor(files, candidate.file)` with `file_map.get(candidate.file)`. Alternatively, since candidates are already sorted by file after `sortAndDedupe`, use a running pointer that advances only when the file changes.

**Lens verdicts:** correctness: UPHELD, zig-semantics-safety: UPHELD, reproduction: UPHELD

---
### [L19] findBlockByLine is an O(B) linear scan called per block ref in the hot doctest cache-key loop

- **Severity:** Low  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 3/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D10-perf
- **Location(s):** `src/doctest/cache.zig`

**Evidence:**
```zig
src/doctest/cache.zig:71: `if (findBlockByLine(blocks, line)) |b|` inside `hashBlock`. src/doctest/cache.zig:79: `if (findBlockByLine(blocks, lineOfRef(ref))) |b|` inside `hashExpectations`, inside `for (c.block_refs[1..]) |ref|`. `findBlockByLine` at lines 88–92 is a sequential scan over all blocks comparing `b.line_start == line`.
```

**Tool confirmation:** Confirmed by reading src/doctest/cache.zig lines 70–93. The outer `buildMetadata` function iterates `cases` (one per doctest case), and for each case calls `hashBlock` (one `findBlockByLine`) and `hashExpectations` (one `findBlockByLine` per expectation block ref). No sorted lookup or index exists.

**Why it is wrong:** If a document has B blocks and C cases with R expectation refs each, the total block-lookup cost is O(C * (1 + R) * B). For large documentation files with many doctest cases this is quadratic in the block count.

**Impact & repro:** Doctest cache metadata is built once per `zentinel doctest` invocation or once at the start of a mutation doctest run. The overhead is modest relative to actual process-execution time for each case, but it is O(B^2) in the worst case and trivially avoidable. For documentation files with dozens of fenced blocks and many cases the scan count is visible in a profiler.  
_Repro:_ Create a Markdown doc with 50 fenced blocks each being a doctest case, each with 2 expectation refs. Instrument `findBlockByLine` with a counter; it will be called 150 times, each scanning up to 50 blocks.

**Suggested fix:** Before the `for (cases)` loop in `buildMetadata`, build a `std.AutoHashMap(u32, block.Block)` keyed by `b.line_start`. Replace the two `findBlockByLine` calls with O(1) map lookups. Alternatively, if blocks are sorted by `line_start`, use `std.sort.binarySearch`.

**Lens verdicts:** correctness: UPHELD, zig-semantics-safety: UPHELD, reproduction: UPHELD

### [L21] zentinel init --test-command writes raw user input into TOML without escaping quotes (structure injection)

- **Severity:** Low  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 3/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D11-cli
- **Location(s):** `src/root.zig`, `src/cli.zig`

**Evidence:**
```zig
src/root.zig lines 147-155: initConfigText performs literal string substitution of commands = ["<user-value>"] with no TOML escaping. If the value contains a closing double-quote (e.g. zig test", "extra), the generated TOML becomes commands = ["zig test", "extra"], a syntactically valid TOML array with two elements. No validation of --test-command occurs in dispatchInit (root.zig:334-364) or initConfigText. The generated TOML is only validated on the next zentinel invocation.
```

**Tool confirmation:** Code read of src/root.zig:147-155 and src/root.zig:334-364. Bash grep found no command.parse call in the init path.

**Why it is wrong:** An automated tool or script that captures arbitrary text and passes it as --test-command could inadvertently produce a zentinel.toml with injected extra test commands. The file looks visually correct to users who glance at it.

**Impact & repro:** If --test-command value contains a double-quote, the generated zentinel.toml may have a different semantic structure than intended: more array elements or a TOML parse error. At worst, an unintended additional test command is added and executed during zentinel run.  
_Repro:_ Run: zentinel init --force --test-command 'zig test", "evil_command'. Inspect zentinel.toml: it will contain commands = ["zig test", "evil_command"] with two array elements.

**Suggested fix:** Validate --test-command with command.parse() before writing and reject values that do not produce a valid single argv. Also TOML-escape the value (replace '"' with '\"' and '\' with '\\') before embedding it in the template string.

**Lens verdicts:** correctness: UPHELD, zig-semantics-safety: UPHELD, reproduction: UPHELD
