### [L22] --mutate anywhere in doctest args hijacks dispatch, preempting named AI subcommands

- **Severity:** Low  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 3/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D11-cli
- **Location(s):** `src/cli.zig`

**Evidence:**
```zig
cli.zig:1183-1185: `for (inv.args) |arg| { if (std.mem.eql(u8, arg, "--mutate")) return runDoctestMutate(...); }` scans ALL elements of `inv.args` before the named-subcommand check at lines 1189-1195. Example: `zentinel doctest suggest --mutate` -> `inv.args = ["suggest", "--mutate"]`. The scan at line 1183 finds `"--mutate"` and dispatches to `runDoctestMutate`. Inside `runDoctestMutate` (line 1352-1367), `suggest` is not `--mutate` and not `--file`, so it hits line 1363 and prints `error[ZNTL_CLI_INVALID_OPTION]: unsupported doctest --mutate option suggest`. The user gets a wrong error instead of the suggest AI flow. The named-subcommand check at lines 1189-1195 is never reached.
```

**Tool confirmation:** Source read directly confirms the dispatch order at cli.zig:1183-1195. Build and tests pass (zig build + zig build test exit 0), meaning no existing test covers this dispatch combination.

**Why it is wrong:** The `--mutate` scan is a linear search over all args before the named-subcommand check. Any occurrence of the literal string `--mutate` in any position hijacks routing. Named subcommands (explain, suggest, review-snapshot, suggest-missing, explain-survivor) are supposed to route first, but the code checks `--mutate` first.

**Impact & repro:** A user who runs `zentinel doctest explain <case-ref> --mutate` or `zentinel doctest suggest <doc-path> --mutate` gets a confusing and wrong error message. The intended command never executes. No wrong report is produced, only a wrong rejection.  
_Repro:_ Run `zentinel doctest suggest docs/CLI_SPEC.md --mutate`. Expected: dispatches to runDoctestAi for suggest_doctest. Actual: dispatches to runDoctestMutate, which rejects 'suggest' as 'unsupported doctest --mutate option suggest' and exits 2.

**Suggested fix:** Perform the named-subcommand check (lines 1189-1195) BEFORE the `--mutate` flag scan (lines 1183-1185). If `inv.args[0]` is a recognized named subcommand, dispatch it immediately regardless of whether `--mutate` appears later. Alternatively, restrict the `--mutate` scan to only check `inv.args[0]` directly (rather than scanning all args).

**Lens verdicts:** correctness: UPHELD, zig-semantics-safety: UPHELD, reproduction: UPHELD

---
### [L23] boolean_literal mutates enum field declarations named `true`/`false`, generating a guaranteed-compile_error mutant on a spec-Forbidden context (`field names`)

- **Severity:** Low  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 3/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** critic
- **Location(s):** `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/mutators/boolean.zig`, `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/run_command.zig`, `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/list_mutants_command.zig`, `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/mutant_runner.zig`, `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/docs/MUTATOR_SPEC.md`

**Evidence:**
```zig
boolean.zig:33-39 `collect` iterates EVERY node and matches `if (tag != .identifier) continue;` then slices the node's main token and calls `replacementFor(text)` for any text == "true"/"false". It applies no context guard (the only filter is `inTestBody`, line 41). In Zig 0.16.0, an enum field DECLARATION named `true`/`false` is an `.identifier` node whose main token slices to `'true'`/`'false'`. AST dump of `const E = enum { true, false };` (zig 0.16.0 std.zig.Ast.parse):
  node[2] tag=identifier main_tok=5 slice='true'
  node[4] tag=identifier main_tok=7 slice='false'
  node[11] tag=field_access slice='.'   <- enum-literal USAGE E.true, NOT matched
A faithful replica of collect's loop (lines 33-39) over `enum { true, false }` emits 2 candidates: node[2] 'true'->'false' @byte17 and node[4] 'false'->'true' @byte23. The patched output fails to compile -- `zig ast-check` on `enum { false, false }`: `error: duplicate enum member name 'false'` (exit 1); on `enum { true, true }`: `error: duplicate enum member name 'true'` (exit 1). The ORIGINAL fixture `const E = enum { true, false }; pub fn use() E { return E.true; }` compiles clean (ast-check exit 0), so the baseline passes and the mutant is genuinely executed/classified, not pre-filtered. MUTATOR_SPEC.md:184 (boolean_literal contract) Forbidden contexts: 'Literals in tests by default; config examples; comments; strings; field names.' -- field names are explicitly forbidden, so this is a documented contract violation. boolean.zig:63 still tags `expected_compile = .compiles`, a false promise for this candidate.
```

**Tool confirmation:** zig 0.16.0 (/opt/homebrew/bin/zig, version 0.16.0): (1) std.zig.Ast.parse AST dump of `enum { true, false }` -> node[2]=identifier slice='true', node[4]=identifier slice='false', node[11]=field_access for E.true usage. (2) Replica of collect lines 33-39 over the fixture -> 'TOTAL boolean_literal candidates = 2' (both enum field names; the E.true usage correctly not matched). (3) `zig ast-check` on `enum { false, false }` -> 'error: duplicate enum member name \'false\'' exit 1; on `enum { true, true }` -> 'error: duplicate enum member name \'true\'' exit 1. (4) `zig ast-check` on original fixture -> exit 0 (baseline valid). (5) `zig ast-check` on `const true = 1;` -> 'error: name shadows primitive \'true\'' exit 1, confirming top-level const true/false is NOT a legal misfire site; enum field decls are the bounded legal misfire. (6) `zig ast-check` on `struct { true: u8 }` -> exit 0 and emits no .identifier match, so struct field names neither misfire nor are illegal -- the misfire is precisely bounded to ENUM field declarations. grep confirmed boolean.collect is wired into both real paths (run_command.zig:589, list_mutants_command.zig:86). grep of test/ for `enum { true`/`true, fals …[clipped]

**Why it is wrong:** collect (boolean.zig:35) gates only on node tag `.identifier` plus literal token text "true"/"false". The mutator's header comment (lines 5-7) claims it excludes enum literals because `.true` is 'a different node tag' -- but that reasoning only covers enum-literal USAGE (`E.true` => `field_access`, confirmed node[11]), NOT enum field DECLARATIONS, which the AST represents as plain `.identifier` nodes whose main token is the keyword `true`/`false`. The comment therefore gives false assurance for a case it does not actually handle. The candidate has a valid edit shape (mutant.zig:100-106: span len 4 == original.len, original != replacement, byte_start<=byte_end, nonzero line/col) so Collector.add (ast_backend.zig:123-143) accepts it and sandbox.apply accepts the well-formed patch. expected_compile is never consulted during classification: terminalStatus (mutant_runner.zig:46-53) maps a failed command with failure_kind==compile_error (runner.zig:161, isCompileFailure) straight to ResultStatus.compile_error, regardless of the candidate's `.compiles` tag.

**Impact & repro:** Every production file containing an enum whose fields are literally named `true`/`false` yields N guaranteed-invalid mutants (one per such field), each landing in the JSON report as a `compile_error` result and incrementing summary.total and summary.compile_error (report.zig:96-104, 224-229). This is the same harmful class as the cited errdefer_remove / error_catch_unreachable findings: a known-useless mutant that consumes a sandbox compile, adds a noise entry to the mutants array, and inflates the total denominator used by any downstream kill-ratio consumer. It is NOT excused by I-010 (INVARIANTS.md:95) -- I-010 covers 'meaningful Zig mutations [that] expose type/comptime/safety boundaries'; a duplicate-enum-member error from mutating a field NAME exposes nothing about production behavior and is explicitly a Forbidden context per the spec. Bounded but real: `enum { true, false }` is legal, reachable Zig (e.g. token-kind or keyword enums) and is mutated on the live generate path.  
_Repro:_ 1. Create a production .zig file with `const E = enum { true, false }; pub fn use() E { return E.true; }`. 2. Run zentinel generate/run (or list-mutants) over it -- boolean.collect (run_command.zig:589 / list_mutants_command.zig:86) emits two boolean_literal candidates at the field-name byte offsets (17 and 23). 3. Each patched source (`enum { false, false }` and `enum { true, true }`) is applied and compiled; Zig reports `duplicate enum member name`. 4. Observe two `compile_error` mutants in the report whose `expected_compile` is `compiles`. Confirmed offline: AST dump shows the field names are `.identifier` nodes matching 'true'/'false'; replica of collect emits 2 candidates; `zig ast-check` on both patched forms exits 1 with duplicate-member errors; the original fixture compiles clean.

**Suggested fix:** In boolean.zig collect, before emitting, confirm the `.identifier` node is a boolean VALUE expression and not a container field NAME. Concretely: skip the candidate when the matched node is the name token of a `container_field`/`container_field_init`/`container_field_align` node (the field-name position), or equivalently require the identifier to be in an expression context. A targeted check is sufficient because struct field names tokenize differently and a top-level `const true` is rejected by Zig -- the only legal misfire site is an enum field declaration. Then add a regression fixture `const E = enum { true, false };` plus a value-use site and assert boolean.collect emits ZERO candidates for the field names (only real boolean VALUES), closing the spec's `field names` Forbidden-context requirement (MUTATOR_SPEC.md:184).

**Lens verdicts:** CORRECTNESS: UPHELD, Zig-semantics/safety: verified the AST node-tag claim, compile behavior of the mutated source, edit-shape acceptance, and the classification data-flow against real Zig 0.16.0 and the actual code.: UPHELD, REPRODUCTION: UPHELD

### [L24] Doctest mutator-spec validator (validateDoc) falsely flags every stable Phase-2 operator as drift: candidatesOrParseError wires only 4 of 8 collectors

- **Severity:** Low  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 3/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** critic
- **Location(s):** `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/doctest/mutator_doctest.zig`, `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/docs/MUTATOR_SPEC.md`, `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/docs/DOCTEST_MUTATION_STRATEGY.md`

**Evidence:**
```zig
candidatesOrParseError (mutator_doctest.zig:68-79) invokes only arithmetic.collect, comparison.collect, logical.collect, boolean.collect -- the 4 files holding the 6 stable Phase-1 operators (arithmetic_add_sub, arithmetic_mul_div, equality_swap, comparison_boundary, logical_and_or, boolean_literal; equality_swap+comparison_boundary live in comparison.zig per comparison.zig:14-15). It omits optional.collect, error_path.collect, integer_boundary.collect, loop_boundary.collect -- the 4 files holding the 6 stable Phase-2 operators (MUTATOR_SPEC.md:51-64 lists 12 stable operators total). All 4 omitted collectors have the identical signature `collect(*Collector, Parsed, file, []const ByteRange) Allocator.Error!void` (confirmed in optional.zig:26-31, error_path.zig:29-34, integer_boundary.zig:38-43, loop_boundary.zig:39-44), so they are trivially wireable. When validatePair finds no candidate matching the documented `after`, validateDoc emits error_codes.doctest_snapshot_mismatch with message 'documented transformation is not produced by any stable mutator' (mutator_doctest.zig:151-156) -- a provably FALSE statement for any Phase-2 operator, since the transformation IS produced by a stable mutator, just one validateDoc never calls.
```

**Tool confirmation:** Built a standalone repro (zig test --dep zentinel -Mzentinel=src/root.zig) calling md.validateDoc on a doc containing a `zig before`/`zig after` pair for optional_orelse_unreachable (`fn pick(x: ?u32) u32 { return x orelse 0; }` -> `... return x orelse unreachable;`). Output: 'pairs.len=1 diagnostics.len=1 / pair matched=false operator='' / diag code='ZNTL_DOCTEST_SNAPSHOT_MISMATCH' line=3 msg='documented transformation is not produced by any stable mutator' / validatePair matched=false operator='' count=0'. A second probe with error_catch_unreachable (`foo() catch doThing();` -> `foo() catch unreachable;`) produced the same ZNTL_DOCTEST_SNAPSHOT_MISMATCH. The candidate_count=0 confirms the 4-collector set generates zero candidates for the Phase-2 snippet. grep confirms docs/MUTATOR_SPEC.md has exactly 6 `zig before`/`zig after` fence lines, all in Phase-1 sections (lines 94,100,153,159,191,197).

**Why it is wrong:** The validator's core contract (module doc comment lines 2-8; DOCTEST_MUTATION_STRATEGY.md:10 'Verify mutator specs with executable before/after examples'; MUTATOR_SPEC.md:3 'A mutator is stable only when this document defines its transformation...'; ROADMAP.md:89,207 'stable mutator docs begin using executable zig before/zig after examples' and 'New stable mutators must pass mutation-aware doctest checks before stabilization') requires every stable mutator to carry a verified executable before/after example. The validator that performs that verification structurally cannot verify half the stable catalog. The drift diagnostic it would emit is semantically wrong (the mutator exists and is stable).

**Impact & repro:** Latent today: docs/MUTATOR_SPEC.md documents all 6 Phase-2 stable operators as Markdown `| Field | Contract |` tables, not `zig before`/`zig after` fences, so validateDoc currently sees only the 3 Phase-1 pairs. The defect becomes live the moment anyone follows the documented stabilization policy and adds a single executable before/after fence for a Phase-2 stable operator (e.g. optional_orelse_unreachable) to the spec: the test 'docs/MUTATOR_SPEC.md before/after pairs all match the mutators' (doctest_mutator_spec_test.zig:108-121, which asserts every pair matched and no snapshot_mismatch) would fail, and the operator would be misreported as documentation drift -- punishing correct adherence to the spec's own rule. The masking `v.pairs.len >= 3` assertion (line 113) hides the restriction by not asserting the count is exactly 3.  
_Repro:_ 1) zig test --dep zentinel -Mroot=<repro.zig> -Mzentinel=/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/root.zig where repro.zig calls zentinel.doctest.mutator_doctest.validateDoc(arena, "docs/MUTATOR_SPEC.md", doc) with doc embedding a ```zig before / ```zig after pair for `x orelse 0` -> `x orelse unreachable`. Observe pairs[0].matched=false and a ZNTL_DOCTEST_SNAPSHOT_MISMATCH diagnostic. 2) Equivalent live trigger: add that fence pair under the optional_orelse_unreachable section of docs/MUTATOR_SPEC.md and run `zig build test` -- the existing doctest_mutator_spec_test.zig:108 test fails.

**Suggested fix:** Wire the 4 remaining stable collectors into candidatesOrParseError (mutator_doctest.zig:73-76) exactly as the real pipeline already does (run_command.zig:586-596 and list_mutants_command.zig:83-93 call all 8 collectors), then tighten the masking assertion at doctest_mutator_spec_test.zig:113 to the true expected pair count. The module doc comment (lines 2-8) and the local names referencing 'stable Phase 1 AST mutator' / 'Phase 1 candidate set' should be updated to 'all stable AST mutators'. Note this same 4-collector body is duplicated in mutation_experiment.zig:435-446 (see separate finding) -- consider a single shared registry so the two doctest copies cannot drift from the pipeline registry again.

**Lens verdicts:** CORRECTNESS: UPHELD, Zig-semantics/safety: UPHELD, REPRODUCTION: UPHELD

### [L25] Documented experimental-backend diagnostics artifact is never written; diagnosticsToJson is a dead public export in both ZIR and AIR backends

- **Severity:** Low  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 3/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** critic
- **Location(s):** `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/zir_backend.zig`, `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/air_backend.zig`, `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/cli.zig`, `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/docs/ZIR_BACKEND.md`, `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/docs/AIR_BACKEND.md`

**Evidence:**
```zig
Both backends document a task-scoped JSON artifact and provide the serializer for it, but nothing in src/ ever calls the serializer or writes the file.

zir_backend.zig:13-14 (module doc): "...unsupported evidence is written to a task-scoped artifact under artifacts/pipeline/<task-id>/experimental-backend-diagnostics/."
zir_backend.zig:123-124 (doc on DiagnosticsArtifact): "The out-of-report diagnostics artifact (a separate schema, never report v1). Written under artifacts/pipeline/<task-id>/experimental-backend-diagnostics/."
zir_backend.zig:135: pub fn diagnosticsToJson(arena, diagnostics) ![]u8 -> serializes DiagnosticsArtifact{ schema_version="zentinel.experimental_backend_diagnostics.v1", ... }.
air_backend.zig:15 + 131-145: identical pattern (adds safety_mode).

The CLI never writes this artifact. It only prints ad-hoc unstructured stderr lines:
cli.zig:709-712 (zir): for (listing.diagnostics) |d| { try stderr.print("note[{s}]: {s} at {s}:{d}..{d} ({s})\n", ...); }
cli.zig:732-736 (air): try stderr.print("note[{s}]: {s} at {s}:{d}..{d} source_mapping={s} mode={s} ({s})\n", ...);
These note[...] lines do not match the committed experimental_backend_diagnostics.v1 schema (no schema_version, no backend, no zig_version, no JSON envelope).

The committed fixtures show the documented-but-unwritten artifact shape: test/fixtures/zir_backend/unsupported_diagnostics.json and test/fixtures/air_backend/unsupported_diagnostics.json (schema_version "zentinel.experimental_backend_diagnostics.v1").
```

**Tool confirmation:** mcp__zigars__zig_references on src/zir_backend.zig:135 (diagnosticsToJson) returned ok:true with exactly one result range = the declaration itself (line 134, char 7..24); no other reference. Same tool on src/air_backend.zig:142 returned exactly one result = its own declaration (line 141, char 7..24). Bash grep -rn 'diagnosticsToJson' src/ test/ docs/ -> only the two declarations in src plus two callers in test/zir_backend_test.zig:80 and test/air_backend_test.zig:85 (no src/ caller). Bash grep -rn 'experimental-backend-diagnostics' src/ test/ docs/ -> only 3 doc-comment lines (zir_backend.zig:14,124; air_backend.zig:15) plus 2 docs/*.md lines; zero code paths. Bash grep -rni 'writeFile|createDir|makeDir|makePath' src/zir_backend.zig src/air_backend.zig -> no matches. Bash grep -rn 'artifacts/pipeline' src/ --include=*.zig -> only the 3 doc-comment lines (the only other 'artifacts' hit, src/property/report.zig:5, is unrelated).

**Why it is wrong:** The doc comments in both backend modules and in docs/ZIR_BACKEND.md:61 / docs/AIR_BACKEND.md:67 promise a structured, schema-versioned, on-disk diagnostics artifact (zentinel.experimental_backend_diagnostics.v1) written under artifacts/pipeline/<task-id>/experimental-backend-diagnostics/. No such artifact is ever produced: diagnosticsToJson (the only code that emits that schema) has zero non-test callers per ZLS references, and the CLI substitutes free-form stderr note[...] lines that carry the same facts in a different, unversioned, unstructured format. So the documented out-of-report artifact pipeline is unimplemented and diagnosticsToJson is dead public API. This is a documentation-vs-code divergence in two modules that the surrounding audit dimensions (D6/D7/D11) never opened.

**Impact & repro:** Behaviorally low. The experimental backends are opt-in and listing-only; mutation generation, apply/revert, and kill detection are unaffected (run --backend is a hard usage error per run_command.zig BackendNotInRun, confirmed by run_command_test.zig:670-671). The harm is (a) a maintenance/contract trap: a reader or future task wiring 'the documented diagnostics artifact' will find a serializer that is never called and a doc-promised path that is never created; (b) a consumer relying on the documented JSON artifact (e.g. tooling scraping experimental-backend-diagnostics/) gets nothing on disk and must instead parse undocumented stderr note[...] text; (c) dead public surface (diagnosticsToJson exported but unused outside tests).  
_Repro:_ 1) Tool: load schema then run mcp__zigars__zig_references on src/zir_backend.zig line 134 char 11 -> single result = declaration only. Repeat for src/air_backend.zig line 141 char 11 -> declaration only. 2) Bash: grep -rn 'diagnosticsToJson' src/ -> only the two pub fn declarations, no src caller. 3) Bash: grep -rni 'writeFile|createDir|makePath' src/zir_backend.zig src/air_backend.zig -> empty. 4) Read src/cli.zig:709-736 -> diagnostics are emitted only via stderr.print note[...]. 5) Read docs/ZIR_BACKEND.md:61 and docs/AIR_BACKEND.md:67 -> both assert the artifacts/pipeline/<task-id>/experimental-backend-diagnostics/ write. Optional end-to-end: zentinel list-mutants --backend zir with [backend] experimental=["zir"] over a fixture containing an arithmetic mutation prints note[ZNTL_ZIR_UNS …[clipped]

**Suggested fix:** Resolve the divergence one of two ways (read-only audit; no change applied): (a) Implement the documented pipeline -- in runListMutants, when listing.diagnostics.len > 0, call zentinel.zir_backend.diagnosticsToJson / air_backend.diagnosticsToJson and write the result under a task/run-scoped artifacts/pipeline/<id>/experimental-backend-diagnostics/ path (reusing the existing path-containment helpers config.pathEscapesRoot used elsewhere in cli.zig), keeping the stderr note[...] lines as a human summary; or (b) if writing the artifact is intentionally deferred, correct the doc comments (zir_backend.zig:13-14,124; air_backend.zig:15; docs/ZIR_BACKEND.md:61; docs/AIR_BACKEND.md:67) to state diagnostics are currently surfaced only as stderr note[...] lines and the on-disk artifact is future work, and either remove the now-dead public diagnosticsToJson or mark it not-yet-wired. Either way, add a CLI-level test that invokes runListMutants with an opted-in experimental backend and asserts the  …[clipped]

**Lens verdicts:** CORRECTNESS: UPHELD, ZIG-SEMANTICS/SAFETY: UPHELD, REPRODUCTION: UPHELD

### [L26] CLI experimental-backend diagnostic rendering (runListMutants stderr note path) has no direct test coverage

- **Severity:** Low  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 3/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** critic
- **Location(s):** `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/cli.zig`, `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/test/cli_backend_experiment_test.zig`, `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/test/integration_run_test.zig`

**Evidence:**
```zig
The actual CLI rendering at cli.zig:703-737 (renderText/renderJson of experimental candidates + the stderr note[...] diagnostic loop) is never exercised. Every experimental-backend test calls the library function experimentalListing directly and asserts on the returned Result struct, not on CLI output:
- test/cli_backend_experiment_test.zig:60,68,119,127 call zir/air.experimentalListing(arena, cfg, ...) and check listing.candidates/listing.diagnostics; none drives runListMutants or inspects stderr/stdout.
- test/cli_test.zig:120-130 only covers init --backend zir/air rejection.
- test/run_command_test.zig:670-671 only covers run --backend rejection.
- test/integration_run_test.zig:197 runs the real binary with list-mutants --format json but never with --backend zir|air, so the experimental branch and its diagnostic loop are never hit end-to-end.
```

**Tool confirmation:** Bash grep -rln '"--backend"|"zir"|"air"' test/ -> matches only cli_backend_experiment_test.zig, cli_test.zig, run_command_test.zig, and the two fixture JSONs. Bash grep -n 'zir|air|--backend|note[' test/cli_test.zig test/run_command_test.zig -> only init/run rejection assertions, no list-mutants experimental rendering. Bash grep -rn 'list-mutants|--backend|argv' test/integration_run_test.zig -> argv lists at lines 61/154/197/246/277 never include --backend zir or --backend air. zig_test_map ground truth (provided): 579 test declarations, none assert the runListMutants experimental stderr-note output.

**Why it is wrong:** The branch in cli.zig that distinguishes experimental backends, renders their candidate listing, and prints the per-diagnostic stderr note[...] lines is integration glue with no test that observes its output. Because no quantitative line coverage could be captured (zig_coverage_map rejected the only artifact with InvalidCoverageEvidence per the gathered ground truth), this is asserted from call-site/grep evidence, not a coverage counter -- hence Low.

**Impact & repro:** Low. The underlying library logic (experimentalListing, fromAst, isSupported, diagnostic construction) IS well tested at the unit level, so a regression in candidate/diagnostic content would likely be caught. The untested surface is narrowly the CLI's note[...] formatting and the dispatch wiring; a formatting or wiring regression there (e.g. printing diagnostics to stdout, or dropping them) would pass CI silently.  
_Repro:_ 1) Bash grep across test/ for --backend zir/air real-binary invocations -> none in integration_run_test.zig. 2) Read test/cli_backend_experiment_test.zig -> all tests call experimentalListing directly, never runListMutants. 3) Read src/cli.zig:703-737 -> the renderText/renderJson + stderr note loop has no corresponding test asserting its bytes.

**Suggested fix:** Add a CLI/integration test that runs list-mutants --backend zir (and air) with the backend opted in via [backend] experimental, over a fixture that yields both supported and unsupported operators, and asserts: (a) stdout listing contains only the re-tagged supported candidates, and (b) the diagnostic surface for unsupported operators matches the contract (currently the stderr note[...] lines; ideally the documented JSON artifact once finding #1 is resolved). This also pins the chosen resolution of finding #1.

**Lens verdicts:** CORRECTNESS: UPHELD, ZIG-SEMANTICS/SAFETY: UPHELD, REPRODUCTION: UPHELD

### [L27] mode_matrix non-primary columns bypass Phase B.5 configured-suite re-verification -> unsound per-mode 'survived'

- **Severity:** Low  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 2/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D2-applyrevert, D3-killdetect, D7-errorsets
- **Location(s):** `src/run_command.zig`, `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/run_command.zig`

**Evidence:**
```zig
Phase B.5 (run_command.zig:297-303) escalates only the PRIMARY-mode `results[ji]` for narrowed-selection survivors: `if (results[ji].status != .survived) continue; ... results[ji] = try mergeReverification(arena, results[ji], reverify);`. The mode-matrix build that follows reuses these reverified statuses ONLY for the primary mode (line 314-315 `if (m == mode) { for (results,0..) |r,ji| col[ji] = r.status; }`), while every non-primary mode column (line 316-318) calls `mutant_executor.runSpecs(job.candidate, job.source, job.command_specs, job.commands, m)` with the NARROWED `job.command_specs` and never re-verifies against `cfg.test_commands`. The default strategy is narrowing: config.zig:367 `test.selection` defaults to `"same_file_then_package"`, and test_selection.needsConfiguredReverification (test_selection.zig:161) returns true whenever the run commands differ from the configured set. || run_command.zig 297-303 re-verifies only the primary results array against the configured suite (commandSpecsForConfigured) and merges via mergeReverification. The matrix primary column reuses these results (lines 314-315), but non-primary columns at lines 316-317 re-run against the narrowed job.command_specs and read .status with no re-verification. job.command_specs is the narrowed selection (lines 271-272). test_selection.zig 154-163 says a narrowed survived is unsound until escalated. The comment at lines 294-296 admits only the primary mode is re-verified before the matrix reads it. || In `run` (src/run_command.zig), Phase B.5 re-verifies narrowed-selection survivors against the full configured suite, but ONLY mutates the primary-mode `results[ji]`:

  297  for (jobs, 0..) |job, ji| {
  298      if (results[ji].status != .survived) continue;
  299      if (!test_selection.needsConfiguredReverification(job.commands, cfg.test_commands)) continue;
  300      const reverify_specs = try commandSpecsForConfigured(arena, cfg.test_commands);
  301      const reverify = mutant_exec …[clipped]
```

**Tool confirmation:** Read of run_command.zig:297-322 (reverification loop vs matrix column construction). Read of test_selection.zig:161 (needsConfiguredReverification) and config.zig:367 (default same_file_then_package). No tool could exercise it dynamically because, per the primary finding, all matrix columns currently run identical commands (mode flag not wired), so the asymmetry is presently masked. || Grep of run_command.zig: the only re-verification is lines 298-302 on results ji; the matrix non-primary runSpecs at line 317 is unguarded. Grep of test/: the only end-to-end matrix test (run_command_test.zig 156) uses calc_src (line 18) which has zero test declarations so it never narrows; fixtures/safety_modes/overflow.zig has a same-file test but is never run through the matrix path. || `zig build` + `zig build test` both exit 0 (ground truth), so this compiles and is not a type error — it is a logic asymmetry. `grep -rn mode_matrix|mode_grid|reverif src/ test/` (run this session) shows the only reverification call sites are run_command.zig:297-302 and the only non-primary matrix execution is run_command.zig:317; there is no reverification inside the matrix loop. test/run_command_test.zig:121-179  …[clipped]

**Why it is wrong:** The primary mode carefully escalates a narrowed `survived` to the configured suite, but the non-primary mode_matrix columns skip that escalation, so they can record `survived` for a mutant that the configured suite would actually kill in that mode. The matrix is the surface used to detect safety-mode effects (`safety_modes.isModeDependent`), so a false `survived` in a non-primary column can both hide a killable mutant for that mode and manufacture a spurious 'mode-dependent' signal versus the (correctly reverified) primary column.

**Impact & repro:** For a realistic config — 2+ distinct `zig.modes` (no `--mode` override) plus the default `same_file_then_package` selection — a mutant that survives the narrowed `zig test <file>` but is killed by the configured suite under a non-primary mode is reported as `survived` in that mode_matrix column. This understates kill effectiveness for non-primary modes and can flip `isModeDependent` to true purely from the selection asymmetry rather than a genuine safety-mode effect. Primary `result.status` is unaffected (it is reverified).  
_Repro:_ After wiring per-mode build flags, configure `test.selection = same_file_then_package` and `zig.modes = ["Debug","ReleaseFast"]` on a file whose generated `zig test <file>` misses a mutant that the configured `zig build test` kills. The Debug column (reverified) shows killed; the ReleaseFast column (not reverified) shows survived purely from the narrowed command, not a true mode effect.

**Suggested fix:** Apply the same configured-suite reverification to every narrowed survivor in each non-primary matrix column. In the `else` branch (run_command.zig:316-318), when the per-mode narrowed run returns `.survived` and `needsConfiguredReverification(job.commands, cfg.test_commands)` is true, re-run the configured specs for that mode and use the reverified status, mirroring Phase B.5. Alternatively, document explicitly (report.zig:118 and the matrix comment) that non-primary mode_matrix statuses are narrowed-selection-only and NOT subject to the I-012 soundness guarantee, and have `isModeDependent` consumers account for that.

**Lens verdicts:** CORRECTNESS: UPHELD, ZIG-SEMANTICS/SAFETY: UPHELD, REPRODUCTION: REFUTED

### [L28] report.normalizeExcerpt leaves machine-absolute paths after ':' / '=' / '>' verbatim -> leaks into committed report, breaks determinism

- **Severity:** Low  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 2/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D6-safety
- **Location(s):** `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/report.zig`, `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/runner.zig`

**Evidence:**
```zig
report.zig:549-551 isExcerptBoundary(c) is a positive set: space/tab/CR/LF, quote, '(', '[', '{'. normalizeExcerpt (line 489-490) only starts an absolute-path scan when `text[i]=='/' and at_boundary` where at_boundary requires the preceding byte to be in that set. So a '/'-rooted path preceded by '=', ':', '>', ',', etc. is never recognized and is emitted verbatim. runner.zig:96-100 boundedExcerpt() pipes ALL captured subprocess stdout/stderr (raw.stdout/raw.stderr at runner.zig:186-187) through normalizeExcerpt before it becomes result.evidence.{stdout,stderr}_excerpt in the report. normalizeForComparison (report.zig:393-397) only scrubs durations/run-id/started_at and does NOT re-normalize paths, so a path that escapes normalizeExcerpt at capture time is never scrubbed later.
```

**Tool confirmation:** Compiled the real src/report.zig + src/mutant.zig standalone (zig 0.16.0). Observed normalizeExcerpt outputs: `root=/Users/dev/secret/leak.zig` -> `root=/Users/dev/secret/leak.zig` (UNCHANGED); `see file:///Users/dev/secret/leak.zig now` -> unchanged; `wrote>/Users/dev/secret/leak.zig` -> unchanged. Contrast: `/Users/dev/proj/src/x.zig:5:10: error: boom` -> `<path> error: boom` and `in /Users/dev/proj/src/x.zig here` -> `in <path> here` (boundary paths normalize correctly).

**Why it is wrong:** The normalizeExcerpt docstring (report.zig:470-474) promises 'absolute machine paths (which differ across machines) ... are replaced with the stable placeholders ... so a killed mutant's stderr can no longer make the report non-deterministic.' Build/test output routinely contains `key=/abs/path`, `note:/abs/path`, and redirection/URI forms where the path does not follow a space/quote/bracket. Those leak both the machine path (privacy/committed-artifact concern) and a machine-varying byte sequence (determinism concern). Because the AI layer re-reads these same excerpt fields and shares the identical boundary blind spot (finding above), the intended defense-in-depth is defeated for this path class.

**Impact & repro:** (1) Cross-machine non-determinism: two developers/CI runners over the same project can produce byte-different reports (e.g. `--cache-dir=/Users/alice/...` vs `/Users/bob/...`), violating the repeated-run / cold-vs-warm determinism contract that normalizeExcerpt exists to uphold; equivalentIgnoringTiming compares evidence bytes (report.zig:577-581,597,613) and would report inequality. (2) An absolute machine path is persisted verbatim into zig-out/zentinel/report.json and then forwarded to an AI provider.  
_Repro:_ Build report.zig+mutant.zig standalone and call normalizeExcerpt(arena, "root=/Users/dev/secret/leak.zig"). Output equals input (path not replaced). Any mutant whose captured stderr contains such a line yields an excerpt that differs across machines and embeds the absolute path.

**Suggested fix:** Broaden isExcerptBoundary to also treat '=', ':' (and ideally any non-path char) as a boundary, OR scan for absolute paths anywhere a '/<seg>/<seg>' run appears regardless of preceding char, mirroring whatever fix is chosen for redaction.normalizeAbsolutePaths so the two normalizers stay consistent. Add regression excerpts: `key=/abs/p`, `note:/abs/p`, `file:///abs/p` asserting <path> output and stable cross-machine bytes.

**Lens verdicts:** CORRECTNESS: REFUTED, Zig-semantics/safety: UPHELD, REPRODUCTION: UPHELD

---
### [L29] AI-context test_context.selection_reason bypasses redaction -> untrusted-report paths/secrets leak verbatim

- **Severity:** Low  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 2/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D6-safety
- **Location(s):** `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/ai/command.zig`, `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/ai/context.zig`, `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/schemas/ai.context.v1.schema.json`

**Evidence:**
```zig
src/ai/command.zig:445 reads the untrusted report's selection block: `const selection = get(mutant, "test_selection");`. src/ai/command.zig:497 then emits it into the provider-bound AI context WITHOUT redaction: `.selection_reason = sOr(getO(selection, "strategy"), "same_file_then_package"),`. Every other string field built in the same `buildContext` literal is routed through redaction -- `.file = try context.redactField(...)` (cmd.zig:427), `.original`/`.replacement` (428-429), `.diff` via redactStrArray (430), project `.name`/`.zig_version`/`.zentinel_version` (431,446,447), and all command/evidence fields -- but `selection_reason` alone is passed raw. The structural validator does not gate it: src/ai/context.zig:391-393 only presence-checks `test_context` keys and enum-checks `baseline_status`, never `selection_reason`. The JSON Schema agrees it is unconstrained: schemas/ai.context.v1.schema.json:187 `"selection_reason": { "type": "string", "minLength": 1 }` (no enum). The whole context is serialized into the prompt envelope (`Prompt.context = ctx`, buildPromptValue cmd.zig:514-531) and validated by validatePrompt->context.validate, which passes, so the field is transmitted to the provider. Because no redaction ran on it, it is never added to the RedactionLog, so `privacy.redactions_applied` (cmd.zig:455) omits it.
```

**Tool confirmation:** mcp__zigars__zig_references on src/ai/provider.zig:48 (provider.run) returned exactly ONE result -- its own declaration -- confirming the provider.Advisory path is not what carries this (the live path is buildContext->buildPromptValue). Bash grep confirmed selection_reason set only at src/ai/command.zig:497 with selection sourced at :445, and that schemas/ai.context.v1.schema.json:187 constrains the field to a bare string with minLength 1 and no enum. GROUND TRUTH: `zig build` and `zig build test` both exit 0 with zero diagnostics, so this is current, compiling behavior, not a parse artifact.

**Why it is wrong:** Distinct from the four prior-pass findings. Those named: file:// URIs in normalizeAbsolutePaths; report.normalizeExcerpt leaving paths after ':'/'='/'>'; the MUTATION-flow `mutant.id` and `operator` fields; and the '//' comment over-match. `test_context.selection_reason` is a separate, never-named context field sourced from a different report key (`test_selection.strategy`). When zentinel WRITES a report, strategy is a typed enum, but on the read side of an untrusted `--input-report` it is parsed as a raw std.json string with no enum gate, so an attacker can place any text there.

**Impact & repro:** An untrusted mutation report supplied via `--input-report` to `zentinel explain`/`suggest` can smuggle an absolute developer path (e.g. /Users/alice/secret-proj/...), a PEM/credential, or any sensitive string in `mutants[].test_selection.strategy`; it is sent verbatim to the configured AI provider (including a `remote` provider when allowed). The privacy contract `privacy.redactions_applied` simultaneously reports the leak did not happen, so an operator auditing the privacy field is misled. Same leak/false-accounting class the project already treats as a real defect for id/operator.  
_Repro:_ Construct a minimal report.json with one mutant whose `result.status` is e.g. "survived" and set `mutants[0].test_selection = { "strategy": "/Users/victim/private/key.pem secret-token-abc", "selected": [], "commands": [], "preflight_commands": [], "fallback_used": false }`. Run `zentinel explain <display_id> --input-report report.json --ai-provider stub --format json` (any enabled provider). Inspect the built prompt context: `test_context.selection_reason` equals the raw string and `privacy.redactions_applied` does not contain `absolute_path`/`secret_value` for it. (Static confirmation via the cited lines is definitive; no build needed to see the missing redactField wrapper.)

**Suggested fix:** Route the value through the same logged redaction as its siblings, e.g. `.selection_reason = try context.redactField(arena, sOr(getO(selection, "strategy"), "same_file_then_package"), patterns, &log),` (buildContext already holds `patterns` and `&log`). Optionally also constrain `selection_reason` to the known Strategy vocabulary in context.validate and the schema so a non-enum value is rejected outright.

**Lens verdicts:** CORRECTNESS: UPHELD, Zig-semantics/safety: slice lifetime/ownership through std.json parse + serialization, and actual runtime reachability of the data sink.: REFUTED, REPRODUCTION: UPHELD

---
### [L30] Each source file is AST-parsed twice per run (generateCandidates and selectionForFile)

- **Severity:** Low  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 2/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D10-perf
- **Location(s):** `src/run_command.zig`

**Evidence:**
```zig
src/run_command.zig:582: `var parsed = try ast_backend.parse(arena, f.path, f.source)` inside `generateCandidates` (iterates every file). src/run_command.zig:533: `var parsed = try ast_backend.parse(arena, file, source)` inside `selectionForFile` — called for each unique file in Phase A when `same_file_enabled` is true. Both branches `defer parsed.deinit()` so the tree is not retained between them.
```

**Tool confirmation:** Confirmed by direct read of src/run_command.zig. `generateCandidates` (line 579) runs over every `FileSource` and calls `ast_backend.parse` at line 582. The Phase A loop at line 267 calls `selectionForFile` for every candidate; `selectionForFile` at line 533 calls `ast_backend.parse` a second time for the same file (guarded only by the `same_file_enabled` condition). `ast_backend.parse` at src/ast_backend.zig:73–79 allocates a null-terminated copy of the source and invokes `std.zig.Ast.parse` — the full Zig parser.

**Why it is wrong:** The `sel_cache` in `selectionForFile` deduplicates at the file level (it skips re-running preflight for already-seen files), but it does not skip the AST parse — the parse happens before the cache check is consulted (line 526–528 vs line 533). So every unique file is parsed by the Zig AST parser at least twice: once in `generateCandidates` to produce candidates, and once in `selectionForFile` to discover same-file tests.

**Impact & repro:** The Zig AST parser is non-trivial (null-terminates source, builds node arrays, maps tokens). For a project with F source files, this is 2F full parses instead of F. For large source files the extra parse time is directly observable. Additionally `ast_backend.parse` allocates into the arena for both trees; the second tree is discarded (deinit'd) immediately after `sameFileTests` extracts test names, so the arena is polluted with a full AST copy per file.  
_Repro:_ Add instrumentation to `ast_backend.parse` counting calls. Run `zentinel run` with `test_selection = "same_file_then_package"`. Call count will be 2 * (number of unique source files) rather than 1 * (number of unique source files).

**Suggested fix:** Pass the already-parsed `Parsed` value (or just the extracted `testDecls` slice) from `generateCandidates` into a per-file table that `selectionForFile` can consume instead of re-parsing. One approach: after `generateCandidates` builds the mutant list, also return (or take) a `std.StringHashMap([]const report.SelectedTest)` mapping each file to its already-computed same-file tests; `selectionForFile` then uses that table instead of calling `ast_backend.parse` again.

**Lens verdicts:** CORRECTNESS: UPHELD, Zig-semantics/safety: REFUTED, REPRODUCTION: UPHELD

---
### [L31] run/list-mutants --operator accepts unknown names and silently produces 0 mutants (clean exit 0)

- **Severity:** Low  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 2/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D11-cli
- **Location(s):** `src/run_command.zig`, `src/list_mutants_command.zig`

**Evidence:**
```zig
run_command.parseArgs (run_command.zig:166-169) assigns args[i] to opts.operator_filter without validating against the known operator registry. generateCandidates (run_command.zig:604-606) applies the filter as `if (!std.mem.eql(u8, c.operator, op)) continue` after candidate generation. list_mutants_command.parseArgs (list_mutants_command.zig:43) has the same pattern; generate (list_mutants_command.zig:101-103) applies it the same way. config.zig:70-91 maintains the canonical operator registry (20 named operators) but parseArgs never consults it.
```

**Tool confirmation:** Code read confirms no call to findOperator or any registry lookup in either parseArgs function. No test file exercises `--operator` with a non-existent operator name (grep across test/ returns zero hits for bogus operator names). The Config.zig operator registry exists but is only used during config loading (expandMutators), not during option parsing.

**Why it is wrong:** `zentinel run --operator typo_operator` silently runs the baseline (which may pass), generates 0 mutants, and exits 0 with '0 mutants: 0 killed, 0 survived'. The user receives a clean exit with no indication the filter matched nothing, which could mask a mistyped operator name in CI scripts that check exit codes only.

**Impact & repro:** A CI script that passes `--operator arithmetic_add_sub` (correct) but after a rename becomes `--operator arithmetic_add` (typo) will silently pass with 0 mutants tested, reporting false coverage confidence. The operator filter has no validation and no zero-result warning.  
_Repro:_ With a valid zentinel project: `zentinel run --operator not_a_real_operator_name`. Exit 0, output '0 mutants: 0 killed, 0 survived'. No error, no warning.

**Suggested fix:** In run_command.parseArgs and list_mutants_command.parseArgs, after consuming the operator value, validate it against the known operators in config.zig (expose the registry or a lookup function). Return `error.UnknownOption` or a new `error.UnknownOperator` with a clear message listing valid operator names when the value is not recognized.

**Lens verdicts:** CORRECTNESS: UPHELD, Zig-semantics/safety: REFUTED, REPRODUCTION: UPHELD

### [L32] Doctest AI subcommands accept a missing required positional arg, returning an opaque AI error instead of a CLI usage error

- **Severity:** Low  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 2/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D11-cli
- **Location(s):** `src/cli.zig`

**Evidence:**
```zig
runDoctestAi (cli.zig:989-1086) parses args into positional/file_opt but performs NO post-loop check that a positional is present when the flow requires one. For flow==.suggest_doctest (requires doc-path), flow==.explain_doctest_failure (requires case-ref), and flow==.review_snapshot (requires case-ref), positional remains null and is forwarded as doc_path=null or case_ref=null. The downstream ai.doctest_command.run then returns error.DoctestDocNotFound (ai/doctest_command.zig:912-913) or error.DoctestCaseNotFound (ai/doctest_command.zig:896-897), which the CLI renders as: 'error[ZNTL_DOCTEST_DOC_NOT_FOUND]: advisory doctest AI command failed'. The help text documents 'doctest suggest <doc-path>' and 'doctest explain <case-ref>' as required positionals.
```

**Tool confirmation:** Read of cli.zig lines 1022-1028 confirms case_ref and doc_path are set from positional without any non-null guard. Read of ai/doctest_command.zig lines 912-913 and 896-897 confirms the AI layer, not the CLI layer, is first to detect the missing argument.

**Why it is wrong:** The top-level AI commands (explain/suggest) have an explicit post-loop check at cli.zig:866-868 ('if (flow != .review_tests and mutant_ref == null) return aiOptionError'). The doctest AI subcommands omit an equivalent guard. A user running 'zentinel doctest suggest' with no doc-path gets exit code 2 but sees a ZNTL_DOCTEST_DOC_NOT_FOUND error code and 'advisory doctest AI command failed' message, rather than 'missing <doc-path>' under ZNTL_CLI_INVALID_OPTION. This breaks the pattern established by the top-level commands and makes the error diagnosis harder.

**Impact & repro:** Missing positional argument to 'doctest suggest', 'doctest explain', or 'doctest review-snapshot' produces an AI-layer error code (ZNTL_DOCTEST_DOC_NOT_FOUND / ZNTL_DOCTEST_CASE_NOT_FOUND) and the message 'advisory doctest AI command failed' — indistinguishable from a report-not-found or runtime AI failure — instead of a clear CLI usage error under ZNTL_CLI_INVALID_OPTION.  
_Repro:_ Run: zentinel doctest suggest (no positional). Expected: 'error[ZNTL_CLI_INVALID_OPTION]: missing <doc-path>'. Actual: 'error[ZNTL_DOCTEST_DOC_NOT_FOUND]: advisory doctest AI command failed'.

**Suggested fix:** After the arg-parsing loop in runDoctestAi (cli.zig around line 1021), add guards matching the top-level AI pattern: if (flow == .suggest_doctest and positional == null) return aiOptionError(stderr, "missing <doc-path>"); if ((flow == .explain_doctest_failure or flow == .review_snapshot) and positional == null) return aiOptionError(stderr, "missing <case-ref>");

**Lens verdicts:** CORRECTNESS: UPHELD, Zig-semantics/safety: REFUTED, REPRODUCTION: UPHELD

### [L33] ci.sh advisory_dogfood: all diagnostic output suppressed and error always blames survivors despite infra-only failure mode

- **Severity:** Low  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 2/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D12-build
- **Location(s):** `scripts/ci.sh`, `scripts/dogfood.sh`

**Evidence:**
```zig
ci.sh lines 68-70: `if ! scripts/dogfood.sh >/dev/null 2>&1; then printf 'advisory dogfood reported a non-zero status (advisory; review survivors)\n' >&2; fi`. dogfood.sh line 22: `./zig-out/bin/zentinel --config zentinel.dogfood.toml --root "$fixture_root" run "$@"` — no `--fail-on-survivors` flag. src/run_command.zig line 366: `if (options.fail_on_survivors and summary.survived > 0) exit_code = 1;` — without the flag, survivors produce exit 0. Therefore a non-zero exit from dogfood.sh is exclusively an infrastructure failure (`zig build` error, binary crash, or ZNTL_ runtime error) but the CI message always says 'review survivors'.
```

**Tool confirmation:** Bash confirmed `grep 'fail-on-survivors' scripts/dogfood.sh` returns empty. Confirmed `grep -n 'fail_on_survivors' src/run_command.zig` shows survivors cause non-zero only when the flag is set.

**Why it is wrong:** The diagnostic message misleads developers into looking for mutation survivors when the actual cause is always a build or runtime infrastructure failure. All stdout/stderr is swallowed, making the actual cause impossible to recover from the CI log.

**Impact & repro:** When `zig build` inside dogfood.sh fails (e.g., a background dependency error, sandbox permission issue), the developer sees 'advisory; review survivors' and wastes time looking for mutation outcomes instead of the real build error. If the failure is actually a deterministic binary crash that should block CI, the advisory downgrade means it silently passes.  
_Repro:_ Break `dogfood.sh` by corrupting the zentinel binary path, then run `scripts/ci.sh`. Observe that the output says 'review survivors' with no indication of where or why dogfood.sh exited non-zero.

**Suggested fix:** Redirect only stdout to /dev/null and let stderr through: `scripts/dogfood.sh >/dev/null`. Or log stderr to a temp file and include it in the advisory message. Separately, update the error message to distinguish survivor vs infrastructure failure (e.g., 'dogfood exited non-zero — this is an infrastructure error since --fail-on-survivors is not set; inspect manually').

**Lens verdicts:** CORRECTNESS: UPHELD, Zig-semantics/safety: REFUTED, REPRODUCTION: UPHELD

### [L34] release_acceptance.py check_criteria uses execute_checks=False -> false-OK when a verified_by script would actually fail

- **Severity:** Low  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 2/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D12-build
- **Location(s):** `scripts/release_acceptance.py`

**Evidence:**
```zig
check_criteria() at lines 98-104 calls rdg.validate_manifest(manifest, check_archives=True) — no execute_checks argument, so it defaults to False. This means any gate whose verified_by is a .py or .sh script is checked only for on-disk existence, not for execution success. The same manifest is then passed to rdg.main() at line 190, which internally calls validate_manifest(manifest, check_archives=True, execute_checks=True) — actually running the scripts. If a verified_by script exists on disk but exits non-zero, check_criteria() prints 'acceptance: final_dogfood_gate: OK (...)' followed by rdg.main() printing the real failure. The overall exit code is still 1 (correct), but the stdout output says the gate passed before reporting that it failed.
```

**Tool confirmation:** Source read confirmed at /Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/scripts/release_acceptance.py:98-104 and :190-192. grep showed rdg.validate_manifest calls at lines 98 (no execute_checks) and rdg.main call at line 190. release_dogfood_gate.py:95 shows the default is execute_checks=False; line 223 shows the main() path explicitly passes execute_checks=True. The release_evidence.json fixture uses 'scripts/validate_task_system.py' and 'scripts/check_pipeline_artifacts.py' as verified_by entries (confirmed via cat of the fixture file), so the divergence is live.

**Why it is wrong:** The release acceptance script is the final human-facing gate for task 060. If a gate-verification script is broken, the acceptance report must say so clearly. A script can be present on disk (archive check passes) but broken at execution time (execute_checks would catch it). The current split — check_criteria without execute_checks, then rdg.main with execute_checks — produces contradictory output: 'OK' then 'violation'. An agent or human reading the acceptance report would see OK for the criterion and might miss the subsequent failure lines from rdg.main, especially if output is captured to a file and scanned for per-criterion status.

**Impact & repro:** A broken verified_by script (e.g. scripts/validate_task_system.py exits 1 due to a task-system bug) goes undetected by the check_criteria pass and is only surfaced by rdg.main's separate invocation, with the output showing contradictory OK/FAILED for the same criterion. This makes the release gate output untrustworthy as a criterion-level status table. Exit code is still 1, so CI does block, but human review of the log is confused.  
_Repro:_ Temporarily make scripts/validate_task_system.py exit 1 unconditionally. Run python3 scripts/release_acceptance.py. Observe 'acceptance: final_dogfood_gate: OK (...)' printed by check_criteria, followed by 'release-gate: violation: verified_by check failed (exit 1) for gate failure_recovery_validation: scripts/validate_task_system.py' from rdg.main().

**Suggested fix:** Pass execute_checks=True in check_criteria() when calling rdg.validate_manifest: gate_clean = not rdg.validate_manifest(manifest, check_archives=True, execute_checks=True). Alternatively, remove the separate rdg.main() call from main() since check_criteria already captures the gate_clean result — the separate rdg.main() call is redundant and diverges in execute_checks semantics.

**Lens verdicts:** CORRECTNESS: UPHELD, Zig-semantics/safety: REFUTED, REPRODUCTION: UPHELD

### [L35] MUTATOR_SPEC Operator Overlap policy (restrict contexts) contradicts code's emit-from-both / dedup-at-sort approach

- **Severity:** Low  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 2/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D13-docs
- **Location(s):** `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/docs/MUTATOR_SPEC.md`, `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/mutant.zig`, `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/mutators/comparison.zig`, `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/mutators/loop_boundary.zig`

**Evidence:**
```zig
MUTATOR_SPEC.md lines 388-392: 'When more than one operator could match the same source span, exactly one candidate is emitted, chosen by a deterministic precedence rule ... Absent such a rule, the lower-precedence operator must restrict its allowed contexts to avoid the overlap rather than emit a duplicate candidate.' The code fix (commit b161a27) instead adds `samePhysicalEdit` deduplication in `sortAndDedupe` (src/mutant.zig:193-227). Both operators still collect candidates for while-condition comparisons: comparison.zig:39-43 handles `.less_than`/`.less_or_equal`/`.greater_than`/`.greater_or_equal` on ALL comparison nodes including those in while conditions; loop_boundary.zig:50-51 explicitly walks `while_simple`, `while_cont`, and `@while` and then calls `whileCond` on their condition nodes (lines 60-93), which also handles `.less_than`/`.less_or_equal`/`.greater_than`/`.greater_or_equal`. Neither operator's 'Forbidden contexts' row has been updated. No documented precedence rule for this specific overlap appears anywhere in MUTATOR_SPEC.md.
```

**Tool confirmation:** Bash grep on MUTATOR_SPEC.md for 'comparison_boundary', 'loop_boundary', 'precedence', 'while.*condition', and 'overlap' confirms zero references to a documented while-condition precedence rule. Full read of comparison.zig and loop_boundary.zig confirms both operators still emit candidates for the same while-condition comparison nodes. Full read of mutant.zig:193-227 confirms `sortAndDedupe` uses `samePhysicalEdit` post-collection dedup, not pre-collection restriction. Git diff of b161a27 confirms no change to MUTATOR_SPEC.md's forbidden-context tables.

**Why it is wrong:** The spec's normative requirement ('must restrict allowed contexts ... rather than emit a duplicate candidate') directly contradicts the implementation ('emit from both, dedup at sort time'). A future mutator author reading the spec would incorrectly understand the precedence mechanism. More critically: the spec's stated requirement is that precedence determines which candidate is canonical and the lower-precedence operator does not emit — but the code emits both candidates and silently drops whichever sorts second in canonical order. Those two are not equivalent: the canonical-order representative depends on operator name alphabetic ordering (sort key 4 in MUTATOR_SPEC.md §Candidate Ordering), which makes the retained candidate ('comparison_boundary' < 'loop_boundary' alphabetically) the deterministic choice — but the spec never documents that 'alphabetically first operator name wins for same-span duplicates.' The spec says 'a documented precedence rule must exist' — no such rule exists.

**Impact & repro:** Governance theater that hides a real behavioral subtlety: when both operators fire on a `while (i < n)` condition, the retained candidate is `comparison_boundary` (alphabetically before `loop_boundary`), silently dropping the `loop_boundary` result. This is deterministic but undocumented. A future operator named `aardvark_boundary` targeting the same span would silently displace `comparison_boundary` without any spec violation. Also: the no-overlap dedup is O(n^2) in the output list — not a current correctness issue but notable since the spec's stated approach (restrict at collection time) would be O(1) per candidate.  
_Repro:_ Read docs/MUTATOR_SPEC.md lines 386-392 and compare to src/mutant.zig:193-227. Read comparison.zig swapFor() (lines 35-45) — it handles .less_than, .less_or_equal, .greater_than, .greater_or_equal with no while-context exclusion. Read loop_boundary.zig:50-51 and whileCond() (lines 60-93) — same four tags on while condition nodes. On any source containing `while (i < n)`, both operators produce candidates with identical (file, span, original, replacement).

**Suggested fix:** Either: (a) update MUTATOR_SPEC.md to document the physical-edit dedup mechanism as the canonical overlap resolution strategy and add a documented precedence note ('when two operators produce the same physical edit, the alphabetically earlier operator name in canonical sort order is retained'); or (b) restrict comparison_boundary to exclude while-condition comparison nodes (add 'while loop condition comparisons, which are owned by loop_boundary' to comparison_boundary Forbidden contexts). Option (a) is less invasive and matches the code. Additionally remove the misleading sentence 'the lower-precedence operator must restrict its allowed contexts to avoid the overlap rather than emit a duplicate candidate' or invert it to say 'physical-edit deduplication in sortAndDedupe is the primary mechanism; operators MAY additionally restrict their contexts to avoid redundancy.'

**Lens verdicts:** CORRECTNESS: UPHELD, Zig-semantics/safety: REFUTED, REPRODUCTION: UPHELD

---
### [L36] MUTATOR_SPEC Operator Overlap omits the loop_boundary/comparison_boundary while-condition precedence rule

- **Severity:** Low  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 2/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D13-docs
- **Location(s):** `docs/MUTATOR_SPEC.md`, `src/mutant.zig`, `src/mutators/loop_boundary.zig`, `src/mutators/comparison.zig`, `test/ast_candidate_ordering_test.zig`

**Evidence:**
```zig
docs/MUTATOR_SPEC.md lines 388-392 state: 'When more than one operator could match the same source span, exactly one candidate is emitted, chosen by a deterministic precedence rule' and 'A documented precedence rule must exist before two operators are allowed to match the same span. Absent such a rule, the lower-precedence operator must restrict its allowed contexts to avoid the overlap rather than emit a duplicate candidate.' The only documented precedence rule in the Operator Overlap section (line 390) is the null-equality/optional_null_check rule. No entry exists for loop_boundary vs comparison_boundary on while-conditions. Both operators independently match `<`, `<=`, `>`, `>=` tokens in while-condition nodes (comparison.zig lines 39-42 via swapFor(); loop_boundary.zig lines 24-30 in boundarySwap() called from whileCond()). The code resolves this silently in sortAndDedupe() via samePhysicalEdit() (mutant.zig:193-199), retaining comparison_boundary as the canonical representative. test/ast_candidate_ordering_test.zig lines 69-82 and 85-108 confirm and test this behavior. None of this is documented in the spec's Operator Overlap section.
```

**Tool confirmation:** Read of docs/MUTATOR_SPEC.md (lines 386-392), src/mutators/comparison.zig (lines 39-42), src/mutators/loop_boundary.zig (lines 24-30, 50-51, 67-93), src/mutant.zig (lines 191-228), src/ast_backend.zig (lines 149-163), test/ast_candidate_ordering_test.zig (lines 69-108). Grep confirmed no loop_boundary/comparison_boundary precedence entry in docs/MUTATOR_SPEC.md.

**Why it is wrong:** The spec functions as the authoritative governance document for operator overlap, and claims that a documented precedence rule must exist before two operators match the same span. The rule is implemented in code and tested, but not documented in the spec. An agent adding a new operator that also targets while-condition comparisons would read the spec, find no documented loop_boundary precedence, and either add a duplicate physical edit (inflating totals) or emit a no-op. The spec's own requirement is violated by the gap, making the governance section misleading.

**Impact & repro:** An agent or reviewer following the spec cannot determine from the spec alone that loop_boundary defers to comparison_boundary for while-condition boundary swaps. New operators targeting the same AST nodes have no documented guidance. The physical-edit dedup mechanism that enforces one-candidate-per-physical-edit is also undocumented in the spec, so an agent could add an operator that defeats the dedup (e.g., by using a different replacement text for the same source span) and introduce intentional or accidental duplicates that slip through.  
_Repro:_ Read docs/MUTATOR_SPEC.md section 'Operator Overlap and Precedence'. Observe that only the optional_null_check/equality_swap rule is listed. Run `grep -n 'loop_boundary\|comparison_boundary' docs/MUTATOR_SPEC.md` to confirm no precedence entry for the while-condition overlap. Then read src/mutators/comparison.zig and src/mutators/loop_boundary.zig to see both match `.less_than`/`.less_or_equal`/`.greater_than`/`.greater_or_equal` nodes including those inside while conditions.

**Suggested fix:** Add a precedence entry to the 'Operator Overlap and Precedence' section of MUTATOR_SPEC.md: 'While-loop condition boundary swaps are owned by comparison_boundary; loop_boundary does not emit a separate candidate for the same operator token in a while condition. The physical-edit deduplication in sortAndDedupe retains the comparison_boundary representative when both operators recognize the same (file, span, original, replacement) tuple.' Also document the physical-edit dedup mechanism as the general enforcement mechanism for undocumented overlaps.

**Lens verdicts:** CORRECTNESS: UPHELD, Zig semantics and safety: UPHELD, REPRODUCTION: REFUTED

### [L37] In-tree TOML parser silently accepts duplicate keys (first value wins) contrary to the TOML spec

- **Severity:** Low  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 2/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D7-errorsets
- **Location(s):** `src/config_toml.zig`, `src/config.zig`

**Evidence:**
```zig
`config_toml.parse` appends every `key = value` entry unconditionally with no duplicate detection:

  src/config_toml.zig:191  const value = try p.readValue();
  src/config_toml.zig:192  try entries.append(arena, .{ .section = section, .key = key, .value = value, .line = key_line });

Resolution then takes the FIRST matching entry:

  src/config.zig:157  fn find(self: Lookup, section: []const u8, key: []const u8) ?toml.Value {
  src/config.zig:158      for (self.doc.entries) |e| {
  src/config.zig:159          if (std.mem.eql(u8, e.section, section) and std.mem.eql(u8, e.key, key)) return e.value;
  src/config.zig:160      }

So a config containing e.g. `[test]` with `commands = [...]` specified twice silently uses the first occurrence; the second is ignored with no diagnostic. The module doc-comment (config_toml.zig:3-7) claims a deterministic subset where 'Anything outside this subset is a parse error,' but duplicate keys are neither rejected nor last-wins.
```

**Tool confirmation:** Read of src/config_toml.zig (full file) and src/config.zig:154-195 this session confirms no duplicate-key check in either the parser or the Lookup. `zig build`/`zig build test` exit 0 (ground truth) — this is silent acceptance, not a compile/type problem.

**Why it is wrong:** A user who accidentally sets the same key twice (e.g. two `commands` arrays, or two `enabled` mutator lists) gets the first value with no warning. For a mutation-testing tool this can silently change which commands run or which operators are enabled versus what the author last wrote, undermining the deterministic-config contract.

**Impact & repro:** Misconfiguration is silently resolved to first-wins rather than flagged. Low impact because it requires an authoring mistake and the result is deterministic, but it can cause a confusing mismatch between intent (typically last-wins expectation) and behavior, and it weakens `zentinel check` as a config oracle.  
_Repro:_ Create zentinel.toml with `[test]` then `commands = ["zig build test"]` followed on a later line by `commands = ["true"]`. Run `zentinel check`: it passes and the first `commands` value is used; the second is silently dropped. No ZNTL_CONFIG_* diagnostic is emitted for the duplicate.

**Suggested fix:** In `config_toml.parse`, before appending, reject a `(section, key)` pair already present with a `ParseError` (e.g. 'duplicate key'), or define and document last-wins explicitly. Surfacing it as ZNTL_CONFIG_PARSE_ERROR keeps `zentinel check` authoritative.

**Lens verdicts:** correctness: UPHELD, zig-semantics-safety: REFUTED, reproduction: UPHELD

---
### [L38] property_report failed_without_shrink branch / 'unsupported' shrink status are untested; a regression at L164 passes CI

- **Severity:** Low  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 2/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D8-tests
- **Location(s):** `src/property/report.zig:160-166`, `test/property_generator_test.zig:97-258`, `test/fixtures/pipeline/property_tests/invalid/failed_without_counterexample.json`, `test/fixtures/pipeline/property_tests/valid/failed_with_counterexample.json`, `test/fixtures/pipeline/property_tests/invalid/status_mismatch.json`, `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/property/report.zig`, `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/test/property_generator_test.zig`

**Evidence:**
```zig
src/property/report.zig:160-164: on a failed property, line 163 returns .failed_without_counterexample if no counterexample, THEN line 164 returns .failed_without_shrink if shrink_status is not in {minimized,unsupported}. To reach line 164 an input must be result==failed AND have a non-null counterexample AND shrink_status==not_triggered. I inspected every fixture with a failed property (Bash grep over valid/ and invalid/): only three exist -> valid/failed_with_counterexample.json (failed+minimized+counterexample => .ok, passes the isOneOf at 164), invalid/failed_without_counterexample.json (failed+not_triggered+counterexample:null => returns at 163 BEFORE 164), invalid/status_mismatch.json (failed+minimized+counterexample, status:passed => passes 164, fails at 170). No fixture has failed+counterexample+not_triggered. || report.zig:29 `shrink_statuses = {not_triggered, minimized, unsupported}` and L30 `failed_shrink_statuses = {minimized, unsupported}`. Bash grep across test/fixtures and artifacts/pipeline found NO property report JSON pairing `shrinking` with `"unsupported"` (the only `"unsupported"` hits are AIR/ZIR backend diagnostic artifacts, unrelated to shrink status). The valid failed fixture failed_with_counterexample.json uses `"status": "minimized"` (L20); passed reports use `not_triggered` (artifacts/pipeline/062/property/report.json). So `unsupported` is never accepted as a passing shrink status (L154 path) nor as a valid failed-shrink status (L164 path).
```

**Tool confirmation:** Bash loop over test/fixtures/pipeline/property_tests/{valid,invalid}/*.json printing status/result/counterexample/shrink-status: output shows exactly the three failed-property fixtures above and none with the not_triggered+counterexample combination. zig_ast_tests on test/property_generator_test.zig enumerated all 9 tests; the only tag-level Violation assertions are .ok, .failed_without_counterexample (line 144), .status_mismatch (line 176), .empty_property_required (line 190); the fixture-suite test (lines 238-257) only asserts `v != .ok` for invalid fixtures, never the specific tag, so it cannot pin failed_without_shrink either. || Bash: `grep -rB2 -A2 '"unsupported"' test/fixtures/pipeline/property_tests/ artifacts/pipeline/` returned only air-unsupported.json / zir-unsupported.json backend diagnostics; the per-file `grep -q shrink` filter over all `"unsupported"` files yielded zero hits, confirming no shrink fixture uses the value. zig_test_for_symbol on `validate` (confidence medium) returned the property-report validator's candidate tests; none reference an `unsupported` shrink status.

**Why it is wrong:** `unsupported` is a legitimate shrink-status per docs (shrinking infeasible for a property), and L164 must accept it for a FAILED report (a failed property whose shrink is `unsupported` is contractually valid). With no fixture, the only thing keeping that membership correct is the source itself; a regression deleting `unsupported` from failed_shrink_statuses (L30) would make valid `unsupported`-shrink failed reports incorrectly return `failed_without_shrink`, and no test would catch it.

**Impact & repro:** A regression that deletes line 164 (or weakens failed_shrink_statuses) would let a failed property report with a counterexample but shrink status 'not_triggered' pass the validator, silently accepting property evidence the contract intends to reject. zig build test stays green. Low impact because this gates internal pipeline metadata, not mutant generation/classification, and the broader rejection paths are exercised.  
_Repro:_ Add (mentally) a fixture failed+counterexample present+shrinking.status=not_triggered: current code returns .failed_without_shrink, but no test asserts it, so deleting the branch (returning .ok/continuing) produces no test failure. Confirmed no such fixture exists via the Bash fixture scan.

**Suggested fix:** Add one invalid fixture (e.g. invalid/failed_without_shrink.json) with result:failed, a non-null counterexample, and shrinking.status:"not_triggered", and assert prep.validate==.failed_without_shrink in test/property_generator_test.zig; also add it to the invalid_fixtures list. Optionally make the fixture-suite loop assert the expected specific Violation tag per fixture instead of only `!= .ok`.

**Lens verdicts:** correctness: UPHELD, zig-semantics-safety: REFUTED, reproduction: UPHELD

### [L39] Generator.intRange (and boolean/bytes) are untested dead public API; intRange carries a latent overflow/panic

- **Severity:** Low  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 2/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D8-tests, D9-arch
- **Location(s):** `src/property/generator.zig:27-49`, `test/property_generator_test.zig`, `test/support/property.zig:23-43`, `src/property/generator.zig`

**Evidence:**
```zig
src/property/generator.zig exports four methods on Generator: next (line 18), intRange (27-31), boolean (33-35), bytes (38-49). Bash grep across src/ and test/ for `intRange`, `.boolean(`, `.bytes(` returns ONLY the definitions in generator.zig -- zero callers anywhere. test/property_generator_test.zig and test/support/property.zig (forAllU64, line 24-27) use only Generator.init and next(). intRange:29 computes `const span: u64 = @intCast(hi - lo + 1)` and :30 `lo + @as(i64, @intCast(self.next() % span))`: for lo=minInt(i64),hi=maxInt(i64) the `hi - lo` subtraction overflows i64; for any range wider than half the i64 domain, `self.next() % span` can exceed maxInt(i64) so `@intCast(...)` to i64 panics in safe builds. || src/property/generator.zig:27: `pub fn intRange(self: *Generator, lo: i64, hi: i64) i64`. Grep of the full repo (`grep -rn '\.intRange\b' /Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/ --include='*.zig'`) returns only the definition itself. The module surface tool (zig_module_surface, confidence: medium, analysis_kind: parser_backed_module_surface) explicitly flags it in `unused_exports`. The test file `test/property_generator_test.zig` exercises `next()`, `boolean()`, and `bytes()` but never calls `intRange`. The test support harness `test/support/property.zig` uses only `next()`. No caller exists in src/ or test/.
```

**Tool confirmation:** Bash grep results: `intRange` -> only src/property/generator.zig:27; `.boolean(` -> (none); `.bytes(` -> (none); generator usage grep shows only Generator.init/next in test/property_generator_test.zig and test/support/property.zig:24. zig_ast_tests on test/property_generator_test.zig enumerated all 9 test bodies verbatim -> none reference intRange/boolean/bytes. The GROUND TRUTH UNSAFE/SAFETY section already independently flagged src/property/generator.zig:1 @truncate (the bytes() path) as an unchecked_integer_cast. || zig_module_surface unused_exports: [{"file": "src/property/generator.zig", "line": 27, "kind": "fn", "name": "intRange"}]. grep confirms single occurrence only at definition.

**Why it is wrong:** The `Generator` struct exports `intRange` as a public method for i64 range draws, but the test harness was built using raw `next()` calls, and no product code (mutation engine, property report, doctest) ever calls `intRange`. The method is live code that compiles and produces correct results, but it is architecturally dead: nothing in the test or production surface ever reaches it.

**Impact & repro:** Low: these methods are currently unused, so the latent intRange overflow cannot be hit in production today. But they are public API (exported via src/root.zig:40 property.generator) and untested, so any future caller (or a refactor that wires them into a real property harness) would inherit an unbounded-range panic with no test to catch it. Also a pure dead-code/coverage-truth gap: the generator's claimed surface is larger than what any test validates.  
_Repro:_ Call gen.Generator.init(0).intRange(std.math.minInt(i64), std.math.maxInt(i64)) -> `hi - lo + 1` overflows i64 (panic in safe modes). No test does this, so it is unguarded. Confirmed zero callers via Bash grep.

**Suggested fix:** Either delete the unused intRange/boolean/bytes methods (preferred if the project's property harness only needs next(), which support/property.zig confirms), or add direct unit tests in test/property_generator_test.zig that exercise intRange bounds (including lo==hi, and a guard/test for ranges where hi-lo+1 overflows u64/i64), boolean balance over many draws, and bytes() fill correctness; fix intRange to compute span in u64 from @as(u64,@bitCast(hi)) -% @as(u64,@bitCast(lo)) +% 1 and map back without an i64 intCast that can panic.

**Lens verdicts:** correctness: UPHELD, zig-semantics-safety: UPHELD, reproduction: REFUTED
