### [L40] Mutator killed/survivor fixtures assert only candidate emission, never the kill/survive outcome

- **Severity:** Low  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 2/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D8-tests
- **Location(s):** `test/mutators/error_path_test.zig:87-112`, `test/mutators/optional_test.zig:108-114`, `test/mutators/errdefer_test.zig:116-122`, `test/mutators/comparison_test.zig`, `tests/coverage-gaps/mutators.v1.json`

**Evidence:**
```zig
Bash grep: no file under test/mutators/ references sandbox.apply, mutant_runner, or `.run(` -- the mutator tests never apply a patch or classify a result. error_path_test.zig:87 'survivor fixture...' and :101 'killed fixture...' both only assert `c.len==1` and the candidate's operator/original (lines 96-98 vs 110-111) -- the two tests are identical in what they verify despite the killed-vs-survivor naming. mutators.v1.json notes for error_catch_unreachable/errdefer/optional claim 'killed/survived fixtures document the outcomes', but the tests do not run those outcomes. The kill/survive classification itself is covered separately by test/mutant_runner_test.zig (mock outcomes) and one real run in test/integration_run_test.zig:41 (total=3,killed=1,survived=2).
```

**Tool confirmation:** Bash greps: `grep -rln 'sandbox.apply|mutant_runner|\.run(' test/mutators/` -> empty; `grep -rn 'survived|killed|ResultStatus|MutationResult' test/mutators/` -> only test-name strings and fixture filenames, no status assertions. Read of error_path_test.zig:87-112 shows both fixture tests assert only candidate count + original text.

**Why it is wrong:** The dimension explicitly targets tests that 'assert on trivia' or 'never exercise the claimed branch'. The fixture names (killed.zig/survivor.zig) and the coverage-gaps registry imply outcome verification per operator, but the unit tests verify only generation; the killed-vs-survivor behavior is not asserted at the operator level.

**Impact & repro:** Low/cosmetic-to-moderate. Kill detection is genuinely tested (mutant_runner_test + the one integration run), so this is not an uncovered classifier branch. The gap is coupling coverage: only the error_catch_unreachable operator on calc.zig is proven end-to-end (apply+run+classify); no other stable operator is verified to actually produce its named kill/survive outcome when run against a real suite. A mutator change that still emits a correct candidate but applies to a wrong span (so the mutant no longer compiles/kills as intended) would not be caught by the mutator tests, only potentially by the single integration fixture.  
_Repro:_ Inspect test/mutators/error_path_test.zig:101-112 -> the 'killed fixture' test never runs the mutant; it asserts the same thing as the survivor test. Inspect Bash grep showing no apply/run in test/mutators/. The only operator with a real apply+run+classify assertion is error_catch_unreachable via test/integration_run_test.zig:108-111.

**Suggested fix:** For the operators whose registry notes promise killed/survived outcomes (error_catch_unreachable, errdefer_remove, optional_orelse_unreachable, arithmetic, comparison), add a small number of apply-and-classify tests that take the emitted candidate, call sandbox.apply, run it through mutant_runner.run with a mock executor reflecting the fixture's real test result, and assert the expected ResultStatus (killed for killed.zig, survived for survivor.zig). Alternatively, broaden the integration fixture to cover at least one of each stable operator end-to-end so the killed/survivor fixture names are actually validated.

**Lens verdicts:** correctness: UPHELD, zig-semantics-safety: REFUTED, reproduction: UPHELD

### [L41] Duplicate ISO-8601 timestamp logic in cli.zig (buildObservation does not reuse isoTimestamp)

- **Severity:** Low  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 2/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D9-arch
- **Location(s):** `src/cli.zig`

**Evidence:**
```zig
Two functionally identical timestamp-formatting code blocks exist in src/cli.zig. `isoTimestamp` (lines 801-810) extracts secs from ms, builds `EpochSeconds`, calls `calculateYearDay`/`calculateMonthDay`/`getDaySeconds`, and formats `"{d:0>4}-{d:0>2}-{d:0>2}T{d:0>2}:{d:0>2}:{d:0>2}Z"`. `buildObservation` (lines 315-323) performs the identical computation inline instead of calling `isoTimestamp`. Only `runDoctest` (line 1236) calls `isoTimestamp`; `runRun` (via `buildObservation`) re-implements it.
```

**Tool confirmation:** grep -n 'isoTimestamp' src/cli.zig returns lines 801 (definition) and 1236 (sole caller). Lines 315-323 of src/cli.zig contain the verbatim epoch arithmetic without delegating to `isoTimestamp`.

**Why it is wrong:** Any future change to the timestamp format (e.g., adding milliseconds, switching to UTC offset) must be applied in both places. The two run-paths (`run` vs `doctest`) can silently drift in timestamp representation. This is the kind of subtle inconsistency that never shows up as a test failure until a user compares two reports.

**Impact & repro:** Low-Medium. No current behavioral difference since both paths produce identical output. The risk is silent divergence on any future format change.  
_Repro:_ Read src/cli.zig lines 311-341 (`buildObservation`) and lines 801-810 (`isoTimestamp`); both compute the same ISO format from the same epoch arithmetic.

**Suggested fix:** Have `buildObservation` call `isoTimestamp(gpa, ts)` at line 321 instead of inlining the arithmetic. The function already takes `gpa` and is reachable from `buildObservation`'s call site.

**Lens verdicts:** correctness: UPHELD, zig-semantics-safety: UPHELD, reproduction: REFUTED

### [L42] isQuotedMeta is a trivially thin wrapper that always equals isMeta

- **Severity:** Low  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 2/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D9-arch
- **Location(s):** `src/command.zig`

**Evidence:**
```zig
src/command.zig:47-49: `fn isQuotedMeta(c: u8) bool { return isMeta(c); }`. The function body is a single unconditional delegation to `isMeta`. It is called at line 84 within the quoted-field parsing branch. The zig_dead_decl_candidates tool flags it as a candidate.
```

**Tool confirmation:** grep of command.zig confirms isQuotedMeta at line 47 returns `isMeta(c)` unchanged, and is called at exactly line 84. No test exercises a path where quoted-field metacharacter handling would differ from unquoted-field handling.

**Why it is wrong:** This is intentional abstraction headroom (in case quoted-field rules diverge), but the comment at src/command.zig:39-44 already explains the current policy is intentionally uniform. The existence of `isQuotedMeta` without any behavioral difference creates indirection overhead and implies a distinction that currently does not exist.

**Impact & repro:** Low (pure style). Negligible. The compiler inlines this call. The risk is that a future author changes `isMeta` without noticing `isQuotedMeta` exists (or vice versa), unintentionally creating a divergence.  
_Repro:_ Read src/command.zig:36-49. `isMeta` and `isQuotedMeta` are identical in behavior.

**Suggested fix:** Either (a) inline `isMeta(c)` at line 84 and delete `isQuotedMeta`, adding a comment explaining that quoted-field metacharacter rules are currently identical to unquoted; or (b) add a code comment to `isQuotedMeta` explicitly stating it currently delegates to `isMeta` and when it would diverge.

**Lens verdicts:** correctness: UPHELD, zig-semantics-safety: UPHELD, reproduction: REFUTED

### [L44] --verbose and --quiet can be passed together to `run` without error; quiet silently wins

- **Severity:** Low  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 2/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D11-cli
- **Location(s):** `src/run_command.zig`, `src/cli.zig`

**Evidence:**
```zig
src/run_command.zig:160-163: both --verbose and --quiet set independent bool fields on Options without conflict detection. src/cli.zig:580: 'if (options.quiet) .quiet else if (options.verbose) .verbose else .normal' -- quiet takes precedence silently. No error is emitted when both flags are present. The parseArgs function (run_command.zig:153-213) has no mutual-exclusion check.
```

**Tool confirmation:** Code read of src/run_command.zig:160-163 and src/cli.zig:579-581.

**Why it is wrong:** A user who accidentally writes zentinel run --verbose --quiet receives quietly-filtered output with no indication that --verbose was ignored. Violates the principle of least surprise.

**Impact & repro:** Silent behavioral surprise: user asked for verbose output but gets quiet output. Low severity since this requires both flags to be explicitly passed.  
_Repro:_ Run zentinel run --verbose --quiet. Output is identical to --quiet alone with no warning.

**Suggested fix:** Add a check in parseArgs: if both opts.verbose and opts.quiet are true after parsing, return error.ConflictingOptions with message '--verbose and --quiet are mutually exclusive'.

**Lens verdicts:** correctness: UPHELD, zig-semantics-safety: REFUTED, reproduction: UPHELD

### [L45] zig.modes = [] is accepted by config validation but silently overrides the user's intent to run Debug

- **Severity:** Low  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 2/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D11-cli
- **Location(s):** `src/config.zig`, `src/safety_modes.zig`

**Evidence:**
```zig
config.zig:335-339: `const zig_modes = try look.getArray("zig", "modes", &.{"Debug"}, diag);` with no length check after the per-element validation loop. An explicitly written `modes = []` in TOML returns `string_array = &.{}` from the parser, passes the for loop (zero iterations), and stores an empty slice in Config.zig_modes. safety_modes.matrixModes (safety_modes.zig:62-83): when no mode is present in the config set (count == 0 at line 70), it silently inserts .Debug (line 71). zentinel check passes without error for a config containing `modes = []`.
```

**Tool confirmation:** Direct code read of config.zig:335-339 confirms no `if (zig_modes.len == 0) return fail(...)` guard. Direct code read of safety_modes.zig:70-73 confirms the silent Debug fallback. No test in test/ exercises `modes = []` (grep returns zero hits).

**Why it is wrong:** The TOML spec and the config default template both imply `modes` should be non-empty (`modes = ["Debug"]` is the default). Explicit `modes = []` is meaningless user intent that the system silently redirects to Debug. Unlike omitting `modes` entirely (which correctly uses the default), an explicit empty array has no sensible semantics and should be rejected. This also diverges from the behavior for `test.commands = []` which is correctly rejected at config.zig:363.

**Impact & repro:** A user who accidentally writes `modes = []` in zentinel.toml gets silent Debug-only behavior. Since `zentinel check` passes, they receive no feedback. Consistent with how `test.commands = []` is handled, an empty `modes` should produce a config validation error.  
_Repro:_ Write `zentinel.toml` with `[zig]\nmodes = []`. Run `zentinel check`. Output: 'check: configuration and environment OK'. Run `zentinel run`. Runs in Debug mode despite the empty modes list.

**Suggested fix:** Add a length check after the per-element validation loop in config.zig: `if (zig_modes.len == 0) return fail(diag, .invalid_value, "zig", "modes", "modes must not be empty");`. This is consistent with the existing check for test.commands at line 363.

**Lens verdicts:** correctness: UPHELD, zig-semantics-safety: REFUTED, reproduction: UPHELD

### [L46] benchmark.sh emits a committed static fixture, not live benchmark measurements

- **Severity:** Low  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 2/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D12-build
- **Location(s):** `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/scripts/benchmark.sh`, `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/test/fixtures/performance/benchmark.json`

**Evidence:**
```zig
benchmark.sh line 14: 'cat test/fixtures/performance/benchmark.json'. The script header says 'emits the machine-readable, normalized benchmark output for trend comparison'. The actual benchmark.json is a committed static file with hardcoded zero-duration equivalences (equivalence.cached_uncached=true, serial_parallel=true, cold_warm=true) generated from the mock executor in performance_benchmark_test.zig line 39: run_id='run_bench00000000000000', duration_ms=0. The zig build test step (line 11 of benchmark.sh) runs a snapshot test (performance_benchmark_test.zig line 163: expectEqualStrings(benchmark_snapshot, json)) that verifies the committed file matches the mock-executor output — it does not regenerate the file from a real Zig compiler invocation.
```

**Tool confirmation:** Read /Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/test/fixtures/performance/benchmark.json: all fields are hardcoded (mutants=3, all equivalences true, no timing fields). Read performance_benchmark_test.zig lines 38-43: observation() uses run_id='run_bench00000000000000', duration_ms=0, pass()/fail() use duration_ms=0. Line 163: expectEqualStrings(benchmark_snapshot, json) validates committed snapshot, not a live run.

**Why it is wrong:** A user or CI job running benchmark.sh for trend comparison would receive the same committed JSON every run, regardless of actual wall-clock performance. Regressions in compilation time, cache efficiency, or parallelism are undetectable from the script output. The script's stated purpose ('trend comparison') is not achieved: the output carries no timing signal.

**Impact & repro:** Benchmark regressions are undetectable via this script. CI infrastructure that collects benchmark.sh output for trend databases would store the same static numbers permanently. The script provides a false sense of performance monitoring.  
_Repro:_ Run scripts/benchmark.sh twice on different machines with different I/O speeds. Observe: benchmark output is identical both times regardless of actual performance.

**Suggested fix:** Either (a) remove the 'trend comparison' claim from the benchmark.sh comment and clarify it validates benchmark logic correctness only, or (b) add a real execution step that actually runs the zentinel binary against the dogfood fixture and measures wall-clock time, emitting those measurements after the snapshot test. Option (a) is the safe, minimal fix.

**Lens verdicts:** correctness: UPHELD, zig-semantics-safety: REFUTED, reproduction: UPHELD

### [L47] release_acceptance.py reads release_evidence.json without an is_file() guard -> uncaught FileNotFoundError

- **Severity:** Low  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 2/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D12-build
- **Location(s):** `scripts/release_acceptance.py`

**Evidence:**
```zig
Line 99: json.loads((ROOT / "test/fixtures/release/valid/release_evidence.json").read_text(encoding="utf-8")) — no is_file() check, no try/except. If the file is absent, Python raises FileNotFoundError and the script terminates with a traceback. The corresponding rdg.main() path at lines 219-233 does handle the missing case gracefully: 'if DEFAULT_MANIFEST.is_file(): ... else: failed=True; print("release-gate: missing manifest ...")'. But that branch is never reached because check_criteria() crashes first.
```

**Tool confirmation:** Read of /Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/scripts/release_acceptance.py line 99 confirmed the bare .read_text() call. Comparison with rdg.main() lines 219-233 (also read) confirms the graceful is_file() guard exists there but is absent in check_criteria(). The _read() helper at line 57 shows the project does use is_file() guards elsewhere ('return p.read_text(encoding="utf-8") if p.is_file() else ""'), confirming the omission in check_criteria() is inconsistent with the project's own pattern.

**Why it is wrong:** release_acceptance.py is intended to be the final acceptance gate for task 060. Running it before the release evidence is prepared (the normal pre-release state) should produce a deterministic 'FAILED: missing manifest' message. Instead it produces a Python traceback that does not clearly identify the missing file to an automated log scanner. The is_file() guard on rdg.main() at line 219 was the deliberate design; omitting it from check_criteria() is an oversight.

**Impact & repro:** Any run of release_acceptance.py before test/fixtures/release/valid/release_evidence.json is committed produces an uncaught FileNotFoundError traceback instead of the expected structured 'acceptance: final_dogfood_gate: FAILED' + 'acceptance: release NOT accepted' output. CI exit code is still non-zero (Python exits 1 on uncaught exception), so the gate does not silently pass, but the diagnostic output is unstructured.  
_Repro:_ Temporarily rename test/fixtures/release/valid/release_evidence.json. Run python3 scripts/release_acceptance.py. Observe FileNotFoundError traceback instead of 'acceptance: final_dogfood_gate: FAILED (...)' + 'acceptance: missing acceptance manifest'.

**Suggested fix:** Guard the read in check_criteria() with an is_file() check, matching the rdg.main() pattern: evidence_path = ROOT / 'test/fixtures/release/valid/release_evidence.json'; if not evidence_path.is_file(): return {cid: (False, 'release_evidence.json missing') for cid in REQUIRED_CRITERIA}. Alternatively use a try/except FileNotFoundError block and return a dict of failing results.

**Lens verdicts:** correctness: UPHELD, zig-semantics-safety: UPHELD, reproduction: REFUTED

### [L49] validate_failure_recovery self-test silently skips non-dict invalid fixtures

- **Severity:** Low  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 2/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D12-build
- **Location(s):** `scripts/validate_task_system.py`

**Evidence:**
```zig
validate_task_system.py lines 1757-1765: the invalid fixture loop calls _load_json_or_none(fx), then `if not isinstance(data, dict): continue` silently skips non-dict JSON files. A JSON array or scalar in invalid/ is neither validated nor flagged as a problem. The valid fixture loop at lines 1751-1756 calls `fail(errors, ...)` for non-dict files, making the discrepancy visible.
```

**Tool confirmation:** Read of validate_task_system.py lines 1740-1765 confirmed the silent continue at line 1763 vs. the fail() call in the valid loop at line 1753.

**Why it is wrong:** An accidental non-dict JSON file in invalid/ passes the self-test silently (it is neither rejected as required nor flagged as a problem), hiding fixture authoring errors.

**Impact & repro:** Self-test coverage gap for failure-recovery fixtures. No product behavior affected. An invalid fixture that is a non-dict passes the self-test silently.  
_Repro:_ Create test/fixtures/pipeline/failure_recovery_validator/invalid/bad.json containing `[]`. Run `python3 scripts/validate_task_system.py`. The file is silently skipped with no diagnostic.

**Suggested fix:** Replace the `continue` at line 1763 with an explicit fail/append: `fail(errors, f"{rel}: invalid failure-recovery fixture must be a JSON object")`, consistent with the valid fixture loop.

**Lens verdicts:** correctness: UPHELD, zig-semantics-safety: REFUTED, reproduction: UPHELD

### [S1] Doctest survivor AI context leaks operator/survivor_ref/case_id/mutant_id unredacted (doctest_command.zig)

- **Severity:** Low  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 1/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D6-safety
- **Location(s):** `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/ai/doctest_command.zig`

**Evidence:**
```zig
In buildSurvivorContextValue, the file and source_ref ARE redacted -- doctest_command.zig:1095 `.file = try context.redactField(arena, s(get(case, "file")), patterns, &log),` and :1096 `.source_ref = if (optStr(get(case, "source_ref"))) |sr| try context.redactField(...) else null,` -- but four sibling fields are passed raw: :1092 `.survivor_ref = s(get(mutation, "survivor_ref")),`, :1099 `.case_id = s(get(case, "id")),`, :1100 `.mutant_id = s(get(mutation, "mutant_id")),`, :1101 `.operator = s(get(mutation, "operator")),`. The survivor validator validateSurvivorContext only does unbounded prefix checks -- :1138 `startsWith(... survivor_ref ..., "ds_")`, :1143 `startsWith(... case_id ..., "dm_")`, :1144 `startsWith(... mutant_id ..., "m_")` -- which constrain only the first few bytes and leave the rest of the string free; `operator` has NO check at all. The context is then serialized whole into the prompt (buildSurvivorPromptValue :1164-1173) and shipped. None of these four fields are added to the RedactionLog, so privacy.redactions_applied under-reports.
```

**Tool confirmation:** Bash sed over doctest_command.zig:1091-1108 confirmed the redactField calls land only on `.file` and `.source_ref`, while survivor_ref/case_id/mutant_id/operator use bare `s(get(...))`. GROUND TRUTH build+test are clean (exit 0, zero diagnostics), so this is live behavior on Zig 0.16.0.

**Why it is wrong:** Prior finding 3 named `mutant.id` and `operator` bypassing redaction in src/ai/command.zig (the MUTATION explain/suggest flow). This is a separate module (src/ai/doctest_command.zig) and the separate task-067 doctest-SURVIVOR flow with its own builder (buildSurvivorContextValue) and its own validator (validateSurvivorContext). The survivor `operator` here has zero structural guard, and the `ds_`/`dm_`/`m_` prefix checks give a false sense of containment because the suffix is arbitrary.

**Impact & repro:** An untrusted `zentinel doctest --mutate` report fed to the survivor explain path can carry a path or secret in the suffix of `mutation.survivor_ref`/`id`/`mutation.mutant_id` (e.g. `m_<...>/Users/victim/...`) or anywhere in `mutation.operator`; it reaches the provider verbatim while privacy.redactions_applied claims completeness. Lower reach than Finding A because it only affects the doctest-survivor subcommand, but the same leak + false-accounting class.  
_Repro:_ Build a doctest-mutate report whose case has status "survived" and `mutation = { "survivor_ref": "ds_x/Users/victim/secret", "mutant_id": "m_x sk-secret", "operator": "/abs/leak literal", ... runner_evidence ... }`. Invoke the survivor explain entrypoint (doctest_command.runSurvivor) with `--input-report`. The serialized survivor context echoes those raw values and redactions_applied does not list them. Static confirmation via the cited lines is conclusive.

**Suggested fix:** Wrap survivor_ref, case_id, mutant_id, and operator in context.redactField(arena, ..., patterns, &log) in buildSurvivorContextValue (the function already has patterns and &log in scope), mirroring how .file/.source_ref are handled. Apply the same to the mutation explain/suggest `id`/`operator` fields in command.zig:466,470,503 if not already tracked under the prior finding.

**Lens verdicts:** CORRECTNESS: REFUTED, Zig-semantics/safety: slice/pointer lifetimes, arena scope, value provenance, comptime-vs-runtime string handling, redaction-primitive behavior.: REFUTED, REPRODUCTION: UPHELD

### [S2] property_report rejection loop asserts only v != .ok, never the intended violation tag -> misrouted/masked violations pass CI

- **Severity:** Low  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 1/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D8-tests
- **Location(s):** `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/test/property_generator_test.zig`, `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/property/report.zig`, `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/test/fixtures/pipeline/property_tests/invalid/bad_invariant_category.json`, `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/test/fixtures/pipeline/property_tests/invalid/missing_seed.json`

**Evidence:**
```zig
src/property/report.zig defines a 19-member `Violation` enum (lines 34-54) and `validate()` returns ~18 distinct tags. The fixture-driven test (test/property_generator_test.zig:238-257) iterates 8 invalid fixtures but the only assertion is line 256 `try std.testing.expect(v != .ok);` — it never checks WHICH violation each fixture triggers. Exact-value `prep.Violation.<tag>` asserts in the whole file are only: ok, failed_without_counterexample (L144), status_mismatch (L176), empty_property_required (L190) (confirmed via `grep -n 'prep\.Violation\.' test/property_generator_test.zig`). So the branches that bad_invariant_category.json (invariant "Vibes" → intends `bad_invariant`, report.zig:125), missing_seed.json (empty seeds → intends `missing_seeds`, report.zig:133), missing_generator_summary.json (`missing_generator`, report.zig:142-148), missing_invariant.json (`bad_invariant`), and missing_shrinking_status.json (`bad_shrinking`, report.zig:153) are SUPPOSED to exercise are never pinned to a tag.
```

**Tool confirmation:** zig_ast_tests on test/property_generator_test.zig (parser_backed, confidence high, parse_status ok, 0 parse errors) enumerated exactly 9 tests and returned the verbatim body of the loop test at line 238 showing its sole invalid-branch assertion is `try std.testing.expect(v != .ok)`. Bash grep `grep -rohn 'Violation\.[a-z_]*' test/` aggregated tag asserts: for the property-report validator only ok/failed_without_counterexample/status_mismatch/empty_property_required are pinned by exact value.

**Why it is wrong:** A test that asserts only 'not ok' verifies the validator rejects SOMETHING, not that it rejects for the RIGHT reason. The validator returns early on the first violation, so two failure modes regress silently: (a) a change that makes an earlier check (e.g. bad_invariant at L125) spuriously fire would mask a later check (e.g. missing_seeds at L133) yet the fixture still rejects; (b) any refactor that returns the wrong Violation tag breaks the documented stable-tag contract (report.zig:33 'Tags are stable so callers and tests can assert the precise failure mode') with no test catching it.

**Impact & repro:** The discrimination logic of the property-evidence gate — the part that tells a pipeline operator WHY property evidence was rejected — is effectively untested for 5 of 8 negative fixtures. Mutations to the per-property validation order or the returned tags survive `zig build test`.  
_Repro:_ Open test/property_generator_test.zig:238-257; the invalid_fixtures loop has no expected-tag table and asserts only `v != .ok` at line 256. Contrast with report.zig:33 which promises tags are stable for tests to assert precise failure modes — that promise is unkept for these fixtures.

**Suggested fix:** Replace the `invalid_fixtures: [_][]const u8` array with a `[_]struct{ name, expected: prep.Violation }` table and assert `expectEqual(expected, prep.validate(value))` per fixture, mirroring how the doctest validator tests pin exact ResponseViolation/ContextViolation values.

**Lens verdicts:** CORRECTNESS: REFUTED, Zig-semantics/safety: REFUTED, REPRODUCTION: UPHELD

### [S3] SHA-256 of each source file recomputed once per mutant in the Phase C hot loop

- **Severity:** Low  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 1/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D10-perf
- **Location(s):** `src/run_command.zig`

**Evidence:**
```zig
src/run_command.zig:350: `source_hash = try cache.sourceHash(arena, job.source)` is inside the `for (jobs, results, 0..)` loop that iterates over every mutant. Multiple mutants share the same `job.source` (they all come from the same file); each hashes the entire file contents independently. A 10 KB file with 50 mutants runs SHA-256 on 10 KB x 50 = 500 KB of data instead of 10 KB.
```

**Tool confirmation:** Confirmed by direct read of src/run_command.zig lines 330–360. `cache.sourceHash` at src/cache.zig:47 runs a full `Sha256.hash(content, &digest, .{})` then hex-encodes and arena-dups 64 bytes. No memoisation exists; every iteration of the Phase C loop (one per mutant) pays the full SHA-256 cost over the whole file content.

**Why it is wrong:** Files with many mutants cause the same bytes to be hashed repeatedly. The result is always identical (same source, same hash) but the work is repeated for each mutant rather than being computed once per unique file and reused.

**Impact & repro:** For a typical project with F source files and M mutants spread over those files, Phase C performs O(M) SHA-256 hash calls instead of O(F). When a single heavily-mutated file has hundreds of operators applied, all CPU time and arena allocations for that file's hash are multiplied by the mutant count. With multi-KB files and hundreds of mutants per file this is measurable wall-clock overhead even though Phase C is otherwise cheap (no process spawning).  
_Repro:_ Add a large source file with many arithmetic operators; run `zentinel run --report json`. Instrument `cache.sourceHash` with a call counter; it will be called once per mutant, not once per file.

**Suggested fix:** Build a `std.StringHashMap([]const u8)` (file path -> hex hash) before the Phase C loop by iterating over `files` once. Then look up `file_hash_map.get(job.candidate.file)` inside the loop instead of calling `cache.sourceHash(arena, job.source)`. Alternatively, store the precomputed per-file hash alongside `FileSource` in a companion slice constructed after `generateCandidates` returns.

**Lens verdicts:** CORRECTNESS: REFUTED, Zig-semantics/safety: UPHELD, REPRODUCTION: REFUTED

---
### [S4] build.zig: silent zero-test build when test/ is inaccessible (catch return swallows openDir error)

- **Severity:** Low  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 1/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D12-build
- **Location(s):** `build.zig`

**Evidence:**
```zig
build.zig line 112: `var test_dir = b.build_root.handle.openDir(io, "test", .{ .iterate = true }) catch return;` — if `test/` is missing or unreadable (permissions, wrong cwd), `addDiscoveredTests` returns immediately with count=0. The test_step then has only the fixture check (line 38) and the integration test (line 46) wired. `zig build test` exits 0, printing something like `Test [1/2] ... passed.` with no indication the 62 unit tests were silently dropped.
```

**Tool confirmation:** Ground-truth confirms `zig build test` passes (exit 0, 12.3s, 0 errors). `find test -name '*_test.zig' | grep -v integration_run_test.zig | wc -l` = 62 test files that would all be lost on openDir failure.

**Why it is wrong:** The `catch return` idiom silently degrades CI coverage: a directory-not-found or permission error is treated identically to a clean (but empty) result. Any subsequent `zig build test` invocation reports pass while running 62 fewer tests than expected.

**Impact & repro:** A developer or CI system that accidentally invokes `zig build test` with a wrong build root or after a partial repository checkout would see green with no mutations covered by unit tests. Zero-test passing CI is the classic false-confidence footgun.  
_Repro:_ Temporarily rename `test/` to `test_bak/` and run `zig build test` — it exits 0 without running any of the 62 discovered unit tests.

**Suggested fix:** Replace `catch return` with `catch @panic("test/ directory not found or unreadable: zig build test cannot discover tests")`. Alternatively, after the walker loop add `if (count == 0) @panic("no test/**/*_test.zig files discovered; check working directory")` to guard against the silent-zero case independently.

**Lens verdicts:** CORRECTNESS: UPHELD, ZIG-SEMANTICS/SAFETY: REFUTED, REPRODUCTION: REFUTED

---
### [S5] release_dogfood_gate.py self_test()/main() crash with unhandled JSONDecodeError on a malformed manifest

- **Severity:** Low  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 1/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D12-build
- **Location(s):** `scripts/release_dogfood_gate.py`

**Evidence:**
```zig
Lines 199, 208 (self_test) and 223 (main) call json.loads() with no try/except guard. By contrast, _reports_normalized_equal (lines 76-79) correctly wraps its json.loads in try/except (OSError, json.JSONDecodeError). Confirmed by reading the full file.
```

**Tool confirmation:** Read of scripts/release_dogfood_gate.py confirmed: lines 199, 208, 223 have bare json.loads calls; grep for JSONDecodeError/try/except (Bash) showed no guard at those sites. Line 79 shows the guarded pattern is already known to the author.

**Why it is wrong:** If test/fixtures/release/valid/release_evidence.json is malformed (partial write, truncation, or accidental edit), main() at line 223 raises an unhandled json.JSONDecodeError that propagates as a Python traceback rather than a diagnostic 'release-gate: ...' message. Similarly, a malformed fixture under valid/ or invalid/ crashes self_test() before it can report a structured problem. Since release_dogfood_gate.py is wired into ci.sh stage 7 (a hard CI gate), a JSON parse crash appears in CI as an unstructured exception rather than a clear gate failure.

**Impact & repro:** CI stage 7 (release_dogfood_gate) crashes with an unhandled Python exception rather than printing a structured diagnostic when the release evidence manifest or any fixture JSON file is malformed. The already-reported FileNotFoundError finding covers the file-not-found code path; this covers the malformed-JSON code path, a distinct failure mode not previously reported.  
_Repro:_ Truncate or corrupt test/fixtures/release/valid/release_evidence.json to invalid JSON, then run `python3 scripts/release_dogfood_gate.py`. The script exits with a json.JSONDecodeError traceback instead of printing 'release-gate: ...' diagnostic lines and returning exit code 1.

**Suggested fix:** Wrap the three bare json.loads call sites in try/except json.JSONDecodeError, following the existing pattern in _reports_normalized_equal. For line 223 in main(): catch the exception, print a structured 'release-gate: malformed manifest JSON: ...' message, set failed=True, and continue. For lines 199/208 in self_test(): catch and append a problem string to problems[] instead of propagating.

**Lens verdicts:** CORRECTNESS: REFUTED, Zig-semantics/safety: REFUTED, REPRODUCTION: UPHELD

### [S6] MUTATOR_SPEC documents error_catch_unreachable as 'compiles' but code emits 'may_fail'

- **Severity:** Low  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 1/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D13-docs
- **Location(s):** `docs/MUTATOR_SPEC.md`, `src/mutators/error_path.zig`, `test/mutators/error_path_test.zig`

**Evidence:**
```zig
MUTATOR_SPEC.md line 250: 'Compile expectation | `compiles` in normal expression contexts.' But `src/mutators/error_path.zig:77` emits `.expected_compile = .may_fail` for every `error_catch_unreachable` candidate. The code comment at `error_path.zig:85` explains why: 'removing the only use of a captured resource can make it unused.' The test at `test/mutators/error_path_test.zig:38` confirms the code behavior: `try expectEqual(mutant.ExpectedCompile.may_fail, c[0].expected_compile);`. The spec says `compiles`; the code, test, and code comment all say `may_fail`.
```

**Tool confirmation:** Read src/mutators/error_path.zig lines 77 and 85 directly; Read docs/MUTATOR_SPEC.md lines 241-251 directly; Read test/mutators/error_path_test.zig line 38 directly. All three confirm the discrepancy.

**Why it is wrong:** `expected_compile` is a public field emitted in every JSON report entry (src/run_command.zig:665 copies it from the candidate). Agents and integrations that read the spec to predict which `error_catch_unreachable` mutants will produce `compile_error` vs succeed will be misled: the spec predicts `compiles` (no compile error), but the emitted field is `may_fail`, meaning the tool does NOT guarantee these mutants compile. A `compile_error` result for an `error_catch_unreachable` mutant is therefore semantically valid, even though the spec implies it should not occur in normal contexts.

**Impact & repro:** Any agent or tool that trusts MUTATOR_SPEC to route `error_catch_unreachable` compile errors as unexpected tool defects rather than expected `may_fail` outcomes will misclassify them. The schema allows all three values so there is no JSON-level rejection, but the documented contract ('compiles') contradicts emitted evidence ('may_fail') in every report containing this operator.  
_Repro:_ Run `zentinel run` on any source containing `expr catch handler` where removing the handler creates an unused-variable compile failure. The emitted report entry has `expected_compile: 'may_fail'` while MUTATOR_SPEC.md predicts `compiles`.

**Suggested fix:** Update MUTATOR_SPEC.md `error_catch_unreachable` 'Compile expectation' row to match the code: change 'compiles in normal expression contexts' to 'may_fail; removing a catch handler can make a captured variable unused, causing a compile error'. No code change is needed — the code and test are correct.

**Lens verdicts:** CORRECTNESS: UPHELD, Zig-semantics/safety: REFUTED, REPRODUCTION: REFUTED

---
### [S7] Sole e2e kill/survive test binds only fungible aggregate counts; an add<->mul classification swap passes CI silently

- **Severity:** Low  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 1/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D8-tests
- **Location(s):** `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/test/integration_run_test.zig`, `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/test/fixtures/integration/sample/calc.zig`, `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/test/fixtures/integration/sample/zentinel.toml`

**Evidence:**
```zig
integration_run_test.zig:41 is the only test that drives the REAL built binary's kill-vs-survive decision via actual `zig test` (mock-executor unit tests script the outcome themselves). The fixture (calc.zig) yields exactly 3 mutants: add's arithmetic_add_sub (should be KILLED by the same-file test), mul's arithmetic_mul_div (should SURVIVE), and parsePositive's error_catch_unreachable (should SURVIVE). The test asserts only aggregate counts at lines 96-99: total==3, killed==1, survived==2, invalid==0. The per-mutant loop at lines 104-114 inspects ONLY the operator=="error_catch_unreachable" entry (asserts status survived, original "0"). Neither arithmetic mutant is bound to a specific status: there is no assertion that the arithmetic_add_sub mutant is killed nor that arithmetic_mul_div survives.
```

**Tool confirmation:** Read integration_run_test.zig lines 96-114 (count-only asserts + error_catch-only per-mutant check). Read fixture calc.zig and zentinel.toml confirming enabled = [arithmetic_add_sub, arithmetic_mul_div, error_catch_unreachable] and same-file test command `zig test calc.zig`. GT: `zig build test` includes addIntegrationTest which spawns the real exe; exit 0.

**Why it is wrong:** killed==1/survived==2 is a symmetric count: if a real-classifier regression caused add's mutant to survive (false negative on kill-detection) AND mul's mutant to be reported killed, the totals stay 1 killed / 2 survived and the test still passes. Kill-detection correctness (the product's core promise) is therefore only loosely pinned end-to-end; the precise add->killed / mul->survived mapping is asserted nowhere against the real binary.

**Impact & repro:** A genuine kill-detection regression that swaps which arithmetic mutant is caught vs missed is invisible to CI. Given this is the single real-binary kill/survive test, a false-negative survivor (mutant should be killed but is reported survived) can hide behind the unchanged aggregate count.  
_Repro:_ Inspect integration_run_test.zig: the only per-mutant status assertions (lines 110-111) are gated on operator=="error_catch_unreachable"; the arithmetic_add_sub and arithmetic_mul_div mutants are covered only by the summary counts at lines 96-99, which are invariant under an add<->mul status swap.

**Suggested fix:** In the per-mutant loop, additionally assert the status of each arithmetic mutant by (operator, file/function or span): require the arithmetic_add_sub mutant on `add` to be .killed and the arithmetic_mul_div mutant on `mul` to be .survived, so the end-to-end test pins the actual kill/survive mapping rather than a fungible count.

**Lens verdicts:** correctness: UPHELD, zig-semantics-safety: REFUTED, reproduction: REFUTED

---
### [S8] cli.zig is a 1431-line god-file spanning six distinct concerns

- **Severity:** Low  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 1/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D9-arch
- **Location(s):** `src/cli.zig`

**Evidence:**
```zig
src/cli.zig is 1431 lines and contains 33 functions covering: (1) top-level routing/passthrough (lines 14-144); (2) process execution and workspace setup (lines 145-341); (3) `runRun` — 175-line run-command I/O adapter (lines 424-598); (4) `runListMutants` — 153-line adapter (lines 599-751); (5) `runDoctest` — 118-line doctest adapter plus 90-line `runDoctestMutate` (lines 1172-1431); (6) three separate AI-command functions — `runAiCommand` (87 lines), `runDoctestAi` (122 lines), `runDoctestSurvivorAi` (80 lines) — plus their shared `aiSettings`/`aiOptionError` helpers (lines 820-1171). The file comment calls it a "thin presentation adapter" but it encapsulates the complete I/O adapter for every command.
```

**Tool confirmation:** wc -l src/cli.zig returns 1431. Function listing via grep returns 33 distinct fn/pub fn declarations. The function spans computed above (runRun: 175 lines, runListMutants: 153 lines, runDoctestAi: 122 lines, runDoctest: 118 lines, runDoctestMutate: 90 lines, runDoctestSurvivorAi: 80 lines) confirm six independently testable concerns are co-located.

**Why it is wrong:** Each `run*` function is tested via a different test file (run_command_test, list_mutants_command_test, cli_test, ai_commands_test, ai_doctest_test, etc.), confirming they are logically independent. Extracting per-command adapters would make each independently readable and allow test isolation without the shared `RunCtx` / `WorkspaceCtx` types leaking across concerns. The architecture doc (ARCHITECTURE.md:89) states "CLI modules route commands; they do not own mutation semantics" — cli.zig does not own mutation semantics, but it does own workspace construction, process spawning, and ISO timestamp formatting, which are more than routing.

**Impact & repro:** Low (no runtime defect). High cognitive load: any reviewer or future contributor must understand all six domains to safely modify any one. The shared `RunCtx` struct (lines 151-167) is implicitly shared state that all six concerns must understand.  
_Repro:_ Read src/cli.zig from line 1 to 1431. Note that `execProcess`, `baselineRunFn`, `workspaceRunFn`, `setupWorkspace`, and `RunCtx` are used only by `runRun` and `runListMutants` (and indirectly by the doctest mutate path), while the AI functions share only `aiSettings` and `openEffectiveProjectRoot`.

**Suggested fix:** Extract the per-command I/O adapters into sibling files: `src/adapters/run.zig`, `src/adapters/list_mutants.zig`, `src/adapters/doctest.zig`, `src/adapters/ai.zig`. `cli.zig` then becomes a true thin router of ~150 lines. This is a refactor task, not a bug fix; it does not change any observable behavior.

**Lens verdicts:** correctness: UPHELD, zig-semantics-safety: REFUTED, reproduction: REFUTED

### [S9] cli.zig private config_path duplicates root.zig's exported config_default_path

- **Severity:** Low  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 1/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D9-arch
- **Location(s):** `src/cli.zig`, `src/root.zig`

**Evidence:**
```zig
src/cli.zig:5 — `const config_path = "zentinel.toml";`. src/root.zig:368 — `pub const config_default_path = "zentinel.toml";`. The Globals struct at root.zig:373 uses `config_default_path` as its default: `config_path: []const u8 = config_default_path`. `cli.zig` never references `zentinel.config_default_path`; it carries a private copy of the literal string. `grep -rn '"zentinel\.toml"' src/` returns exactly these two lines and no others.
```

**Tool confirmation:** grep -rn '"zentinel\.toml"' /Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/ returned two hits: src/cli.zig:5 and src/root.zig:368. Zero callers of zentinel.config_default_path exist in src/cli.zig or any test/ file.

**Why it is wrong:** When `runPassthrough` probes config existence (cli.zig:69) and writes the init config (cli.zig:89), it uses the private `config_path` constant. The `Globals` struct's default field uses the exported `config_default_path`. These two constants are currently identical but are not linked — changing one does not change the other. A future rename or path change applied to one location but not the other would silently cause `runPassthrough` to probe and write to a different path than Globals defaults expect, breaking `init` and passthrough config-existence detection without a compile error.

**Impact & repro:** Maintenance hazard only today (both are `"zentinel.toml"`). If either constant is updated unilaterally, `zentinel init` could write a file that `zentinel check`/`run` never finds, or the config-exists probe in `runPassthrough` could silently diverge from the path the rest of the system resolves.  
_Repro:_ Inspect src/cli.zig:5 and src/root.zig:368 side-by-side; confirm no `use zentinel.config_default_path` anywhere in cli.zig.

**Suggested fix:** Replace `cli.zig`'s private `const config_path = "zentinel.toml";` with `const config_path = zentinel.config_default_path;`, making the adapter derive its constant from the single source of truth in the core module.

**Lens verdicts:** correctness: UPHELD, zig-semantics-safety: REFUTED, reproduction: REFUTED

---
### [S10] enabled() called once per candidate -> O(M*E) post-collection operator filter

- **Severity:** Low  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 1/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D10-perf
- **Location(s):** `src/run_command.zig`

**Evidence:**
```zig
src/run_command.zig:603: `if (!enabled(cfg, c.operator)) continue;` inside `for (all) |c|` — iterates every raw candidate (M total). `enabled` at lines 570–575 scans `cfg.mutators_enabled` (E entries, one per enabled operator) with `std.mem.eql` per entry.
```

**Tool confirmation:** Confirmed by reading src/run_command.zig lines 601–612 (`generateCandidates` filter loop) and lines 570–575 (`enabled` implementation). `cfg.mutators_enabled` is `[]const []const u8` (see src/config.zig:49); no set or hash-set is used.

**Why it is wrong:** For M raw candidates and E configured operators, the operator-enable check costs O(M * E) string comparisons. E is bounded (8 built-in operators), so this is effectively O(M * 8) = O(M). Still, each comparison runs `std.mem.eql` on operator name strings for every candidate when a simple set membership check (via a small bitmask or hash-set built once before the loop) would do it in O(1) per candidate.

**Impact & repro:** Low in absolute terms because E <= 8 and operator strings are short (< 20 bytes). However, the pattern is repeated identically on every mutant candidate across every run. With thousands of candidates (which is realistic for a large project with all operators enabled), this is tens of thousands of redundant string comparisons in a tight loop.  
_Repro:_ Instrument `enabled` with a counter and run `zentinel run` on a large project. The counter will equal M * (average scans to find/miss an operator in the enabled list).

**Suggested fix:** Before the filter loop, convert `cfg.mutators_enabled` to a small hash-set or, given E <= 8, a single packed bitmask keyed by operator tag enum. One `StringHashMap` lookup or one bitmask AND replaces the O(E) inner scan per candidate.

**Lens verdicts:** correctness: UPHELD, zig-semantics-safety: REFUTED, reproduction: REFUTED

---
### [S11] matchModeFor silently treats 'text output subset' as exact matching

- **Severity:** Low  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 1/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D11-cli
- **Location(s):** `src/doctest_command.zig`, `src/doctest/block.zig`

**Evidence:**
```zig
block.matchModeFromToken (block.zig:60) accepts 'subset' and returns `.subset` regardless of the block language. matchModeFor (doctest_command.zig:245-248) for non-JSON blocks only maps `.contains => .contains`, with `else => .exact`. So a non-JSON block with `.subset` match mode falls through to `.exact`. The tag is silently discarded without an error or diagnostic.
```

**Tool confirmation:** Code read of block.zig:59-63 confirms `matchModeFromToken` returns `.subset` for 'subset' on any block. Code read of doctest_command.zig:244-249 confirms `else => .exact` catches `.subset` in the non-JSON path. The block parser at parser.zig:150-166 would mark a block as `unsupported` only for unrecognized bare tokens, not for recognized mode tokens — `subset` is recognized and passes through.

**Why it is wrong:** A user writing ` ```text output subset ``` ` (perhaps intending line-prefix containment) gets the 'subset' tag silently accepted by the parser (no diagnostic), stored in match_mode, but then silently treated as exact matching by matchModeFor. The docs for `text output` list only `contains` and `regex` as named modes; `subset` is a JSON-only concept. However since the parser accepts `subset` without error and the docs make no statement that `subset` is invalid for text blocks, the silent discard is confusing.

**Impact & repro:** Low: `subset` is not a documented text output mode, so most users will not write it. But the silent behavior means if a user mistakenly uses it, they get a harder-to-diagnose false mismatch rather than a clear diagnostic. The parser should either reject `subset` for non-JSON blocks or emit an unsupported-tag diagnostic.  
_Repro:_ Write a doctest with ` ```text output subset ``` ` following a CLI case. Run `zentinel doctest`. No diagnostic is emitted; the snapshot match uses exact mode, not subset semantics.

**Suggested fix:** In matchModeFor (doctest_command.zig:244-248), add an explicit `.subset => .exact` case with a comment, OR emit a parser diagnostic for `subset` when used on a non-JSON block. The cleanest fix is to not add 'subset' as a block-level token for text blocks in matchModeFromToken, or to check language context before accepting mode tokens in parser.zig classify.

**Lens verdicts:** correctness: UPHELD, zig-semantics-safety: REFUTED, reproduction: REFUTED

---
### [S12] TOML parser does not process backslash escape sequences in double-quoted strings

- **Severity:** Low  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 1/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D11-cli
- **Location(s):** `src/config_toml.zig`

**Evidence:**
```zig
readString (config_toml.zig:91-106) returns a zero-copy slice of the raw source bytes between the opening and closing quotes, with no escape-sequence processing. TOML 1.0 requires that double-quoted strings process at minimum: \\, \", \n, \t, \r. As written: (1) '"C:\\Users"' returns 'C:\\Users' (two backslashes) instead of 'C:\Users' (one backslash). When combined with normalizePath (config.zig:263-269), this produces 'C://Users' instead of 'C:/Users'. (2) '"say \"hi\""' causes early string termination at the first '\"', followed by a parse error when the entry parser sees residual garbage. The parser is documented at line 6 as supporting 'double-quoted strings', implying TOML conformance.
```

**Tool confirmation:** Read of config_toml.zig:91-106 confirms the while loop advances past every character that is not '"' or '\n', including '\\'. No escape dispatch is present. Read of config.zig:263-269 confirms normalizePath blindly replaces every '\\' with '/', compounding the double-backslash error.

**Why it is wrong:** The mismatch between the documented subset ('double-quoted strings') and the actual behaviour (no escape processing) means any config value intentionally containing a literal backslash will hold wrong data. On Windows, paths like 'C:\\Users' in a quoted config string are common. On all platforms, '\\\\server\\share' UNC paths are affected. Additionally, a config value containing '\"' causes a parse error rather than embedding a quote, violating user expectations based on standard TOML tooling.

**Impact & repro:** Silent data corruption for any double-quoted config string value that contains '\\' — most practically Windows path strings. normalizePath then double-converts the extra backslashes, yielding double-slash path components. Strings containing '\"' cause a hard parse error rather than embedding a literal quote, so the failure is caught, but the error message ('unterminated string' at the wrong line) is misleading.  
_Repro:_ Create zentinel.toml with: [report]\noutput_dir = "zig-out\\zentinel" — the parser returns 'zig-out\\zentinel' (two backslashes), then normalizePath produces 'zig-out//zentinel' instead of 'zig-out/zentinel'.

**Suggested fix:** In readString, replace the inner while loop with a branch that checks for '\\' and dispatches to an escape handler: on '\\' consume the next character and emit the escaped character ('\\'->'\\', '"'->'"', 'n'->'\n', 't'->'\t', 'r'->'\r'); return an error for unrecognized escapes. The return value must then be an arena-allocated copy rather than a source slice. Alternatively, document that the subset intentionally disallows all escape sequences and validate that no config field ever needs one — but the current 'double-quoted strings' claim must be updated to say 'no escape sequences supported'.

**Lens verdicts:** correctness: UPHELD, zig-semantics-safety: REFUTED, reproduction: REFUTED

---
### [S13] validate_task_system: empty allowed_files=[] / forbidden_files=[] pass validation via Python all() vacuous truth

- **Severity:** Low  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 1/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D12-build
- **Location(s):** `scripts/validate_task_system.py`

**Evidence:**
```zig
Line 338: `require(isinstance(value, list) and all(isinstance(item, str) and item for item in value), errors, f"task {task_id} {key} must be a non-empty string array")`. Python `all()` on an empty iterable returns `True` vacuously. Confirmed: `python3 -c "print(all(isinstance(item, str) and item for item in []))"` prints `True`. An empty list `[]` satisfies this guard while the error message says 'non-empty string array'.
```

**Tool confirmation:** Bash confirmed `python3 -c` output is True for empty list, False for [""] — so an empty string element IS caught but a completely empty list is not.

**Why it is wrong:** A task entry with `allowed_files: []` would pass validation, silently granting the task an unconstrained scope (since validate_completion_scope_evidence only checks allowed/forbidden against files_changed when the lists are non-empty). This undermines the scope-enforcement guarantees the task system is designed to provide.

**Impact & repro:** A task author or erroneous generator that produces an empty `allowed_files` array passes the validator, potentially allowing scope creep to go undetected by the automated CI check. The impact is limited to the governance layer (not product behavior) and no current task has this defect.  
_Repro:_ Temporarily set any task's `allowed_files` to `[]` in `tasks/queue.json` and run `python3 scripts/validate_task_system.py`. It passes without error.

**Suggested fix:** Change the condition to: `require(isinstance(value, list) and len(value) > 0 and all(isinstance(item, str) and item for item in value), errors, f"task {task_id} {key} must be a non-empty string array")`.

**Lens verdicts:** correctness: UPHELD, zig-semantics-safety: REFUTED, reproduction: REFUTED

---
### [S14] completion_evidence files_changed/tests_added/tests_run/follow_up_tasks accept empty lists via vacuous all()

- **Severity:** Low  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 1/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D12-build
- **Location(s):** `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/scripts/validate_task_system.py`

**Evidence:**
```zig
Line 575: require(isinstance(entry.get(field), list) and all(isinstance(item, str) and item for item in entry.get(field, [])), errors, ...) is applied to fields 'files_changed', 'tests_added', 'tests_run', 'follow_up_tasks'. Python's all() returns True for an empty iterable, so a task completion entry with files_changed=[] passes this check. The error message says 'must be a string array' but does not enforce non-emptiness despite the intent implied by the constraint.
```

**Tool confirmation:** Bash: python3 -c "val=[]; print(isinstance(val, list) and all(isinstance(item, str) and item for item in val))" → True. This is the same vacuous-truth pattern as the already-reported allowed_files/forbidden_files bug (line 338), here applied to completion evidence fields at line 575.

**Why it is wrong:** validate_completion_scope_evidence (lines 636-663) uses files_changed from the completion evidence entry to verify that every changed file falls within the task's allowed scope (line 644: for path in files_changed). If files_changed=[] passes validation, a task's completion evidence can omit all changed files, defeating the scope enforcement check entirely. An agent could submit evidence that changed out-of-scope files while listing files_changed=[] to bypass the scope audit.

**Impact & repro:** Governance bypass: task completion evidence with files_changed=[] passes the 'non-empty string array' validation, and since validate_completion_scope_evidence iterates over files_changed, no scope violation is checked. The semantic contract (every changed file must be in allowed_files) is silently unenforceable when files_changed is empty.  
_Repro:_ Create a completion_evidence entry in status.json with files_changed=[], tests_added=[], tests_run=['python3 scripts/validate_task_system.py'], follow_up_tasks=[]. Run python3 scripts/validate_task_system.py. Observe: no error on the empty-array fields, but the tests_run 'any()' check at line 589 is not vacuous and would fail if the list were empty.

**Suggested fix:** At line 575, add an explicit non-emptiness check for files_changed specifically: require(isinstance(entry.get('files_changed'), list) and len(entry.get('files_changed', [])) > 0 and all(...), ...). Or extract a helper require_nonempty_string_array that enforces both non-empty and element validity. Same fix needed for allowed_files/forbidden_files (already reported).

**Lens verdicts:** correctness: UPHELD, zig-semantics-safety: REFUTED, reproduction: REFUTED

### [S15] No doc states which commands require the external 'zig' binary (and which do not)

- **Severity:** Low  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 1/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D13-docs
- **Location(s):** `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/docs/FAILURE_MODES.md`, `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/docs/CLI_SPEC.md`, `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/docs/ARCHITECTURE.md`, `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/cli.zig`

**Evidence:**
```zig
`list-mutants` (cli.zig:593-730) has no `fatalStatusLine` call. It does call `project_model.discover` and `list_mutants_command.generate`, which perform AST parsing using the std.zig.Ast parser embedded in zentinel — not the external `zig` binary. So the absence of Zig enforcement is likely intentional: `list-mutants` does not need the external Zig binary. However, no governance document explicitly states 'list-mutants does not require an external Zig binary' or enumerates which commands do versus do not need external Zig. FAILURE_MODES.md F-001 uses the vague phrase 'commands that require Zig' without defining which commands those are. ARCHITECTURE.md §Pipeline step 2 says 'Validate Zig version' but only in the context of the run pipeline. CLI_SPEC.md never explicitly separates the two groups.
```

**Tool confirmation:** Bash grep for 'fatalStatusLine' in cli.zig returns exactly 3 call sites (lines 457-461, 1212-1216, 1382-1386), none in runListMutants (lines 593-730). Full read of runListMutants confirms it reads source files and calls list_mutants_command.generate with no Zig binary invocation. CLI_SPEC.md grep for 'require.*Zig', 'Zig.*required': only the 'version' and 'check' sentences appear.

**Why it is wrong:** Without a clear enumeration of which commands need the external Zig binary, future agents cannot know whether to add `fatalStatusLine` to a new command. If a new command is added that does NOT need external Zig but adds `fatalStatusLine` following the pattern it sees in `run`, it creates a spurious failure mode. Conversely, if a new command is added that DOES need external Zig but the implementer reads 'only check is mentioned,' it may skip the fatal gate. The current state — three commands in code, two named in docs — is fragile.

**Impact & repro:** Currently low because the set of implemented commands is stable. Becomes a real governance gap when a new command (e.g. 'report', 'compare', or a future 'watch' mode) is implemented by an autonomous agent.  
_Repro:_ Search CLI_SPEC.md and FAILURE_MODES.md for a sentence that explicitly says 'list-mutants does not invoke the external zig binary' or 'the following commands require external Zig: check, run, doctest'. No such sentence exists.

**Suggested fix:** Add a table or bullet list to CLI_SPEC.md (or FAILURE_MODES.md §F-001) that explicitly enumerates: commands that call `fatalStatusLine` (check, run, doctest); commands that use only the embedded std.zig.Ast parser and do NOT need external Zig (list-mutants); commands that do not involve Zig at all (version, init). This makes the policy self-describing for future implementers.

**Lens verdicts:** correctness: UPHELD, zig-semantics-safety: REFUTED, reproduction: REFUTED

### [S16] MUTATION_GATE_POLICY.md retry table omits the 'Architecture' task class, diverging from FAILURE_RECOVERY.md

- **Severity:** Low  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 1/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** D13-docs
- **Location(s):** `docs/MUTATION_GATE_POLICY.md`, `docs/FAILURE_RECOVERY.md`, `scripts/validate_task_system.py`

**Evidence:**
```zig
docs/MUTATION_GATE_POLICY.md lines 89-95 list a retry table with three rows (low-risk: 1, normal: 2, high-risk or compiler-internal: 3) and state: 'These retry limits are the same ones recorded in docs/FAILURE_RECOVERY.md; the two documents must not diverge.' docs/FAILURE_RECOVERY.md lines 62-68 list five rows: Low-risk (1), Normal (2), High-risk (3), Compiler-internal (3 plus architecture review), and Architecture (1 plus contract review). The 'Architecture' class appears only in FAILURE_RECOVERY.md. scripts/validate_task_system.py line 1613 implements FAILURE_RECOVERY_RETRY_LIMITS with 'architecture': 1, so the validator knows the correct limit, but an agent reading only MUTATION_GATE_POLICY.md would find no Architecture row and either reject the task class or apply the wrong limit.
```

**Tool confirmation:** Read of docs/MUTATION_GATE_POLICY.md (lines 89-95), docs/FAILURE_RECOVERY.md (lines 60-68), scripts/validate_task_system.py (lines 1607-1614). Grep confirmed 'architecture' absent from MUTATION_GATE_POLICY.md retry table.

**Why it is wrong:** MUTATION_GATE_POLICY.md explicitly claims parity with FAILURE_RECOVERY.md and asserts the two must not diverge. The omission of the Architecture task class means an agent or task author reading MUTATION_GATE_POLICY.md's retry table cannot determine the Architecture limit (1 cycle), and might apply high-risk limits (3 cycles) instead, exceeding the correct budget without triggering the correct escalation path.

**Impact & repro:** An architecture-class task that hits repeated gate failures could be retried up to 3 cycles under a literal reading of MUTATION_GATE_POLICY.md, when the correct limit is 1 cycle per FAILURE_RECOVERY.md. The validator enforces the correct 1-cycle limit and would catch this at runtime, but the spec-level misdirection remains a real governance gap. The claim 'these documents must not diverge' is itself false.  
_Repro:_ Compare docs/MUTATION_GATE_POLICY.md lines 89-93 against docs/FAILURE_RECOVERY.md lines 62-68. MUTATION_GATE_POLICY.md has 3 rows; FAILURE_RECOVERY.md has 5. The Architecture row (limit 1) exists only in FAILURE_RECOVERY.md.

**Suggested fix:** Add the Architecture task class row to MUTATION_GATE_POLICY.md's retry table: '- architecture: 1 cycle then contract review'. Also split the currently-combined 'high-risk or compiler-internal' row into two separate rows to match FAILURE_RECOVERY.md's table exactly.

**Lens verdicts:** correctness: UPHELD, zig-semantics-safety: REFUTED, reproduction: REFUTED

---
### [S17] Third verbatim copy of the unchecked-u32 lineOfRef accumulator overflow in mutator_doctest.zig (panics in isolation; bounded reachability)

- **Severity:** Low  |  **Confidence:** High  |  **Verification:** 1/3 lenses upheld  |  **Dimension(s):** critic
- **Location(s):** `/Users/oli/Projects/zentinel/src/doctest/mutator_doctest.zig`

**Evidence:**
```zig
mutator_doctest.zig:183-189 lineOfRef: `var n: u32 = 0; while (i < ref.len and ref[i] >= '0' and ref[i] <= '9') : (i += 1) n = n * 10 + (ref[i] - '0');` -- the same unchecked accumulator already flagged CONFIRMED Critical for doctest/cache.zig:99 and present a third time at doctest_command.zig:264 (grep `n = n * 10` finds exactly these 3 sites). In ReleaseSafe/Debug this panics 'integer overflow' on a 10+ digit numeric segment. The sole caller is validateDoc:128 `findBlockByLine(parsed.blocks, lineOfRef(c.block_refs[1]))`.
```

**Tool confirmation:** Ran `zig test -OReleaseSafe` on an isolated copy of this exact lineOfRef body calling lineOfRef("x:999999999999"): output 'thread panic: integer overflow ... terminated with signal ABRT'. Reachability scoped via grep `mutator_doctest\.`/`md\.` across src/+test/: the only callers are test/doctest_mutator_spec_test.zig and the root.zig:117 re-export; there is NO src/ caller (validateDoc is never wired into the doctest CLI -- doctest_command.zig runs its own separate pipeline). Read of extractor.zig:156-159 + formatRef (239-242) confirms block_refs entries are internally minted as `"{file}:{line_start}"` where line_start is the parser's u32 line counter (parser.zig:50, incremented once per source newline).

**Why it is wrong:** Defense-in-depth / code-duplication hygiene: this is the third live copy of an accumulator already accepted as a Critical defect elsewhere, sitting in the one src/mutators-area file the ground-truth flagged as having no direct test/ counterpart. A shared, bounds-checked parseLine helper would have prevented all three copies.

**Impact & repro:** Practically unreachable through any realistic input: c.block_refs[1] is always a parser-generated ref whose numeric segment is a 1-based source line number, so triggering u32 overflow (n > 4,294,967,295) requires a markdown document with >4.29 billion lines (>8 GiB; the test harness caps reads at 1 MiB via readFileAlloc limit 1<<20). Combined with the module being test-only, there is no production crash path here today -- hence Low, in contrast to the doctest_command.zig:264 copy whose lineOfRef is fed an untrusted `--case` CLI argument at selectByRef:282.  
_Repro:_ Direct unit: `zig test -OReleaseSafe` a file with `fn lineOfRef(ref: []const u8) u32 { const first = std.mem.indexOfScalar(u8, ref, ':') orelse return 0; var i = first + 1; var n: u32 = 0; while (i < ref.len and ref[i] >= '0' and ref[i] <= '9') : (i += 1) n = n * 10 + (ref[i] - '0'); return n; }` and `_ = lineOfRef("x:999999999999");` -> SIGABRT integer overflow. Not reachable through validateDoc with any sub-8GiB document.

**Suggested fix:** Replace all three lineOfRef bodies (cache.zig:95-101, mutator_doctest.zig:183-189, doctest_command.zig:258-267) with one shared helper that uses std.fmt.parseInt(u32, digits, 10) and returns 0 (or a checked sentinel) on Overflow/Invalid, so a malformed or oversized ref can never panic. Track this with the existing spawned task for the cache.zig copy rather than as a new behavioral bug.

**Lens verdicts:** CORRECTNESS: UPHELD, Zig-semantics/safety: integer overflow/UB, runtime-safety (Debug/ReleaseSafe panic vs ReleaseFast wrap), and reachability of the panic path.: REFUTED, REPRODUCTION: REFUTED

## Coverage & Limits

**Partition (every src/ file assigned to ≥1 dimension; test/ → D8; docs/specs/prior-audits → D13; build/scripts → D12):**

- **D1-mutators** — Mutation operators — semantic validity & compilability: src/mutators/arithmetic.zig, src/mutators/boolean.zig, src/mutators/logical.zig, src/mutators/comparison.zig, src/mutators/integer_boundary.zig, src/mutators/optional.zig, src/mutators/loop_boundary.zig, src/mutators/error_path.zig, src/mutant.zig, src/ast_backend.zig, src/zir_backend.zig, src/air_backend.zig, src/source_map.zig, src/doctest/mutator_doctest.zig, src/doctest/mutation_experiment.zig, src/doctest/mutation_id.zig
- **D2-applyrevert** — Apply/revert round-trip integrity: src/mutant.zig, src/source_map.zig, src/mutant_runner.zig, src/cache.zig, src/runner.zig, src/run_command.zig
- **D3-killdetect** — Kill-detection & classification soundness: src/runner.zig, src/mutant_runner.zig, src/run_command.zig, src/report.zig, src/sandbox.zig, src/check_command.zig
- **D4-memory** — Zig memory & lifetimes: ALL of src/ — prioritize allocator-heavy: src/cli.zig, src/run_command.zig, src/report.zig, src/config.zig, src/config_toml.zig, src/cache.zig, src/mutant_runner.zig, src/runner.zig, src/ai/command.zig, src/ai/doctest_command.zig, src/ai/context.zig, src/ai/redaction.zig, src/doctest/*.zig, src/mutant.zig, src/project_model.zig, src/worker_pool.zig
- **D5-concurrency** — Concurrency & parallel execution: src/worker_pool.zig, src/runner.zig, src/run_command.zig, src/mutant_runner.zig, src/cache.zig, src/test_selection.zig
- **D6-safety** — Safety & containment: src/sandbox.zig, src/safety_modes.zig, src/ai/redaction.zig, src/ai/context.zig, src/ai/command.zig, src/ai/doctest_command.zig, src/ai/provider.zig, src/source_map.zig, src/cache.zig, src/report.zig

- **D10-perf** — Performance & wasted work: src/cache.zig, src/runner.zig, src/worker_pool.zig, src/run_command.zig, src/test_selection.zig, src/report.zig, src/doctest/runner.zig, src/doctest/cache.zig, src/mutant_runner.zig

**Discovery passes per dimension:** D1-mutators=4, D2-applyrevert=4, D3-killdetect=4, D4-memory=2, D5-concurrency=4, D6-safety=4, D7-errorsets=4, D8-tests=4, D9-arch=4, D10-perf=4, D11-cli=4, D12-build=4, D13-docs=4

**Verification methodology:** Each Critical/High/Medium finding was tested by three independent skeptic agents (correctness, Zig-semantics/safety, reproduction lenses), kept only if ≥2 upheld it. Low-severity findings were each tested by one consolidated skeptic applying all three lenses — a cost-control concession after the first end-to-end run exhausted the account session token budget (~13.4M tokens, 239 agents) during the verify phase; on the completing run the ground-truth + 13-dimension discovery + dedup phases were reused from cache and only verification onward re-ran. Verify agents were constrained to lightweight, read-mostly checks (≤3-4 tool calls, no heavy whole-repo rebuilds).

## Cross-Cutting Themes

- Kill-detection / score integrity is fragile and under-tested: the compile-vs-test discriminator is heuristic (H4), summarize arithmetic is unpinned (M10), and the only e2e classification test binds fungible counts (S7) — the product's headline output can drift silently
- Mutators routinely emit guaranteed-dead (compile_error) or guaranteed-equivalent mutants that pollute the survivor set and waste apply+compile cycles: dangling-semicolon errdefer (H2), unused catch capture (M1), enum field names true/false (L23), byte-exact skip-guards (L6)
- Unrecoverable panics on legal/attacker-controllable input deny or abort the tool instead of degrading gracefully: i128 boundary overflow (H1), u32 doctest line-ref accumulators (M4, S17)
- A large 'parsed/validated but never consumed' and 'dead public export' surface creates a false impression of wiring: safety modes (H5), cache/report/ai config (M5, L43, L45), worker isolation (L10), writeJson (L15), backend diagnostics (L25), the entire property subsystem (L13)
- Documented AI-context/report redaction guarantees are only partially enforced: several fields and path shapes bypass redactField or normalizeExcerpt, leaking absolute developer paths/secrets to providers and breaking committed-report determinism (M3, M8, M9, L28, L29)
- Parallel/workspace filesystem handling under --jobs>1 is hazardous: a live-root tree walk races sibling workers (H3), prefix-only exclusion over/under-matches (M2, L7), and partial/stale workspaces leak (L8, L9)
- Doctest and experimental-backend feature paths silently diverge from spec: 4-of-8 collector restriction under-reports mutants (M7) and falsely flags stable operators as drift (L24); matcher modes are unreachable (M6)

## Top 5 Fixes (priority order)

1. H4 — Make the compile-vs-test-failure classification reliable under `zig build test` (replace the brittle 'passed;' marker / isCompileFailure heuristic with an exit-code/structured signal). #1 because kill/survive counts are the product's entire reason to exist: genuinely killed mutants are silently moved into the compile_error bucket (and vice-versa), so the headline score is untrustworthy on the standard configured command — every downstream verdict inherits the error.
2. H1 — Bounds-check the i128 `value +/- 1` in integer_boundary.zig:83-84 and loop_boundary before formatting (skip or clamp at the type extremes). #2 because it is a total-tool denial: a single legal max-value decimal comparison operand anywhere in a scanned file panics the whole `run`/`list-mutants` process, and mutation candidate generation must be total over any parseable source.
3. H5 — Actually thread safety_modes.buildFlag's `-O<mode>` flag into the spawned test command (it currently has no production caller). #3 because an advertised headline feature is silently inert: every mode runs Debug, so `--mode ReleaseFast/ReleaseSmall` and the mode matrix report uniform Debug results, giving users who rely on safety modes confidently wrong mutation outcomes.
4. H3 — Stop walking the live project root in setupWorkspace (cli.zig:249-256) under parallel runs; snapshot or exclude the workspaces subtree from traversal. #4 because `--jobs > 1` is a supported mode and sibling workers concurrently creating/deleting workspaces inside the tree being walked nondeterministically yields spurious `invalid` mutants — flaky, irreproducible misclassification that hides real survivors.
5. H2 — Fix errdefer_remove's span to include the statement's terminating `;` (error_path.zig:94-100) so the mutant is syntactically valid. #5 because the targeted idiom (`errdefer self.deinit();` and similar single-expression cleanups) is the common case, and every such mutant is a guaranteed compile_error — the operator can never kill at those sites, so error-cleanup paths go effectively untested while looking covered.
